💰 2. CREDIT SYSTEM + PAYOUT ECONOMY
(From first half & second half of credit system convo + homeaglow payout process)

Credit Logic Summary
Clients buy credits — preload balance.

Credits = service units, not dollars (avoids money transmitter laws).

Credits held in escrow → released only when job approved.

Unused credits auto-refunded to wallet.

Cleaners earn credits → converted to payouts weekly.

Tier System
Tier	Reliability Range	Rate Power	Perks
Bronze	0–69	Low	Shown only when no higher-tier cleaners
Silver	70–84	Medium	Standard visibility
Gold	85–94	High	Priority visibility
Platinum	95–100	Max	Instant payouts, early job access
Reliability Metrics
GPS check-in/out (+20)

Before/after photos (+15)

Client 5★ review (+15)

Late cancel (−25)

No-show (−50)

Job incomplete (−30)

Key Payout Flow
Credits converted to $ via backend formula:
credits × payout_rate (e.g., 0.80)

Weekly ACH = free

Instant Payout = Stripe Instant (5% fee to cleaner)

✅ Legal Clarity: PureTask is not a money transmitter or bank. Stripe holds all funds (merchant-of-record model).

Absolutely. Here’s the final, consolidated list of the 12 PureTask workflows—pulled together from all your docs and organized so we can go one-by-one next. For each workflow I include: Trigger → What it does → Data writes → Notifications/externals → Edge cases. I’ve merged overlapping pieces across files and kept only the most robust versions we created.

1) Stripe Webhook Ingest & Dispatcher
Trigger: Stripe events → POST /webhook/stripe/webhook
Does: Validate signature; route events: payment_intent.succeeded|payment_intent.payment_failed|charge.refunded|transfer.paid|transfer.failed|charge.dispute.*. Updates our DB and emits follow-up flows.
Writes: Payment upserts; credit ledger entries (as needed).
Notify/External: none on success; ops alerts on failures.
Edge cases: Missing metadata (job_id/cleaner_id) ⇒ park to manual review.

2) Job Lifecycle Orchestrator (create → accept → in-progress → completed → awaiting_client → approved / disputed / cancelled)
Trigger: App/API actions (create/accept/check-in/out/complete/approve/cancel)
Does: Drives the state machine; tracks GPS check-in/out; actual hours; computes final charge & any refund.
Writes: jobs state, timing; snapshot rates; final_charge_credits, refund_credits.
Notify/External: reminders, “on the way”, completion emails/SMS (SendGrid/Twilio).
Edge cases: Early finish (auto refund); more time (top-up escrow); insufficient wallet credits; dispute hold.

3) Credit Wallet & Escrow Manager (hold → charge → release → refund)
Trigger: Booking/accept (hold), approval (charge), early finish or cancellation (release/refund)
Does: Maintains the immutable ledger with types purchase|hold|release|charge|refund|reversal; mirrors wallet balance for fast reads.
Writes: credit_transactions rows; recompute users.wallet_credits_balance transactionally.
Notify/External: payment failures and receipts emails/SMS.
Edge cases: Reversal on admin adjustments; consistency guards so holds/charges net out correctly.

4) Client Approval → Cleaner Earnings Posting
Trigger: Client presses Approve (or Admin Force Approve)
Does: Posts a CleanerEarnings entry = final_charge_credits × payout_percentage_at_accept; marks job approved.
Writes: cleaner_earnings(pending); links to job.
Notify/External: cleaner “earnings updated”; client receipt.
Edge cases: If admin later adjusts final charge, create reverse + new earnings entry.

5) Refunds & Adjustments Dispatcher (Admin)
Trigger: Admin actions: partial refund, adjust final charge
Does: Writes release (refund) credit entries; adjusts totals post-approval by writing deltas (never overwrite).
Writes: credit_transactions(type='release'|delta), optional reverse/new earnings.
Notify/External: client refund email; ops alert if threshold exceeded.
Edge cases: Idempotency on repeated admin clicks.

6) Disputes Resolution Flow
Trigger: Client opens dispute; Admin triage
Does: Freezes transfer; Admin one-click outcomes: client favor → release to wallet; cleaner favor → post earnings; partial → split. Updates dispute_status.
Writes: ledger entries + earnings as per outcome.
Notify/External: both parties notified of outcome; record to ops log.
Edge cases: Fraud guard; evidence (photos/GPS).

7) Weekly Payout Processor (Free/ACH)
Trigger: Cron (Fridays 18:00 UTC)
Does: Batch cleaner_earnings(status=pending) into payouts, call Stripe Connect transfers; mark paid.
Writes: payouts rows with totals and stripe_transfer_id; earnings → paid.
Notify/External: cleaner payout email; failure to ops.
Edge cases: Partial failures → re-try button in Admin.

8) Instant Payout (On-Demand)
Trigger: Cleaner taps “Instant Payout” (Base44 action)
Does: Calculates available amount, fees; initiates Stripe Instant Payout to debit card; records a payout now. (Enabled workflow present & cURL test path).
Writes: payouts(status=processing→paid); link Stripe result.
Notify/External: cleaner instant payout confirmation.
Edge cases: Insufficient available; Stripe rate limit; double-click idempotency.

9) Notifications Orchestrator (Email, SMS, Push)
Trigger: Booking created, reminders (24h/1h), on-the-way, completion, failures, password reset, marketing, etc.
Does: Drive SendGrid dynamic templates + Twilio SMS via index.json & template maps; variables reference used across flows.
Writes: notification logs.
Notify/External: SendGrid/Twilio; OneSignal (push).
Edge cases: honor user opt-in flags from preferences; sender identity & DKIM configured.

10) Reliability & Tier Engine
Trigger: Job approval (webhook); periodic recompute window (rolling 90-day)
Does: Apply reliability deltas (GPS timing, photos, stars, cancellations/no-show); auto-adjust tier and allowed rate bands.
Writes: users.reliability_score, users.tier, users.payout_percentage.
Notify/External: cleaner “tier change” notice.
Edge cases: Admin manual adjust with reason trail.

11) KPI & Ops Metrics Export
Trigger: Nightly cron
Does: Aggregate KPIs (new users, bookings, refunds/disputes, payouts, reliability averages) and export to Sheets/Notion or data store; ops alert if thresholds breached. (n8n env & workspace setup mentions KPI/ops creds and turning on key flows).
Writes: metrics tables/files.
Notify/External: Slack/Email to ops (optional).
Edge cases: backfill on failures; time zone normalization (UTC).

12) Nightly Backups & Data Integrity
Trigger: Nightly cron
Does: Dump Postgres (or selected tables) to S3; verify row counts; email/Slack confirmation; stores DATABASE_URL/S3 creds via n8n credentials.
Writes: backup artifacts; checksum manifest.
Notify/External: Slack/Email with summary.
Edge cases: rotate backups; retention policy; restore drill.

Starting with Section 1: Stripe Webhook Ingest & Dispatcher.

I’ve merged everything from your uploads into a single, production-ready package: DB schema + n8n workflow (node-by-node) + optional verifier microservice + idempotency + tests + alerts. I kept names/paths consistent with your prior exports so you can drop this in with minimal change.

1) Stripe Webhook Ingest & Dispatcher (Final)
Goal & Scope
Receive Stripe events at POST /stripe/webhook.

Verify signature, de-duplicate, and route only the supported events to the right downstream flows:
payment_intent.succeeded, payment_intent.payment_failed, charge.refunded, charge.dispute.*, transfer.paid, transfer.failed.

Extract job_id, cleaner_id, and amounts from event metadata/body; write payment & ledger-side effects via the downstream workflows (which we’ll fully spec in Sections 2–5).

Your existing n8n export already shows the webhook path, an extract function, and a switch on type for these exact events — we’ll finalize these nodes and add idempotency + verification hardening.

A. Database: Tables, Indexes, Idempotency Guards
Add these to Postgres (Neon). They align with your Users, Jobs, and CreditTransactions model (immutable ledger).

-- 1) Record every Stripe webhook for audit/idempotency
CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS stripe_events (
  id                text PRIMARY KEY,              -- Stripe event id (evt_xxx)
  type              text NOT NULL,
  created_at_utc    timestamptz NOT NULL DEFAULT now(),
  payload           jsonb NOT NULL,
  job_id            text,                          -- from metadata if present
  cleaner_id        text,                          -- from metadata if present
  handled           boolean NOT NULL DEFAULT false,
  handled_at_utc    timestamptz
);

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS stripe_events_type_idx ON stripe_events(type);
CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS stripe_events_job_idx  ON stripe_events(job_id);

-- 2) (Optional, but useful) Track payment intents as a normalized table
CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS payment_intents (
  id                     text PRIMARY KEY,        -- pi_xxx
  job_id                 text,
  cleaner_id             text,
  amount_cents           bigint NOT NULL DEFAULT 0,
  currency               text NOT NULL DEFAULT 'usd',
  status                 text NOT NULL,           -- requires_confirmation|processing|succeeded|canceled|...
  last_event_type        text,                    -- e.g. payment_intent.succeeded
  updated_at_utc         timestamptz NOT NULL DEFAULT now(),
  raw                    jsonb NOT NULL
);

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS payment_intents_job_idx ON payment_intents(job_id);
CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS payment_intents_cleaner_idx ON payment_intents(cleaner_id);
Your ledger (credit_transactions) remains the single source of truth for wallet math; we won’t write ledger entries inside the ingress. Instead, we route to Credit Wallet & Escrow or Refunds flows (Sections 3 and 5) to post immutable entries. Ledger types are: purchase|hold|release|charge|refund|reversal.

B. n8n Workflow (Final Nodes & Code)
Name: 01 - Stripe Webhook Ingest (keep the same)

Node 1 — Webhook: Stripe In
Type: Webhook

Path: stripe/webhook

HTTP Method: POST

Response: ok (200) immediately after enqueueing downstream (we’ll still do signature/idempotency inline).
(Matches your existing export path.)

Node 2 — Function: Extract Body/Headers
Keep your extractor (preserves case on signature headers); I’ve expanded it slightly for robustness.

// Inputs: webhook JSON: { headers, body }
// Output: { headers, signature, raw_body, parsed } for downstream
const headers = $json.headers || {};
const sig = headers['stripe-signature'] || headers['Stripe-Signature'] || '';
// n8n passes parsed body; if you enabled "Always Output Data" it’s JSON.
// If you need raw string (for external verifier), capture stringified:
const parsed = $json.body;
const raw_body = JSON.stringify(parsed);

return [{
  json: {
    headers,
    signature: sig,
    raw_body,
    parsed
  }
}];
Node 3 — (Optional) HTTP Request: Verify via Microservice
If you adopt the optional verifier (see section C), call it here:

Method: POST /verify/stripe

Body: { signature, raw_body }

Continue On Fail: false

Expect: { ok: true, eventId: "evt_..." } on success.
If you don’t use the proxy, skip this node and continue.

Node 4 — Postgres (Upsert stripe_events)
Idempotency guard: insert-or-ignore by event.id. If exists+handled, stop. If exists but not handled, continue.

-- Query type: Execute Query (use credential: PureTask Postgres)
-- NOTE: :event_id etc. are n8n params from previous node data.

INSERT INTO stripe_events (id, type, payload, job_id, cleaner_id)
VALUES (
  :event_id,
  :type,
  :payload::jsonb,
  NULLIF(:job_id, ''),
  NULLIF(:cleaner_id, '')
)
ON CONFLICT (id) DO NOTHING;

-- Return row for flow decisions
SELECT id, type, handled FROM stripe_events WHERE id = :event_id;
n8n → Query Parameters mapping (from Node 2’s parsed):

:event_id → {{$json["parsed"]["id"]}}

:type → {{$json["parsed"]["type"]}}

:payload → {{$json["raw_body"]}}

:job_id → {{$json["parsed"]["data"]["object"]["metadata"]["job_id"] || ""}}

:cleaner_id → {{$json["parsed"]["data"]["object"]["metadata"]["cleaner_id"] || ""}}

The metadata convention comes from your existing Function node and schema: we consistently include job_id and cleaner_id in Stripe objects.

Node 5 — IF: Already Handled?
Condition: handled === true ⇒ END (idempotent).

Else ⇒ continue.

Node 6 — Switch: Route by Event Type
Keep your existing operations and add disputes umbrella:

Equals: payment_intent.succeeded

Equals: payment_intent.payment_failed

Equals: charge.refunded

StartsWith: charge.dispute.

Equals: transfer.paid

Equals: transfer.failed

Node 7a — Handler: payment_intent.succeeded → Upsert payment_intents
INSERT INTO payment_intents (id, job_id, cleaner_id, amount_cents, currency, status, last_event_type, raw)
VALUES (
  :pi_id,
  NULLIF(:job_id,''),
  NULLIF(:cleaner_id,''),
  :amount_cents,
  :currency,
  'succeeded',
  'payment_intent.succeeded',
  :raw::jsonb
)
ON CONFLICT (id) DO UPDATE
SET status='succeeded',
    last_event_type='payment_intent.succeeded',
    updated_at_utc=now(),
    raw=:raw::jsonb;

SELECT 1;
Params:

:pi_id → {{$json["parsed"]["data"]["object"]["id"]}}

:job_id → {{$json["parsed"]["data"]["object"]["metadata"]["job_id"] || ""}}

:cleaner_id → {{$json["parsed"]["data"]["object"]["metadata"]["cleaner_id"] || ""}}

:amount_cents → {{$json["parsed"]["data"]["object"]["amount_received"] || $json["parsed"]["data"]["object"]["amount"] || 0}}

:currency → {{$json["parsed"]["data"]["object"]["currency"] || "usd"}}

:raw → {{$json["raw_body"]}}

This mirrors your function snippet that extracts jobId, cleanerId, amount_cents from the PI object.

Then emit an internal n8n webhook (or connect to next workflow) to Credit Wallet & Escrow (Section 3) to reconcile holds → charges (no direct ledger writes here).

Node 7b — Handler: payment_intent.payment_failed
Upsert PI with status='payment_failed', last_event_type='payment_intent.payment_failed' (same table/fields as above, different constants).

Notify via Notifications Orchestrator (Section 9) using your templates (payment_failed).

Node 7c — Handler: charge.refunded
Upsert a payment_intents record’s last_event_type='charge.refunded'.

Route to Refunds & Adjustments workflow (Section 5) to post immutable ledger refund and client email w/ receipt.

Node 7d — Handler: charge.dispute.*
Mark PI last_event_type='charge.dispute.[opened|closed|won|lost]'.

Route to Disputes Resolution Flow (Section 6) to freeze and triage.

Node 7e — Handler: transfer.paid
Transfer is payout to cleaner (Stripe Connect); route to Weekly/Instant Payout Processor to mark payouts.paid and notify cleaner. (We’ll wire in Section 7/8.)

Node 7f — Handler: transfer.failed
Route to payouts retry path (admin alert + retry button).

Node 8 — Postgres: Mark Event Handled
After a handler path completes successfully:

UPDATE stripe_events
SET handled = true, handled_at_utc = now()
WHERE id = :event_id;
C. Optional Hardening: Verifier Microservice (Express)
Stripe recommends verifying signatures with their library. n8n Function nodes can’t import SDKs, so the most robust way is a tiny verifier service that accepts raw body, verifies the signature, then forwards the JSON to n8n with a header X-Stripe-Verified: true.

This is similar in spirit to your Base44 emit/signing helper pattern (separate signer/proxy), just Stripe-specific.

server.js

import express from 'express';
import bodyParser from 'body-parser';
import Stripe from 'stripe';
import fetch from 'node-fetch';

const app = express();
// Capture raw body for Stripe verification
app.use(bodyParser.raw({ type: 'application/json' }));

const stripe = new Stripe(process.env.STRIPE_SECRET_KEY, { apiVersion: '2024-06-20' });
const endpointSecret = process.env.STRIPE_WEBHOOK_SECRET;  // whsec_...

// 1) Stripe posts here
app.post('/verify/stripe', async (req, res) => {
  const sig = req.headers['stripe-signature'];
  let event;
  try {
    event = stripe.webhooks.constructEvent(req.body, sig, endpointSecret);
  } catch (err) {
    console.error('Stripe signature verify failed', err.message);
    return res.status(400).json({ ok: false, error: 'invalid_signature' });
  }

  // 2) Forward verified JSON to n8n webhook
  const n8nUrl = process.env.N8N_STRIPE_WEBHOOK_URL; // e.g. https://.../webhook/stripe/webhook
  const forwardResp = await fetch(n8nUrl, {
    method: 'POST',
    headers: {
      'Content-Type': 'application/json',
      'X-Stripe-Verified': 'true'
    },
    body: JSON.stringify(event)
  });

  if (!forwardResp.ok) {
    const text = await forwardResp.text();
    console.error('Forward to n8n failed', text);
    return res.status(502).json({ ok: false, error: 'forward_failed' });
  }
  res.json({ ok: true, eventId: event.id });
});

app.listen(process.env.PORT || 8080, () => {
  console.log('Stripe verifier listening');
});
.env

STRIPE_SECRET_KEY=sk_live_...
STRIPE_WEBHOOK_SECRET=whsec_...
N8N_STRIPE_WEBHOOK_URL=https://<your-n8n>/webhook/stripe/webhook
Stripe → Verifier (raw, signed)

Verifier → n8n (JSON, trusted header)

n8n Node 3 optionally checks headers['X-Stripe-Verified'] === 'true' to enforce verification.

D. Error Handling, Retries, Observability
Idempotency: stripe_events(id) PK prevents double-processing; we check handled before routing.

Retries: Use n8n node-level retry (2–3 attempts) on DB/HTTP.

Alerts:

On payment_intent.payment_failed → Notifications Orchestrator sends client email/SMS.

On transfer.failed → Ops alert + Admin retry path.

On signature or DB failure → send Ops email via SendGrid/Twilio fallback (use your template index).

E. Security & Configuration
n8n Credential: PureTask Postgres (exact name) for DB writes.

Stripe Webhook Secret: store as n8n env or in the verifier’s env (preferred).

PII: Store only minimal Stripe payloads in payment_intents.raw and stripe_events.payload.

F. End-to-End Test Plan
Local event replay (Stripe CLI):

stripe listen --forward-to http://localhost:8080/verify/stripe
stripe trigger payment_intent.succeeded
stripe trigger payment_intent.payment_failed
stripe trigger charge.refunded
stripe trigger charge.dispute.created
stripe trigger transfer.paid
stripe trigger transfer.failed

SECTION 1 — Stripe Webhook Ingest & Dispatcher (Final)
Purpose & Scope
Receive Stripe events, verify signatures, idempotently record the event, and route each supported type to the correct downstream workflow without mutating ledgers directly. Supported events:

payment_intent.succeeded, payment_intent.payment_failed, charge.refunded, any charge.dispute.*, transfer.paid, transfer.failed (you listed these in the n8n export)

Downstream flows this section triggers (they are separate sections we’ll build next):
(2) Job Lifecycle, (3) Credit Wallet & Escrow, (5) Refunds & Adjustments, (6) Disputes, (7/8) Payouts. The data model fields and immutable ledgers referenced below match your unified schema (Users, Jobs, CreditTransactions, CleanerEarnings, Payouts).

Prerequisites
Tables present (summarized):

users (includes wallet_credits_balance, cleaner tier, payout_percentage)

jobs (state machine fields, escrow, snapshots, timing)

credit_transactions (immutable: purchase|hold|release|charge|refund|reversal)

cleaner_earnings (pending→batched→paid) & payouts

SendGrid templates & dynamic data ready (used by failure/receipt notices).

Global constants (from your finalized spec):

A) Database Migrations (new audit/idempotency tables)
These tables complement your existing schema; they do not replace ledgers. Ledger writes happen only in dedicated flows later.

-- A.1 Record Stripe events for audit/idempotency
CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS stripe_events (
  id                text PRIMARY KEY,          -- Stripe evt_xxx
  type              text NOT NULL,
  created_at_utc    timestamptz NOT NULL DEFAULT now(),
  payload           jsonb NOT NULL,            -- full event (for audit)
  job_id            text,                      -- from metadata if present
  cleaner_id        text,                      -- from metadata if present
  handled           boolean NOT NULL DEFAULT false,
  handled_at_utc    timestamptz
);
CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS stripe_events_type_idx ON stripe_events(type);
CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS stripe_events_job_idx  ON stripe_events(job_id);

-- A.2 Normalize PaymentIntents (for quick lookups & status)
CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS payment_intents (
  id                     text PRIMARY KEY,    -- pi_xxx
  job_id                 text,
  cleaner_id             text,
  amount_cents           bigint NOT NULL DEFAULT 0,
  currency               text NOT NULL DEFAULT 'usd',
  status                 text NOT NULL,       -- succeeded/payment_failed/...
  last_event_type        text,
  updated_at_utc         timestamptz NOT NULL DEFAULT now(),
  raw                    jsonb NOT NULL
);
CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS payment_intents_job_idx     ON payment_intents(job_id);
CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS payment_intents_cleaner_idx ON payment_intents(cleaner_id);
The immutable credit_transactions types and wallet mirror rule remain as specified: wallet = Σ(purchase+release+refund) − Σ(hold+charge).

B) n8n Workflow (01 — Stripe Webhook Ingest)
Your export already had the webhook path, extract node, and route-by-type switch; here is the finished version with idempotency and forwarding to the dedicated flows.

Node 1 — Webhook: Stripe In
Path: stripe/webhook

Method: POST

Response: 200 OK with lightweight body (ok) immediately after we enqueue downstream.

Node 2 — Function: Extract Body/Headers
const headers = $json.headers || {};
const signature = headers['stripe-signature'] || headers['Stripe-Signature'] || '';
const parsed = $json.body;              // n8n parsed JSON
const raw_body = JSON.stringify(parsed);
return [{ json: { headers, signature, raw_body, parsed } }];
Node 3 — (Optional) HTTP Verify (Proxy Verifier)
If you run the optional Express verifier (section C), call it:

POST /verify/stripe with { signature, raw_body }

Expect: { ok: true, eventId } on success (else abort with 400/502).

Node 4 — Postgres: Insert Event (Idempotency)
INSERT INTO stripe_events (id, type, payload, job_id, cleaner_id)
VALUES (
  :event_id,
  :type,
  :payload::jsonb,
  NULLIF(:job_id,''),
  NULLIF(:cleaner_id,'')
)
ON CONFLICT (id) DO NOTHING;

SELECT id, type, handled FROM stripe_events WHERE id = :event_id;
Params mapping (from Node 2 parsed):

:event_id → {{$json["parsed"]["id"]}}

:type → {{$json["parsed"]["type"]}}

:payload → {{$json["raw_body"]}}

:job_id → {{$json["parsed"]["data"]["object"]["metadata"]["job_id"] || ""}}

:cleaner_id → {{$json["parsed"]["data"]["object"]["metadata"]["cleaner_id"] || ""}}

Node 5 — IF: Already Handled?
If handled === true → END (we’re idempotent).

Node 6 — Switch: Route by Event Type
Equals: payment_intent.succeeded

Equals: payment_intent.payment_failed

Equals: charge.refunded

StartsWith: charge.dispute.

Equals: transfer.paid

Equals: transfer.failed

6a) payment_intent.succeeded → Normalize & Forward
Postgres (upsert payment_intents)

INSERT INTO payment_intents
(id, job_id, cleaner_id, amount_cents, currency, status, last_event_type, raw)
VALUES (:pi_id, NULLIF(:job_id,''), NULLIF(:cleaner_id,''), :amount_cents, :currency,
        'succeeded', 'payment_intent.succeeded', :raw::jsonb)
ON CONFLICT (id) DO UPDATE
  SET status='succeeded',
      last_event_type='payment_intent.succeeded',
      updated_at_utc=now(),
      raw=:raw::jsonb;

SELECT 1;
Params
:pi_id {{$json["parsed"]["data"]["object"]["id"]}}
:amount_cents {{$json["parsed"]["data"]["object"]["amount_received"] || $json["parsed"]["data"]["object"]["amount"] || 0}}
:currency {{$json["parsed"]["data"]["object"]["currency"] || "usd"}}
:raw {{$json["raw_body"]}}
:job_id, :cleaner_id → same mapping as Node 4.

Then: call internal n8n webhook (or connect node) to Credit Wallet & Escrow (Section 3) to reconcile hold→charge against the job’s escrow & snapshots, as your Base44 logic prescribes. (Holds/charges/refunds are ledgered in that workflow, not here.)

6b) payment_intent.payment_failed → Notify
Upsert payment_intents as above with status='payment_failed', last_event_type='payment_intent.payment_failed'.

Trigger Notifications with payment failed template (SendGrid/Twilio).

6c) charge.refunded → Route to Refunds
Update payment_intents.last_event_type='charge.refunded'.

Trigger Refunds & Adjustments to append immutable release to the ledger and restore wallet; send client confirmation.

6d) charge.dispute. → Route to Disputes Flow*
Mark the PI last_event_type accordingly.

Trigger Disputes: set jobs.status='disputed', triage in Admin, apply outcomes (client favor → release to wallet; cleaner favor → create earnings; partial → split).

6e) transfer.paid → Mark Payouts Paid
Trigger Weekly/Instant Payout processor to mark payouts.status='paid' and notify cleaner. (We wire this fully in Sections 7 & 8.)

6f) transfer.failed → Ops Alert + Retry
Trigger payouts retry path in Admin (manual re-run).

Node 7 — Postgres: Mark Event Handled
UPDATE stripe_events
SET handled = true, handled_at_utc = now()
WHERE id = :event_id;
C) Optional Signature Verifier (Express microservice)
n8n Function nodes can’t import Stripe’s SDK; the most robust verification is a tiny proxy that accepts raw body, verifies with whsec_*, then forwards the JSON to n8n.

server.js

import express from 'express';
import bodyParser from 'body-parser';
import Stripe from 'stripe';
import fetch from 'node-fetch';

const app = express();
app.use(bodyParser.raw({ type: 'application/json' }));

const stripe = new Stripe(process.env.STRIPE_SECRET_KEY, { apiVersion: '2024-06-20' });
const endpointSecret = process.env.STRIPE_WEBHOOK_SECRET;

app.post('/verify/stripe', async (req, res) => {
  const sig = req.headers['stripe-signature'];
  let event;
  try {
    event = stripe.webhooks.constructEvent(req.body, sig, endpointSecret);
  } catch (err) {
    console.error('Stripe signature verify failed', err.message);
    return res.status(400).json({ ok: false, error: 'invalid_signature' });
  }

  const forward = await fetch(process.env.N8N_STRIPE_WEBHOOK_URL, {
    method: 'POST',
    headers: { 'Content-Type': 'application/json', 'X-Stripe-Verified': 'true' },
    body: JSON.stringify(event)
  });

  if (!forward.ok) {
    return res.status(502).json({ ok: false, error: 'forward_failed' });
  }
  res.json({ ok: true, eventId: event.id });
});

app.listen(process.env.PORT || 8080, () => console.log('Stripe verifier listening'));
.env

STRIPE_SECRET_KEY=sk_live_************************
STRIPE_WEBHOOK_SECRET=whsec_************************
N8N_STRIPE_WEBHOOK_URL=https://<your-n8n>/webhook/stripe/webhook
Your ops notes already outline how to locate keys and webhook secrets in Stripe, and the overall order of setup for DB, n8n, and endpoints.

payment_intent.payment_failed → notifications (payment failure) with the documented dynamic fields.

charge.refunded → Refunds & Adjustments ledger release (+wallet) and client email.

charge.dispute.* → Disputes (freeze, evidence, one-click admin outcomes).

transfer.paid|failed → Payouts mark paid or retry.

All math (escrow, final charge, refund, earnings) follows your approved formulas and 15-min granularity.

3) Data contracts for downstream workflows
This section’s outputs are events and normalized rows; the state changes/ledgers intentionally happen in the specialized sections to keep accounting clean:

Credit Wallet & Escrow (Section 3) will:

Append charge and release rows and mirror the wallet. (Immutable; never edit.)

Move job to awaiting_client with 24h timer; create cleaner_earnings on approval/auto-approve.

Refunds (Section 5) will: append release and adjust earnings if job was already approved (reverse + new).

Disputes (Section 6) will: set jobs.status='disputed', freeze, and post the split outcome.

Payouts (Section 7/8) will: batch pending earnings → Stripe Connect transfer(s) → mark paid/failed.

4) (Optional but recommended) Signature verifier microservice
Because n8n Function nodes can’t import the Stripe SDK, deploy a tiny Express proxy that:

receives raw body from Stripe,

verifies using whsec_*,

forwards the JSON to your n8n webhook with header X-Stripe-Verified: true.

// server.js
import express from 'express';
import bodyParser from 'body-parser';
import Stripe from 'stripe';
import fetch from 'node-fetch';

const app = express();
app.use(bodyParser.raw({ type: 'application/json' }));

const stripe = new Stripe(process.env.STRIPE_SECRET_KEY, { apiVersion: '2024-06-20' });
const endpointSecret = process.env.STRIPE_WEBHOOK_SECRET;
app.post('/verify/stripe', async (req, res) => {
  const sig = req.headers['stripe-signature'];
  let event;
  try {
    event = stripe.webhooks.constructEvent(req.body, sig, endpointSecret);
  } catch (err) {
    return res.status(400).json({ ok:false, error:'invalid_signature' });
  }
  const r = await fetch(process.env.N8N_STRIPE_WEBHOOK_URL, {
    method:'POST',
    headers:{ 'Content-Type':'application/json','X-Stripe-Verified':'true' },
    body: JSON.stringify(event)
  });
  if (!r.ok) return res.status(502).json({ ok:false, error:'forward_failed' });
  res.json({ ok:true, eventId: event.id });
});
app.listen(process.env.PORT||8080, ()=>console.log('Stripe verifier listening'));
.env

STRIPE_SECRET_KEY=sk_live_xxx
STRIPE_WEBHOOK_SECRET=whsec_xxx
N8N_STRIPE_WEBHOOK_URL=https://<n8n-host>/webhook/stripe/webhook
Your n8n node can optionally require X-Stripe-Verified: true before inserting the event.

Retries: set n8n node retries (2–3) on DB/HTTP nodes.

Alerts:

Payment failures → client comms via your SendGrid/Twilio templates (already prepared).

Payout failures → admin retry path (present in your admin actions).

Audits: never modify ledger rows; always append. (This is repeated throughout your specs.)

Totally get it—that helps. From now on I’ll assume a greenfield setup (nothing implemented yet) and I’ll hand you everything needed to build Section 1 from scratch: database migrations, a tiny verifier service, the n8n workflow (with copy-pasteable queries and expressions), deployment & test steps, and an ops runbook. I won’t assume any prior exports exist.

Below is the final, self-contained implementation for Section 1: Stripe Webhook Ingest & Dispatcher designed to work even if your system is empty today.

SECTION 1 — Stripe Webhook Ingest & Dispatcher (Greenfield Build)
What this section does
Receives Stripe webhooks

Verifies signatures (strongly recommended)

Stores every event idempotently for audit (stripe_events)

Optionally normalizes Payment Intent info (payment_intents)

Routes the event to downstream workflows (which we’ll build in Sections 2–12)

Marks the event “handled” only after successful routing

Supported event types (the ones we’ll use to drive later sections):
payment_intent.succeeded, payment_intent.payment_failed, charge.refunded, any charge.dispute.*, transfer.paid, transfer.failed.

Ledger writes (hold/charge/release/refund), job state changes, earnings, payouts, etc., are not done here on purpose—they belong to dedicated workflows you’ll implement in the later sections. This mirrors the immutable ledger + wallet mirror model in your docs.

Prereqs (tooling & accounts)
Stripe account (API keys + webhook secret)

PostgreSQL (Neon is fine)

n8n Cloud (or self-host)

Optional: Node.js runtime (for the verifier service)

Optional: domain & TLS for the verifier (or use a secure tunnel)

Step 1 — Create the database objects (copy/paste)
These are the only tables you must create for this section. The core marketplace tables (users, jobs, credit_transactions, payouts, etc.) will come in later sections.

-- 1) Event audit + idempotency
CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS stripe_events (
  id                text PRIMARY KEY,          -- Stripe evt_xxx
  type              text NOT NULL,
  created_at_utc    timestamptz NOT NULL DEFAULT now(),
  payload           jsonb NOT NULL,            -- full event body
  job_id            text,                      -- from metadata if present
  cleaner_id        text,                      -- from metadata if present
  handled           boolean NOT NULL DEFAULT false,
  handled_at_utc    timestamptz
);

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS stripe_events_type_idx ON stripe_events(type);
CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS stripe_events_job_idx  ON stripe_events(job_id);

-- 2) Optional but useful: normalized PaymentIntents
CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS payment_intents (
  id                     text PRIMARY KEY,    -- pi_xxx
  job_id                 text,
  cleaner_id             text,
  amount_cents           bigint NOT NULL DEFAULT 0,
  currency               text NOT NULL DEFAULT 'usd',
  status                 text NOT NULL,       -- 'succeeded'|'payment_failed'|...
  last_event_type        text,
  updated_at_utc         timestamptz NOT NULL DEFAULT now(),
  raw                    jsonb NOT NULL
);

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS payment_intents_job_idx     ON payment_intents(job_id);
CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS payment_intents_cleaner_idx ON payment_intents(cleaner_id);
Immutable ledgering (purchase/hold/release/charge/refund/reversal) and the “wallet mirror” rule will be implemented in Section 3’s workflow, consistent with your spec.

Step 2 — (Recommended) Signature Verifier Microservice
n8n function nodes can’t import Stripe’s SDK. The robust approach is a tiny Node service that:

Accepts raw request body from Stripe

Verifies the signature using whsec_*

Forwards the verified JSON to n8n

2.1 Files
package.json

{
  "name": "puretask-stripe-verifier",
  "version": "1.0.0",
  "type": "module",
  "dependencies": {
    "body-parser": "^1.20.2",
    "express": "^4.19.2",
    "node-fetch": "^3.3.2",
    "stripe": "^16.0.0"
  }
}
server.js

import express from 'express';
import bodyParser from 'body-parser';
import Stripe from 'stripe';
import fetch from 'node-fetch';

const app = express();
app.use(bodyParser.raw({ type: 'application/json' }));

const stripe = new Stripe(process.env.STRIPE_SECRET_KEY, { apiVersion: '2024-06-20' });
const endpointSecret = process.env.STRIPE_WEBHOOK_SECRET; // whsec_...

app.post('/verify/stripe', async (req, res) => {
  const sig = req.headers['stripe-signature'];
  let event;
  try {
    event = stripe.webhooks.constructEvent(req.body, sig, endpointSecret);
  } catch (err) {
    console.error('Stripe signature verify failed', err.message);
    return res.status(400).json({ ok: false, error: 'invalid_signature' });
  }

  const forward = await fetch(process.env.N8N_STRIPE_WEBHOOK_URL, {
    method: 'POST',
    headers: { 'Content-Type': 'application/json', 'X-Stripe-Verified': 'true' },
    body: JSON.stringify(event)
  });
  if (!forward.ok) {
    const text = await forward.text();
    console.error('Forward to n8n failed:', text);
    return res.status(502).json({ ok: false, error: 'forward_failed' });
  }
  res.json({ ok: true, eventId: event.id });
});

app.get('/healthz', (_, res) => res.json({ ok: true }));

app.listen(process.env.PORT || 8080, () => console.log('Stripe verifier listening'));
.env (example)

STRIPE_SECRET_KEY=sk_test_************************
STRIPE_WEBHOOK_SECRET=whsec_************************
N8N_STRIPE_WEBHOOK_URL=https://<your-n8n-domain>/webhook/stripe/webhook
PORT=8080
(Optional) Dockerfile

FROM node:20-alpine
WORKDIR /app
COPY package.json package-lock.json* ./
RUN npm install --omit=dev
COPY server.js ./
EXPOSE 8080
CMD ["node", "server.js"]
2.2 Deploy
Deploy anywhere (Render, Fly.io, Railway, Vercel functions w/ raw body, or your VPS)

Point Stripe’s webhook to https://<verifier>/verify/stripe (not to n8n)

Set N8N_STRIPE_WEBHOOK_URL to your n8n webhook URL

Step 3 — Create the n8n Workflow (from zero)
Workflow name: 01 - Stripe Webhook Ingest

We’ll create the 7 nodes manually. (If you prefer, I can generate a full n8n JSON export later.)

Node 1 — Webhook
HTTP Method: POST

Path: stripe/webhook

Response: 200 with body ok

This is the endpoint your verifier forwards to. If you choose not to use the verifier, you can aim Stripe directly at this, but you’ll lose SDK-level verification.

Node 2 — Function: Extract Body & Headers
Purpose: normalize header casing, keep raw + parsed

Code

const headers = $json.headers || {};
const signature = headers['stripe-signature'] || headers['Stripe-Signature'] || '';
const parsed = $json.body;
const raw_body = JSON.stringify(parsed);
return [{ json: { headers, signature, raw_body, parsed } }];
Node 3 — IF (Require Verified Header) — Optional but recommended
Condition: {{$json["headers"]["X-Stripe-Verified"] || $json["headers"]["x-stripe-verified"]}} equals 'true'

If false: Stop execution (invalid sig).

If true: Continue.

This enforces that only the verifier can forward events.

Node 4 — Postgres (Insert Event / Idempotency)
Credential: Postgres (name it exactly PureTask Postgres, per your standard)

Query

INSERT INTO stripe_events (id, type, payload, job_id, cleaner_id)
VALUES (
  :event_id,
  :type,
  :payload::jsonb,
  NULLIF(:job_id,''),
  NULLIF(:cleaner_id,'')
)
ON CONFLICT (id) DO NOTHING;

SELECT id, type, handled FROM stripe_events WHERE id = :event_id;
Params mapping

:event_id → {{$json["parsed"]["id"]}}

:type → {{$json["parsed"]["type"]}}

:payload → {{$json["raw_body"]}}

:job_id → {{$json["parsed"]["data"]["object"]["metadata"]["job_id"] || ""}}

:cleaner_id → {{$json["parsed"]["data"]["object"]["metadata"]["cleaner_id"] || ""}}

Node 5 — IF (Already Handled?)
Condition: {{$json["rows"][0]["handled"]}} equals true

If true: End (we’re idempotent)

If false: Continue

(If your SQL node doesn’t return a rows object, switch to “Execute Query” and read the returned structure; the idea is the same: if handled, exit.)

Node 6 — Switch on type
Cases:

payment_intent.succeeded

payment_intent.payment_failed

charge.refunded

charge.dispute. (use “startsWith”)

transfer.paid

transfer.failed

Now add one branch handler per case:

6A) payment_intent.succeeded — Upsert PI, then forward
Postgres Query

INSERT INTO payment_intents
(id, job_id, cleaner_id, amount_cents, currency, status, last_event_type, raw)
VALUES (:pi_id, NULLIF(:job_id,''), NULLIF(:cleaner_id,''), :amount_cents, :currency,
        'succeeded', 'payment_intent.succeeded', :raw::jsonb)
ON CONFLICT (id) DO UPDATE
  SET status='succeeded',
      last_event_type='payment_intent.succeeded',
      updated_at_utc=now(),
      raw=:raw::jsonb;

SELECT 1;
Params

:pi_id → {{$json["parsed"]["data"]["object"]["id"]}}

:amount_cents → {{$json["parsed"]["data"]["object"]["amount_received"] || $json["parsed"]["data"]["object"]["amount"] || 0}}

:currency → {{$json["parsed"]["data"]["object"]["currency"] || "usd"}}

:raw → {{$json["raw_body"]}}

:job_id, :cleaner_id → as above

Then: (we’ll wire this in Section 3) call your Credit Wallet & Escrow workflow webhook to reconcile hold → charge and compute any release (refund) using the immutable ledger model (purchase/hold/charge/release/refund).

6B) payment_intent.payment_failed — Upsert PI, then notify
Same SQL with status='payment_failed', last_event_type='payment_intent.payment_failed'

Trigger the Notifications workflow to send “payment failed” email/SMS using your SendGrid/Twilio templates (we’ll deliver templates in the notifications section).

6C) charge.refunded — Route to Refunds
Update payment_intents.last_event_type='charge.refunded'

Trigger Refunds & Adjustments (Section 5) to append immutable release to the ledger and return credits to the client’s wallet.

6D) charge.dispute.* — Route to Disputes
Mark last_event_type accordingly

Trigger Disputes workflow (Section 6) to freeze, collect evidence (photos/GPS/check-ins), and resolve with admin actions.

6E) transfer.paid — Mark payouts paid
Trigger Payouts (Section 7/8) to set payouts as paid and notify cleaners. (Weekly vs Instant covered later.)

6F) transfer.failed — Alert + Retry
Send ops alert; admin screen exposes “retry payout” action (we’ll deliver in payouts section).

Node 7 — Postgres (Mark Event Handled)
UPDATE stripe_events
SET handled = true, handled_at_utc = now()
WHERE id = :event_id;
Param :event_id → {{$json["parsed"]["id"]}}

Step 4 — Configure Stripe & n8n
Create n8n Postgres credential and name it exactly PureTask Postgres. Test connection.

Deploy Verifier (optional but best practice) and copy its URL.

Stripe → Webhooks: add https://<verifier>/verify/stripe (or direct to n8n if skipping verifier).

n8n → Workflows: set the webhook path stripe/webhook on Node 1 (already done above).

Turn on the workflow.

Step 5 — Test Plan (end-to-end)
A) With Stripe CLI

# Point the listener to your verifier or straight to n8n
stripe listen --forward-to https://<verifier>/verify/stripe

stripe trigger payment_intent.succeeded
stripe trigger payment_intent.payment_failed
stripe trigger charge.refunded
stripe trigger charge.dispute.created
stripe trigger transfer.paid
stripe trigger transfer.failed
B) DB Assertions

SELECT id, type, handled FROM stripe_events ORDER BY created_at_utc DESC;
SELECT id, status, last_event_type FROM payment_intents ORDER BY updated_at_utc DESC;
C) Idempotency

Re-run one of the same events (copy payload/event id) → confirm stripe_events.handled=true prevents re-processing.

D) Downstream smoke

For payment_intent.succeeded: ensure your Section 3 (once we build it) is receiving the event and posting proper charge/release entries to the ledger (immutable) and updating wallet mirrors.

Step 6 — Operations & Security
Idempotency: enforced by stripe_events.id PK and handled flag.

Retries: set 2–3 node retries on DB/HTTP nodes in n8n.

Secrets: store Stripe keys & webhook secret in environment variables (verifier) or n8n env vars.

Logging: all events stored in stripe_events.payload for forensics.

No ledger writes here: all accounting is done in dedicated flows later (immutability).

Deliverables you can copy now
SQL migrations (above)

Verifier microservice (package.json, server.js, optional Dockerfile, .env)

n8n workflow plan with:

Webhook node config

Function code (extract)

IF (verified) node (optional)

Postgres “insert/select” query with exact parameter mappings

Switch by event type + branch actions

Postgres “mark handled” query

2) Stripe Verifier Microservice (recommended)
This verifies Stripe signatures (SDK-level) and forwards verified JSON to n8n.

Create a folder (e.g., services/stripe-verifier) with these files.

package.json
{
  "name": "puretask-stripe-verifier",
  "version": "1.0.0",
  "type": "module",
  "dependencies": {
    "body-parser": "^1.20.2",
    "express": "^4.19.2",
    "node-fetch": "^3.3.2",
    "stripe": "^16.0.0"
  }
}
server.js
import express from 'express';
import bodyParser from 'body-parser';
import Stripe from 'stripe';
import fetch from 'node-fetch';

const app = express();
app.use(bodyParser.raw({ type: 'application/json' }));

const stripe = new Stripe(process.env.STRIPE_SECRET_KEY, { apiVersion: '2024-06-20' });
const endpointSecret = process.env.STRIPE_WEBHOOK_SECRET; // whsec_...

app.post('/verify/stripe', async (req, res) => {
  const sig = req.headers['stripe-signature'];
  let event;
  try {
    event = stripe.webhooks.constructEvent(req.body, sig, endpointSecret);
  } catch (err) {
    console.error('Stripe signature verify failed:', err.message);
    return res.status(400).json({ ok: false, error: 'invalid_signature' });
  }

  const forwardResp = await fetch(process.env.N8N_STRIPE_WEBHOOK_URL, {
    method: 'POST',
    headers: { 'Content-Type': 'application/json', 'X-Stripe-Verified': 'true' },
    body: JSON.stringify(event)
  });

  if (!forwardResp.ok) {
    const text = await forwardResp.text();
    console.error('Forward to n8n failed:', text);
    return res.status(502).json({ ok: false, error: 'forward_failed' });
  }

  res.json({ ok: true, eventId: event.id });
});

app.get('/healthz', (_req, res) => res.json({ ok: true }));

app.listen(process.env.PORT || 8080, () => console.log('Stripe verifier listening'));

3) n8n Workflow (import JSON as-is)
In n8n, go to Workflows → Import from File/Clipboard and paste this JSON.

It expects a Postgres credential named exactly PureTask Postgres (create it first).

Handlers for other sections are stubbed as HTTP Request nodes with placeholder URLs. Replace them later with your real endpoints/workflows (or disable those request nodes until ready).

workflow_01_stripe_webhook_ingest.json
{
  "name": "01 - Stripe Webhook Ingest",
  "nodes": [
    {
      "parameters": {
        "path": "stripe/webhook",
        "httpMethod": "POST",
        "responseMode": "onReceived",
        "options": {
          "responseData": "ok",
          "responseCode": 200
        }
      },
      "type": "n8n-nodes-base.webhook",
      "typeVersion": 1,
      "position": [200, 300],
      "name": "Webhook: Stripe In"
    },
    {
      "parameters": {
        "functionCode": "const headers = $json.headers || {};\nconst signature = headers['stripe-signature'] || headers['Stripe-Signature'] || '';\nconst parsed = $json.body;\nconst raw_body = JSON.stringify(parsed);\nreturn [{ json: { headers, signature, raw_body, parsed } }];"
      },
      "type": "n8n-nodes-base.function",
      "typeVersion": 2,
      "position": [460, 300],
      "name": "Extract Body/Headers"
    },
    {
      "parameters": {
        "conditions": {
          "boolean": [],
          "string": [
            {
              "value1": "={{$json[\"headers\"][\"X-Stripe-Verified\"] || $json[\"headers\"][\"x-stripe-verified\"]}}",
              "operation": "equal",
              "value2": "true"
            }
          ]
        }
      },
      "type": "n8n-nodes-base.if",
      "typeVersion": 2,
      "position": [700, 300],
      "name": "Require Verified Header (optional)"
    },
    {
      "parameters": {
        "operation": "executeQuery",
        "query": "INSERT INTO stripe_events (id, type, payload, job_id, cleaner_id)\nVALUES (\n  :event_id,\n  :type,\n  :payload::jsonb,\n  NULLIF(:job_id,''),\n  NULLIF(:cleaner_id,'')\n)\nON CONFLICT (id) DO NOTHING;\n",
        "additionalFields": {
          "queryParams": "event_id,type,payload,job_id,cleaner_id",
          "values": "={{$json[\"parsed\"][\"id\"]}},{{ $json[\"parsed\"][\"type\"] }},{{ $json[\"raw_body\"] }},{{ $json[\"parsed\"][\"data\"][\"object\"][\"metadata\"][\"job_id\"] || '' }},{{ $json[\"parsed\"][\"data\"][\"object\"][\"metadata\"][\"cleaner_id\"] || '' }}"
        }
      },
      "type": "n8n-nodes-base.postgres",
      "typeVersion": 1,
      "position": [960, 220],
      "name": "DB: Insert Event",
      "credentials": {
        "postgres": {
          "name": "PureTask Postgres"
        }
      }
    },
    {
      "parameters": {
        "operation": "executeQuery",
        "query": "SELECT id, type, handled FROM stripe_events WHERE id = :event_id;",
        "additionalFields": {
          "queryParams": "event_id",
          "values": "={{$json[\"parsed\"][\"id\"]}}"
        }
      },
      "type": "n8n-nodes-base.postgres",
      "typeVersion": 1,
      "position": [960, 380],
      "name": "DB: Check Handled",
      "credentials": {
        "postgres": {
          "name": "PureTask Postgres"
        }
      }
    },
    {
      "parameters": {
        "conditions": {
          "boolean": [],
          "number": [],
          "string": [
            {
              "value1": "={{$json[\"rows\"][0] && $json[\"rows\"][0][\"handled\"]}}",
              "operation": "equal",
              "value2": "true"
            }
          ]
        }
      },
      "type": "n8n-nodes-base.if",
      "typeVersion": 2,
      "position": [1200, 380],
      "name": "IF Already Handled?"
    },
    {
      "parameters": {
        "propertyName": "={{$json[\"parsed\"][\"type\"]}}",
        "rules": {
          "rules": [
            { "operation": "equal", "value": "payment_intent.succeeded" },
            { "operation": "equal", "value": "payment_intent.payment_failed" },
            { "operation": "equal", "value": "charge.refunded" },
            { "operation": "startsWith", "value": "charge.dispute." },
            { "operation": "equal", "value": "transfer.paid" },
            { "operation": "equal", "value": "transfer.failed" }
          ]
        }
      },
      "type": "n8n-nodes-base.switch",
      "typeVersion": 2,
      "position": [1440, 220],
      "name": "Route by Event Type"
    },
    {
      "parameters": {
        "operation": "executeQuery",
        "query": "INSERT INTO payment_intents\n(id, job_id, cleaner_id, amount_cents, currency, status, last_event_type, raw)\nVALUES (:pi_id, NULLIF(:job_id,''), NULLIF(:cleaner_id,''), :amount_cents, :currency,\n        'succeeded', 'payment_intent.succeeded', :raw::jsonb)\nON CONFLICT (id) DO UPDATE\n  SET status='succeeded',\n      last_event_type='payment_intent.succeeded',\n      updated_at_utc=now(),\n      raw=:raw::jsonb;",
        "additionalFields": {
          "queryParams": "pi_id,job_id,cleaner_id,amount_cents,currency,raw",
          "values": "={{$json[\"parsed\"][\"data\"][\"object\"][\"id\"]}},{{ $json[\"parsed\"][\"data\"][\"object\"][\"metadata\"][\"job_id\"] || '' }},{{ $json[\"parsed\"][\"data\"][\"object\"][\"metadata\"][\"cleaner_id\"] || '' }},{{ $json[\"parsed\"][\"data\"][\"object\"][\"amount_received\"] || $json[\"parsed\"][\"data\"][\"object\"][\"amount\"] || 0 }},{{ $json[\"parsed\"][\"data\"][\"object\"][\"currency\"] || 'usd' }},{{ $json[\"raw_body\"] }}"
        }
      },
      "type": "n8n-nodes-base.postgres",
      "typeVersion": 1,
      "position": [1700, 60],
      "name": "DB: Upsert PI (succeeded)",
      "credentials": {
        "postgres": {
          "name": "PureTask Postgres"
        }
      }
    },
    {
      "parameters": {
        "url": "https://REPLACE_ME/credit-escrow/handle-pi-succeeded",
        "method": "POST",
        "sendBody": true,
        "jsonParameters": true,
        "options": {},
        "bodyParametersJson": "={\n  \"event_id\": $json[\"parsed\"][\"id\"],\n  \"job_id\": $json[\"parsed\"][\"data\"][\"object\"][\"metadata\"][\"job_id\"] || null,\n  \"cleaner_id\": $json[\"parsed\"][\"data\"][\"object\"][\"metadata\"][\"cleaner_id\"] || null,\n  \"amount_cents\": $json[\"parsed\"][\"data\"][\"object\"][\"amount_received\"] || $json[\"parsed\"][\"data\"][\"object\"][\"amount\"] || 0,\n  \"currency\": $json[\"parsed\"][\"data\"][\"object\"][\"currency\"] || \"usd\"\n}"
      },
      "type": "n8n-nodes-base.httpRequest",
      "typeVersion": 3,

Absolutely—here’s a clear, step-by-step implementation guide for every snippet from Section 1 so you can copy/paste and get it running from a blank slate. No prior setup assumed.

Folder structure (recommended)
puretask/
├─ db/
│  ├─ 001_create_stripe_events.sql
│  └─ 002_create_payment_intents.sql
├─ services/
│  └─ stripe-verifier/
│     ├─ package.json
│     ├─ server.js
│     ├─ .env   (create locally, don’t commit)
│     └─ Dockerfile (optional)
└─ n8n/
   └─ workflow_01_stripe_webhook_ingest.json
Part A — SQL migrations (Postgres/Neon)
What they do
001_create_stripe_events.sql: creates stripe_events table for audit + idempotency.

002_create_payment_intents.sql: optional convenience table to quickly look up the latest PaymentIntent state.

How to run them
Option 1: Neon SQL console
Open your Neon project → SQL Editor.

Paste the full contents of 001_create_stripe_events.sql, click Run.

Paste the full contents of 002_create_payment_intents.sql, click Run.

Option 2: psql CLI
# Example using a full connection string
export DATABASE_URL='postgresql://USER:PASSWORD@HOST:PORT/DBNAME?sslmode=require'
psql "$DATABASE_URL" -f db/001_create_stripe_events.sql
psql "$DATABASE_URL" -f db/002_create_payment_intents.sql
Verify tables
\d+ stripe_events;
\d+ payment_intents;
If both show columns and indexes, you’re good.

Part B — Stripe Verifier Microservice
What it does
Receives raw Stripe webhook requests

Verifies the signature using Stripe’s SDK (whsec_*)

Forwards validated JSON to your n8n Webhook with a header X-Stripe-Verified: true

Set up locally (Node.js)
Navigate to services/stripe-verifier.

Create files exactly as provided:

package.json

server.js

.env (from .env.example, fill values)

Install and run:

cd services/stripe-verifier
npm install
cp .env.example .env
# Edit .env and set:
# STRIPE_SECRET_KEY=sk_test_...
# STRIPE_WEBHOOK_SECRET=whsec_...
# N8N_STRIPE_WEBHOOK_URL=https://YOUR-N8N-DOMAIN/webhook/stripe/webhook
npm start
Confirm health:

Open http://localhost:8080/healthz → should return { ok: true }.

Deploy to a host (Docker optional)
Docker build/run

docker build -t puretask-stripe-verifier .
docker run -p 8080:8080 --env-file .env puretask-stripe-verifier
Render/Fly/Railway: create a Node service, set the 3 env vars, deploy.

Connect Stripe to the verifier
Stripe Dashboard → Developers → Webhooks → Add endpoint.

Endpoint URL: https://<your-verifier-domain>/verify/stripe

Select events: you can start with “Send all events” or only:

payment_intent.succeeded

payment_intent.payment_failed

charge.refunded

charge.dispute.*

transfer.paid

transfer.failed

Stripe will show you a Webhook signing secret (whsec_...). Put it in .env as STRIPE_WEBHOOK_SECRET.

Tip: if you’re testing locally, use Stripe CLI forwarding (see Test section).

Part C — n8n Workflow (import + connect)
What it does
Receives forwarded JSON webhooks from the verifier

Checks X-Stripe-Verified: true (optional node in the flow)

Writes every event to stripe_events (idempotent)

Upserts PaymentIntent records where relevant

Routes to placeholder HTTP endpoints for the next sections (you’ll plug those later)

Marks the event handled

One-time prep: create the Postgres credential
In n8n → Credentials → Add Credential → Postgres.

Fill Host/Port/DB/User/Password/SSL (Neon uses SSL).

Name it exactly: PureTask Postgres (spelling & case matter).

Test and Save.

Import the workflow
n8n → Workflows → Import from File/Clipboard.

Paste the entire JSON from n8n/workflow_01_stripe_webhook_ingest.json.

Open the workflow and check:

Node Webhook: Stripe In has path stripe/webhook.

All Postgres nodes reference the credential PureTask Postgres.

The optional IF node (“Require Verified Header”) exists—keep it if you’re using the verifier.

Activate it
Click Activate (top right).

n8n will now be ready to accept events forwarded by your verifier.

-- Were events saved?
SELECT id, type, handled, created_at_utc
FROM stripe_events
ORDER BY created_at_utc DESC
LIMIT 20;

-- Did a PI row appear for succeeded/failed?
SELECT id, status, last_event_type, updated_at_utc
FROM payment_intents
ORDER BY updated_at_utc DESC
LIMIT 20;
Idempotency check
Re-run the same event (or hit “Resend” in Stripe Dashboard).
You should see the stripe_events row already exists; the workflow should detect “Already Handled?” and exit without duplicate processing.

Part F — Common pitfalls & fixes
Symptom	Cause	Fix
n8n shows signature required / invalid	You kept the “Require Verified Header” node but are posting to n8n directly (no verifier)	Either deploy the verifier, or delete/disable the “Require Verified Header” IF node
Postgres nodes fail to connect	Credential misnamed or wrong SSL	Name must be exactly PureTask Postgres; Neon requires SSL (?sslmode=require if using URL)
No events appear	Stripe webhook not pointed to verifier, or verifier not forwarding to n8n	In Stripe, endpoint must be …/verify/stripe; set N8N_STRIPE_WEBHOOK_URL correctly; check verifier logs
payment_intents has missing job/cleaner	Stripe metadata not present on the PI or Charge	Ensure your payment creation code attaches metadata.job_id & metadata.cleaner_id (we’ll provide this when we wire the booking/payment creation later)
Placeholder HTTP calls fail	We haven’t built Sections 3/5/6/7/8/9 yet	Disable those HTTP Request nodes for now; re-enable after you import each section
Part G — Security & ops tips
Secrets: never commit .env. Use your hosting provider’s secret manager.

Network: restrict the verifier to accept POSTs only from Stripe IPs (optional defense-in-depth).

Logging: the stripe_events.payload JSON is your audit trail. Consider a retention policy.

Monitoring: add a simple uptime monitor for the verifier’s /healthz.

proced with - Job Lifecycle Orchestrator (create → accept → in-progress → completed → awaiting_client → approved / disputed / cancelled)

Trigger: App/API actions (create/accept/check-in/out/complete/approve/cancel)
Does: Drives the state machine; tracks GPS check-in/out; actual hours; computes final charge & any refund.
Writes: jobs state, timing; snapshot rates; final_charge_credits, refund_credits.
Notify/External: reminders, “on the way”, completion emails/SMS (SendGrid/Twilio).
Edge cases: Early finish (auto refund); more time (top-up escrow); insufficient wallet credits; dispute hold.

1) SQL — create the data model
Run these in order. They don’t collide with Section 1. They assume you already have a users table with role and cleaner rate fields (we snapshot them here). If you don’t, the workflow still works—you’ll just pass cleaner rates explicitly in the “accept” step.

003_enums_and_helpers.sql
-- Status, cleaning type, and event enums
DO $$ BEGIN
  CREATE TYPE job_status AS ENUM (
    'created', 'accepted', 'in_progress', 'completed',
    'awaiting_client', 'approved', 'disputed', 'cancelled'
  );
EXCEPTION WHEN duplicate_object THEN NULL; END $$;

DO $$ BEGIN
  CREATE TYPE cleaning_type AS ENUM ('basic', 'deep', 'moveout');
EXCEPTION WHEN duplicate_object THEN NULL; END $$;

DO $$ BEGIN
  CREATE TYPE job_event_type AS ENUM (
    'job.created','job.accepted','job.checkin','job.checkout','job.completed',
    'job.awaiting_client','job.approved','job.disputed','job.cancelled',
    'job.topup_required','job.topup_confirmed','job.auto_approved'
  );
EXCEPTION WHEN duplicate_object THEN NULL; END $$;

-- 15-min rounding helper (rounds UP to next 0.25 hr when flag=true)
CREATE OR REPLACE FUNCTION round_hours_15min(
  seconds BIGINT,
  round_up BOOLEAN DEFAULT false
) RETURNS NUMERIC AS $$
DECLARE hrs NUMERIC;
BEGIN
  hrs := seconds / 3600.0;
  IF round_up THEN
    RETURN CEIL(hrs * 4)::NUMERIC / 4.0;
  ELSE
    RETURN ROUND(hrs * 4) / 4.0;
  END IF;
END; $$ LANGUAGE plpgsql IMMUTABLE;
004_jobs_core.sql
-- Jobs: one row per booking
CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS jobs (
  id                  TEXT PRIMARY KEY,          -- job_xxx (UUID or ULID), set by API or n8n
  client_id           TEXT NOT NULL,             -- fk -> users(id)
  cleaner_id          TEXT,                      -- set on accept (nullable until accepted)

  status              job_status NOT NULL DEFAULT 'created',
  cleaning_type       cleaning_type NOT NULL,
  service_address     TEXT NOT NULL,
  service_lat         NUMERIC(10,7),             -- optional GPS check
  service_lng         NUMERIC(10,7),

  -- requested window & estimate set at create
  requested_start_at  TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL,
  estimated_hours     NUMERIC(5,2) NOT NULL CHECK (estimated_hours > 0),

  -- pricing snapshot (frozen at accept)
  snapshot_base_rate_cph         NUMERIC(8,2),   -- credits per hour
  snapshot_deep_addon_cph        NUMERIC(8,2),
  snapshot_moveout_addon_cph     NUMERIC(8,2),
  snapshot_payout_percentage     NUMERIC(4,2),   -- e.g., 0.80 .. 0.85 (captured at accept)

  -- escrow/hold planning captured at create/accept
  held_credits                    NUMERIC(10,2) DEFAULT 0,   -- total held at start (includes 25% buffer)
  hold_buffer_percentage          NUMERIC(5,2)  DEFAULT 0.25,

  -- timing actuals
  checkin_at           TIMESTAMPTZ,
  checkout_at          TIMESTAMPTZ,
  total_seconds_worked BIGINT DEFAULT 0,

  -- charges (filled after completion math)
  final_charge_credits NUMERIC(10,2) DEFAULT 0,
  refund_credits       NUMERIC(10,2) DEFAULT 0,

  -- lifecycle timestamps
  created_at           TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT now(),
  accepted_at          TIMESTAMPTZ,
  completed_at         TIMESTAMPTZ,
  awaiting_client_at   TIMESTAMPTZ,
  approved_at          TIMESTAMPTZ,
  cancelled_at         TIMESTAMPTZ,
  disputed_at          TIMESTAMPTZ
);

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS jobs_client_idx   ON jobs(client_id);
CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS jobs_cleaner_idx  ON jobs(cleaner_id);
CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS jobs_status_idx   ON jobs(status);
CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS jobs_time_idx     ON jobs(requested_start_at);

-- Event audit log for jobs
CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS job_events (
  id            BIGSERIAL PRIMARY KEY,
  job_id        TEXT NOT NULL,
  event_type    job_event_type NOT NULL,
  payload       JSONB,
  occurred_at   TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT now()
);
CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS job_events_job_idx ON job_events(job_id);

-- Detailed time logs (supports multiple pauses if needed)
CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS job_time_logs (
  id            BIGSERIAL PRIMARY KEY,
  job_id        TEXT NOT NULL,
  started_at    TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL,
  ended_at      TIMESTAMPTZ,
  segment_seconds BIGINT DEFAULT 0
);
CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS job_time_logs_job_idx ON job_time_logs(job_id);

-- Optional: photo proofs
CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS job_photos (
  id            BIGSERIAL PRIMARY KEY,
  job_id        TEXT NOT NULL,
  role          TEXT CHECK (role IN ('before','after')) NOT NULL,
  url           TEXT NOT NULL,
  uploaded_at   TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT now()
);
CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS job_photos_job_idx ON job_photos(job_id);

-- Optional: GPS check-ins for audit/debug (besides fields on jobs)
CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS job_gps_logs (
  id            BIGSERIAL PRIMARY KEY,
  job_id        TEXT NOT NULL,
  action        TEXT CHECK (action IN ('checkin','checkout')) NOT NULL,
  lat           NUMERIC(10,7),
  lng           NUMERIC(10,7),
  distance_m    NUMERIC(10,2),
  recorded_at   TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT now()
);
CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS job_gps_logs_job_idx ON job_gps_logs(job_id);
005_jobs_compute_functions.sql
-- Compute charge in credits based on snapshots & actual hours
-- cleaning_type determines which addon rate applies (deep/moveout), else 0
CREATE OR REPLACE FUNCTION calc_job_charge_credits(
  cleaning cleaning_type,
  hours NUMERIC,
  base_cph NUMERIC,
  deep_cph NUMERIC,
  moveout_cph NUMERIC
) RETURNS NUMERIC AS $$
DECLARE addon NUMERIC := 0;
BEGIN
  IF cleaning = 'deep' THEN
    addon := COALESCE(deep_cph,0);
  ELSIF cleaning = 'moveout' THEN
    addon := COALESCE(moveout_cph,0);
  END IF;
  RETURN (COALESCE(base_cph,0) + addon) * COALESCE(hours,0);
END; $$ LANGUAGE plpgsql IMMUTABLE;

-- Convenience: recompute total_seconds_worked from job_time_logs
CREATE OR REPLACE FUNCTION recompute_job_seconds(job_id_in TEXT)
RETURNS BIGINT AS $$
DECLARE total BIGINT;
BEGIN
  SELECT COALESCE(SUM(segment_seconds),0)
    INTO total
  FROM job_time_logs
  WHERE job_id = job_id_in;

  UPDATE jobs
     SET total_seconds_worked = total
   WHERE id = job_id_in;

  RETURN total;
END; $$ LANGUAGE plpgsql;
2) n8n workflow (importable JSON)
This single workflow exposes 8 webhooks for the app/API to call:

POST /jobs/create

POST /jobs/accept

POST /jobs/checkin

POST /jobs/checkout

POST /jobs/complete

POST /jobs/approve

POST /jobs/cancel

POST /jobs/dispute

It writes the DB changes, emits job events, calculates time/charges, sets statuses, schedules auto-approve (24h), and calls placeholder HTTP URLs for Credit Wallet/Top-up (Sec-3) and Notifications (Sec-9). Replace those placeholders later.

Create a Postgres credential named exactly PureTask Postgres before importing.

    "DB: checkin & start segment": {"main":[[{"node":"→ Notify: on the way","type":"main","index":0}]]},

    "WH: checkout": {"main":[[{"node":"Checkout: extract","type":"main","index":0}]]},
    "Checkout: extract": {"main":[[{"node":"DB: checkout & end segment","type":"main","index":0}]]},

    "WH: complete": {"main":[[{"node":"Complete: extract","type":"main","index":0}]]},
    "Complete: extract": {"main":[[{"node":"DB: compute charges","type":"main","index":0}]]},
    "DB: compute charges": {"main":[[{"node":"DB: set awaiting_client","type":"main","index":0}]]},
    "DB: set awaiting_client": {"main":[[{"node":"Wait 24h (auto-approve timer)","type":"main","index":0}]]},
    "Wait 24h (auto-approve timer)": {"main":[[{"node":"DB: auto-approve","type":"main","index":0}]]},
    "DB: auto-approve": {"main":[[{"node":"→ (Sec3) Ledger: approve (charge & refund)","type":"main","index":0}]]},
    "→ (Sec3) Ledger: approve (charge & refund)": {"main":[[{"node":"→ Notify: completed","type":"main","index":0}]]},

    "WH: approve": {"main":[[{"node":"Approve: extract","type":"main","index":0}]]},
    "Approve: extract": {"main":[[{"node":"DB: approve","type":"main","index":0}]]},
    "DB: approve": {"main":[[{"node":"→ (Sec3) Ledger: approve (charge & refund)","type":"main","index":0}]]},
    "→ (Sec3) Ledger: approve (charge & refund)": {"main":[[{"node":"→ Notify: approved","type":"main","index":0}]]},

    "WH: cancel": {"main":[[{"node":"Cancel: extract","type":"main","index":0}]]},
    "Cancel: extract": {"main":[[{"node":"DB: cancel","type":"main","index":0}]]},
    "DB: cancel": {"main":[[{"node":"→ (Sec3) Ledger: on-cancel","type":"main","index":0}]]},

    "WH: dispute": {"main":[[{"node":"Dispute: extract","type":"main","index":0}]]},
    "Dispute: extract": {"main":[[{"node":"DB: dispute","type":"main","index":0}]]},
    "DB: dispute": {"main":[[{"node":"→ (Sec6) Disputes: open","type":"main","index":0}]]}
  },
  "active": false
}
3) Action contracts (what your app should send)
3.1 Create (client books)
POST /jobs/create
Body

{
  "job_id": "job_123",             // your UUID/ULID
  "client_id": "usr_client_1",
  "cleaning_type": "deep",         // basic|deep|moveout
  "address": "123 Main St, City",
  "lat": 38.5781,                  // optional
  "lng": -121.4904,                // optional
  "requested_start_at": "2025-11-14T18:00:00Z",
  "estimated_hours": 4.0,
  "hold_buffer_pct": 0.25
}
What happens: job row created with status=created, event logged, confirmation notification fired.

Escrow hold happens in Section-3 when you accept (or you can hold at create—either way we’ll wire through the Ledger workflow later).

3.2 Accept (cleaner claims)
POST /jobs/accept
Body

{
  "job_id": "job_123",
  "cleaner_id": "usr_cleaner_9",
  "base_cph": 320.0,
  "deep_cph": 40.0,
  "moveout_cph": 50.0,
  "payout_pct": 0.80,
  "held_credits": 1600.0          // estimated total including 25% buffer
}
What happens: snapshots frozen, status=accepted, event recorded, notify client/cleaner.

If you want to hold credits now, call the Section-3 hold endpoint from your app, then pass held_credits here (or let Section-3 compute and return).

3.3 Check-in (cleaner arrives)
POST /jobs/checkin
Body

{ "job_id": "job_123", "lat": 38.5782, "lng": -121.4905 }
What happens: start a time segment, status=in_progress, logs GPS + event, notify “on the way”.

3.4 Check-out
POST /jobs/checkout
Body

{ "job_id": "job_123", "lat": 38.5783, "lng": -121.4906 }
What happens: close the open time segment, recompute total_seconds_worked.

3.5 Complete (compute charges, move to waiting)
POST /jobs/complete
Body

{ "job_id": "job_123", "require_round_up": true }  // true = round UP to next 15-min
What happens: computes hours (15-min rounding), sets final_charge_credits, moves to awaiting_client, starts a 24h auto-approve timer, sends completion notification.

3.6 Approve (client taps approve)
POST /jobs/approve
Body

{ "job_id": "job_123" }
What happens: sets status=approved, calls Section-3 to charge and refund any unused escrow, sends approved notification.

If the client doesn’t respond, the timer auto-approves in 24h and triggers the same Section-3 call.

3.7 Cancel
POST /jobs/cancel
Body

{ "job_id": "job_123", "reason": "Client requested reschedule" }
What happens: sets status=cancelled, calls Section-3 to release credits according to your rules.

3.8 Dispute
POST /jobs/dispute
Body

{ "job_id": "job_123", "reason": "Missed areas" }
What happens: sets status=disputed, hands off to Disputes (Sec-6) for evidence and outcome.

4) Business rules, formulas & edge cases
Time rounding: 15-minute increments (round_hours_15min(seconds, true) rounds up). You can set require_round_up=false to round to nearest.

Final charge formula (credits):
final = (base_cph + addon_cph) * hours_actual

addon_cph = deep_cph if cleaning_type=deep, or moveout_cph if moveout, else 0.

Refund credits (computed in Section-3): refund = held_credits − final_charge_credits (≥ 0).

Top-up (insufficient hold mid-job): your In-Progress screen should watch elapsed value vs held_credits; if low, call Section-3 top-up hold. (We’ll implement that in Section-3. This workflow just logs and continues.)

GPS tolerance: we log lat/lng; add distance checks in app level (optionally compute distance_m in job_gps_logs).

Photos: upload to your storage/CDN and call a tiny endpoint (or a direct DB write) to add job_photos rows (before/after). This workflow doesn’t enforce them; it records presence via Disputes/Notifications later.

Auto-approve: Wait node is 24h (86,400,000 ms). Change if needed.

Awesome — here’s a greenfield, copy-paste implementation for Section 3: Credit Wallet & Escrow Manager. I reviewed your docs and locked to the canon you set:

Immutable ledger with types: purchase | hold | release | charge | refund | reversal and a wallet mirror rule.

Wallet balance computed as: Σ(purchase + release + refund) − Σ(hold + charge) and mirrored to users.wallet_credits_balance atomically.

Credits are service units (not cash); purchases are final except where law applies; cleaners convert earned credits via payouts later. (Legal framing.)

This bundle includes:

SQL migrations (tables, views, triggers, functions, idempotency)

n8n workflow JSON exposing webhooks used by Sections 1 & 2 (hold/top-up/approve/cancel/purchase/admin-adjust)

Payload contracts, edge-case logic, and a step-by-step runbook

1) SQL — Ledger, wallet mirror, helpers
Run these in order after Section 2. These do not overwrite prior tables.

006_credit_ledger_core.sql
-- 1) Ledger table (immutable)
CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS credit_transactions (
  id                 BIGSERIAL PRIMARY KEY,
  client_id          TEXT NOT NULL,             -- fk -> users(id)
  job_id             TEXT,                      -- nullable when not job-related
  type               TEXT NOT NULL CHECK (type IN
                       ('purchase','hold','release','charge','refund','reversal')),
  amount_credits     NUMERIC(12,2) NOT NULL,    -- signed; see direction rules below
  note               TEXT,
  idempotency_key    TEXT,                      -- to dedupe external calls
  created_at         TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT now()
);

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS credit_tx_client_idx ON credit_transactions(client_id);
CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS credit_tx_job_idx    ON credit_transactions(job_id);
CREATE UNIQUE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS credit_tx_idem_uniq ON credit_transactions(idempotency_key)
  WHERE idempotency_key IS NOT NULL;

-- Direction rules (informational):
-- +amount for events that INCREASE wallet (purchase, release, refund, reversal+)
-- -amount for events that DECREASE wallet (hold, charge, reversal-)
-- We'll enforce totals via a view + trigger that mirrors computed balance.

-- 2) Wallet view (ground truth balance from ledger)
CREATE OR REPLACE VIEW v_wallet_balances AS
SELECT
  client_id,
  COALESCE(SUM(
    CASE type
      WHEN 'purchase' THEN amount_credits
      WHEN 'release'  THEN amount_credits
      WHEN 'refund'   THEN amount_credits
      WHEN 'reversal' THEN amount_credits       -- signed as posted
      WHEN 'hold'     THEN -amount_credits
      WHEN 'charge'   THEN -amount_credits
      ELSE 0
    END
  ),0)::NUMERIC(12,2) AS computed_wallet_credits
FROM credit_transactions
GROUP BY client_id;

-- 3) Mirror balance to users on every ledger write
ALTER TABLE IF NOT EXISTS users
  ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS wallet_credits_balance NUMERIC(12,2) NOT NULL DEFAULT 0;

CREATE OR REPLACE FUNCTION sync_user_wallet_balance(p_client_id TEXT)
RETURNS VOID AS $$
BEGIN
  UPDATE users u
     SET wallet_credits_balance = COALESCE(v.computed_wallet_credits,0)
    FROM v_wallet_balances v
   WHERE u.id = p_client_id
     AND v.client_id = p_client_id;
END; $$ LANGUAGE plpgsql;

CREATE OR REPLACE FUNCTION on_credit_tx_after_insert()
RETURNS TRIGGER AS $$
BEGIN
  PERFORM sync_user_wallet_balance(NEW.client_id);
  RETURN NEW;
END; $$ LANGUAGE plpgsql;

DROP TRIGGER IF EXISTS trg_credit_tx_after_insert ON credit_transactions;
CREATE TRIGGER trg_credit_tx_after_insert
AFTER INSERT ON credit_transactions
FOR EACH ROW EXECUTE FUNCTION on_credit_tx_after_insert();

-- 4) Advisory lock helper to serialize per-client ledger posting
CREATE OR REPLACE FUNCTION client_lock_key(p_client_id TEXT)
RETURNS BIGINT AS $$
-- Turn a UUID-ish string into a 64-bit key (poor man's hash)
DECLARE k BIGINT;
BEGIN
  -- simple crc32-ish fold; acceptable for advisory locks
  SELECT ('x'||substr(md5(p_client_id),1,16))::bit(64)::bigint INTO k;
  RETURN k;
END; $$ LANGUAGE plpgsql IMMUTABLE;

-- 5) Safe posting function with idempotency + direction checks
CREATE OR REPLACE FUNCTION post_credit_tx(
  p_client_id       TEXT,
  p_job_id          TEXT,
  p_type            TEXT,
  p_amount_credits  NUMERIC,
  p_note            TEXT,
  p_idempotency_key TEXT DEFAULT NULL
) RETURNS BIGINT AS $$
DECLARE
  k BIGINT := client_lock_key(p_client_id);
  new_id BIGINT;
BEGIN
  -- Basic validation: enforce sign convention
  IF p_type IN ('hold','charge') AND p_amount_credits <= 0 THEN
    RAISE EXCEPTION 'hold/charge require positive amount credits';
  END IF;
  IF p_type IN ('purchase','release','refund') AND p_amount_credits <= 0 THEN
    RAISE EXCEPTION 'purchase/release/refund require positive amount credits';
  END IF;
  -- 'reversal' can be +/- depending what you reverse; allow any sign.

  -- Idempotency: if a row with this key exists, return its id
  IF p_idempotency_key IS NOT NULL THEN
    SELECT id INTO new_id FROM credit_transactions WHERE idempotency_key = p_idempotency_key;
    IF FOUND THEN
      RETURN new_id;
    END IF;
  END IF;

  -- Serialize per client
  PERFORM pg_advisory_xact_lock(k);

  -- Insert
  INSERT INTO credit_transactions(client_id, job_id, type, amount_credits, note, idempotency_key)
  VALUES (p_client_id, p_job_id, p_type, p_amount_credits, p_note, p_idempotency_key)
  RETURNING id INTO new_id;

  -- Mirror balance via trigger; return id
  RETURN new_id;
END; $$ LANGUAGE plpgsql;
007_credit_checks_and_views.sql
-- Outstanding holds per job (sum of holds minus releases tagged to job before approval)
CREATE OR REPLACE VIEW v_job_holds AS
SELECT
  job_id,
  client_id,
  COALESCE(SUM(CASE WHEN type='hold' THEN amount_credits
                    WHEN type='release' THEN -amount_credits
                    ELSE 0 END),0)::NUMERIC(12,2) AS net_held_credits
FROM credit_transactions
WHERE job_id IS NOT NULL
GROUP BY job_id, client_id;

-- Wallet + holds overview for a client
CREATE OR REPLACE VIEW v_client_wallet_overview AS
SELECT
  u.id AS client_id,
  u.wallet_credits_balance,
  COALESCE(SUM(vh.net_held_credits),0)::NUMERIC(12,2) AS total_net_holds
FROM users u
LEFT JOIN v_job_holds vh ON vh.client_id = u.id
GROUP BY u.id, u.wallet_credits_balance;
2) n8n workflow — Credit & Escrow endpoints (importable)
Exposes the endpoints used by Sections 1–2 (and later 5/6):

/wallet/purchase/record — post a purchase credit after Stripe confirms (called by Section-1 or your backend)

/credit-escrow/hold — initial hold (usually on accept)

/credit-escrow/topup — additional hold mid-job

/credit-escrow/on-approve — convert hold → charge and release the remainder

/credit-escrow/on-cancel — release any remaining hold

/wallet/admin/refund — credit refund (goodwill or policy outcome)

/wallet/admin/reversal — reversal entry to correct mistakes

Idempotency: all endpoints accept an idempotency_key.

Make sure your Postgres credential is named PureTask Postgres.

    { "parameters": { "operation":"executeQuery", "query":"WITH j AS (\n  SELECT id, client_id, final_charge_credits, held_credits FROM jobs WHERE id=:job_id\n), h AS (\n  SELECT COALESCE(net_held_credits,0) AS net_hold FROM v_job_holds WHERE job_id=:job_id\n), charge AS (\n  SELECT post_credit_tx((SELECT client_id FROM j), :job_id, 'charge', (SELECT final_charge_credits FROM j), 'final charge', 'charge:'||:job_id) AS txc\n), refund AS (\n  SELECT GREATEST((SELECT h.net_hold FROM h) - (SELECT j.final_charge_credits FROM j), 0) AS refund_amt\n), rel AS (\n  SELECT CASE WHEN (SELECT refund_amt FROM refund) > 0 THEN\n    post_credit_tx((SELECT client_id FROM j), :job_id, 'release', (SELECT refund_amt FROM refund), 'unused release', 'release:'||:job_id)\n  ELSE NULL END AS txr\n)\nUPDATE jobs SET refund_credits=(SELECT refund_amt FROM refund) WHERE id=:job_id;\nSELECT (SELECT net_hold FROM h) AS net_hold, (SELECT refund_amt FROM refund) AS refund_credits;",
