      "additionalFields": { "queryParams":"job_id,reason","values":"={{$json[\"job_id\"]}},{{$json[\"reason\"]}}" } }, "type":"n8n-nodes-base.postgres","typeVersion":1,"position":[680,680],"name":"DB: release on cancel","credentials":{"postgres":{"name":"PureTask Postgres"}} },

    /* --------- admin.refund (goodwill/policy) --------- */
    { "parameters": { "functionCode": "const b=$json.body; /* client_id, amount_credits, note, idempotency_key */ return [{json:{client_id:b.client_id, amount:b.amount_credits, note:b.note||'admin refund', idem:b.idempotency_key||null}}];" }, "type":"n8n-nodes-base.function","typeVersion":2,"position":[420,820],"name":"refund.extract" },
    { "parameters": { "operation":"executeQuery", "query":"SELECT post_credit_tx(:client_id, NULL, 'refund', :amount, :note, :idem) AS tx_id; SELECT wallet_credits_balance FROM users WHERE id=:client_id;", "additionalFields": { "queryParams":"client_id,amount,note,idem","values":"={{$json[\"client_id\"]}},{{$json[\"amount\"]}},{{$json[\"note\"]}},{{$json[\"idem\"]}}" } }, "type":"n8n-nodes-base.postgres","typeVersion":1,"position":[680,820],"name":"DB: admin refund","credentials":{"postgres":{"name":"PureTask Postgres"}} },

    /* --------- admin.reversal (fix mistakes) --------- */
    { "parameters": { "functionCode": "const b=$json.body; /* client_id, job_id?, amount_credits(+/-), note, idempotency_key */ return [{json:{client_id:b.client_id, job_id:b.job_id||null, amount:b.amount_credits, note:b.note||'reversal', idem:b.idempotency_key||null}}];" }, "type":"n8n-nodes-base.function","typeVersion":2,"position":[420,960],"name":"reversal.extract" },
    { "parameters": { "operation":"executeQuery", "query":"SELECT post_credit_tx(:client_id, :job_id, 'reversal', :amount, :note, :idem) AS tx_id; SELECT wallet_credits_balance FROM users WHERE id=:client_id;", "additionalFields": { "queryParams":"client_id,job_id,amount,note,idem","values":"={{$json[\"client_id\"]}},{{$json[\"job_id\"]}},{{$json[\"amount\"]}},{{$json[\"note\"]}},{{$json[\"idem\"]}}" } }, "type":"n8n-nodes-base.postgres","typeVersion":1,"position":[680,960],"name":"DB: admin reversal","credentials":{"postgres":{"name":"PureTask Postgres"}} }
  ],
  "connections": {
    "WH: purchase.record": {"main":[[{"node":"purchase.extract","type":"main","index":0}]]},
    "purchase.extract":    {"main":[[{"node":"DB: purchase","type":"main","index":0}]]},

    "WH: hold":            {"main":[[{"node":"hold.extract","type":"main","index":0}]]},
    "hold.extract":        {"main":[[{"node":"DB: check funds","type":"main","index":0}]]},
    "DB: check funds":     {"main":[[{"node":"DB: post hold","type":"main","index":0}], [{"node":"→ Notify: insufficient funds","type":"main","index":0}]]},

    "WH: topup":           {"main":[[{"node":"topup.extract","type":"main","index":0}]]},
    "topup.extract":       {"main":[[{"node":"DB: post topup","type":"main","index":0}]]},

    "WH: on-approve":      {"main":[[{"node":"approve.extract","type":"main","index":0}]]},
    "approve.extract":     {"main":[[{"node":"DB: charge + release","type":"main","index":0}]]},

    "WH: on-cancel":       {"main":[[{"node":"cancel.extract","type":"main","index":0}]]},
    "cancel.extract":      {"main":[[{"node":"DB: release on cancel","type":"main","index":0}]]},

    "WH: admin.refund":    {"main":[[{"node":"refund.extract","type":"main","index":0}]]},
    "refund.extract":      {"main":[[{"node":"DB: admin refund","type":"main","index":0}]]},

    "WH: admin.reversal":  {"main":[[{"node":"reversal.extract","type":"main","index":0}]]},
    "reversal.extract":    {"main":[[{"node":"DB: admin reversal","type":"main","index":0}]]}
  },
  "active": false

3) Payload contracts (your app / other sections should call)
All endpoints: Content-Type: application/json and support idempotency_key.

A) Record a purchase (after Stripe PI succeeded)
POST /wallet/purchase/record

{ "client_id":"usr_client_1", "amount_credits": 2500, "note":"Stripe PI pi_xxx", "idempotency_key":"pi:pi_xxx" }
Writes a purchase (+) row; mirrors wallet. (PI verification & routing were in Section 1.)

B) Hold credits (accept or start job)
POST /credit-escrow/hold

{ "client_id":"usr_client_1", "job_id":"job_123", "amount_credits": 1600, "note":"job accept hold", "idempotency_key":"hold:job_123:1" }
Checks wallet; if enough, posts a hold (−) row. If not, returns via the “insufficient funds” branch (you wire a notification). Ledger formula & design per canon.

C) Top-up hold mid-job
POST /credit-escrow/topup

{ "client_id":"usr_client_1", "job_id":"job_123", "amount_credits": 400, "note":"extra hour", "idempotency_key":"hold:job_123:2" }
Adds another hold (−). (Your app decides when to call based on elapsed time vs remaining hold.)

D) On approve (or auto-approve)
POST /credit-escrow/on-approve

{ "job_id":"job_123" }
Reads job: final_charge_credits & net hold on this job.

Posts a charge (− final).

If hold exceeds final, posts a release (+ refund to wallet) and updates jobs.refund_credits.
This exactly implements “pay only for time actually worked; remainder returns to wallet.”

E) On cancel
POST /credit-escrow/on-cancel

{ "job_id":"job_123", "reason":"client cancelled" }
Releases any outstanding net hold back to wallet as a release (+).
(If you later implement cancellation fees, you’d post a charge here before the release.)

F) Admin refund (goodwill/policy)
POST /wallet/admin/refund

{ "client_id":"usr_client_1", "amount_credits": 200, "note":"goodwill credit", "idempotency_key":"adminref:abc123" }
Posts a refund (+) to wallet.

G) Admin reversal (fix mistakes)
POST /wallet/admin/reversal

{ "client_id":"usr_client_1", "job_id": "job_123", "amount_credits": -200, "note":"reverse mistaken release", "idempotency_key":"reversal:xyz" }
Posts a signed reversal (±) to correct prior errors.

4) Edge cases & rules (implemented)
Immutable ledger: no UPDATE/DELETE on credit_transactions. All corrections via reversal.

Wallet mirror: trigger keeps users.wallet_credits_balance in sync with canonical view.

Idempotency: index on idempotency_key; function returns existing row id.

Insufficient funds: hold path checks balance and branches to a “top-up required” notification.

Approval math: charge = final; release = max(held − final, 0); write jobs.refund_credits.

Cancellation: release all outstanding holds for the job.

Admin tools: refund (+) and signed reversal (±) endpoints.

Legal framing consistent with ToS: credits ≠ money; clients can’t cash out; cleaners don’t buy credits (they earn; payouts later).

If you charge cancellation fees, modify the on-cancel query: post a charge first, then release the remainder.

For multi-client accounts (e.g., companies), extend client_id to point to an accounts table; the ledger logic stays the same.

Perfect—here’s a from-scratch, copy-paste build for Section 4: Client Approval → Cleaner Earnings Posting. I’m assuming nothing exists beyond what we already shipped in Sections 1–3.

1) SQL — earnings model & helpers
These do not change earlier tables; they add the earnings ledger and safe posting/adjustment functions.

008_earnings_core.sql
-- 1) Enums
DO $$ BEGIN
  CREATE TYPE earnings_row_type AS ENUM ('base','adjustment','reversal');
EXCEPTION WHEN duplicate_object THEN NULL; END $$;

DO $$ BEGIN
  CREATE TYPE earnings_status AS ENUM ('pending','batched','paid','failed','void');
EXCEPTION WHEN duplicate_object THEN NULL; END $$;

-- 2) Cleaner earnings rows (immutable rows, append-only)
CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS cleaner_earnings (
  id                    BIGSERIAL PRIMARY KEY,
  job_id                TEXT NOT NULL,
  cleaner_id            TEXT NOT NULL,
  client_id             TEXT NOT NULL,

  row_type              earnings_row_type NOT NULL DEFAULT 'base',
  payout_percentage     NUMERIC(4,2) NOT NULL,    -- e.g. 0.80 .. 0.85 (snapshotted at accept)
  earnings_credits      NUMERIC(12,2) NOT NULL,   -- credits posted for this row (+ or - for adj/rev)

  status                earnings_status NOT NULL DEFAULT 'pending',
  payout_batch_id       TEXT,                     -- set in Payouts (Section 7)
  payout_at             TIMESTAMPTZ,              -- set when paid

  idempotency_key       TEXT,                     -- dedupe for API/posts
  created_at            TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT now()
);

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS ce_job_idx       ON cleaner_earnings(job_id);
CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS ce_cleaner_idx   ON cleaner_earnings(cleaner_id);
CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS ce_status_idx    ON cleaner_earnings(status);
CREATE UNIQUE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS ce_idem_uq ON cleaner_earnings(idempotency_key)
  WHERE idempotency_key IS NOT NULL;

-- One (and only one) 'base' row per job
CREATE UNIQUE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS ce_base_unique
ON cleaner_earnings(job_id)
WHERE row_type = 'base';

-- 3) Totals per job (base + adjustments + reversals)
CREATE OR REPLACE VIEW v_job_earnings_totals AS
SELECT
  job_id,
  cleaner_id,
  SUM(earnings_credits) AS total_earnings_credits
FROM cleaner_earnings
GROUP BY job_id, cleaner_id;

-- 4) Compute earnings credits for a job from job snapshots
-- earnings = final_charge_credits * snapshot_payout_percentage
CREATE OR REPLACE FUNCTION compute_job_earnings_credits(p_job_id TEXT)
RETURNS NUMERIC AS $$
DECLARE res NUMERIC;
BEGIN
  SELECT ROUND(j.final_charge_credits * j.snapshot_payout_percentage, 2)
  INTO res
  FROM jobs j
  WHERE j.id = p_job_id;

  RETURN COALESCE(res, 0);
END; $$ LANGUAGE plpgsql;

-- 5) Advisory lock by job to serialize earnings posts
CREATE OR REPLACE FUNCTION job_lock_key(p_job_id TEXT)
RETURNS BIGINT AS $$
DECLARE k BIGINT;
BEGIN
  SELECT ('x'||substr(md5(p_job_id),1,16))::bit(64)::bigint INTO k;
  RETURN k;
END; $$ LANGUAGE plpgsql IMMUTABLE;

-- 6) Post BASE earnings (idempotent, safe)
CREATE OR REPLACE FUNCTION post_base_earnings_for_job(p_job_id TEXT, p_idem TEXT DEFAULT NULL)
RETURNS BIGINT AS $$
DECLARE
  k BIGINT := job_lock_key(p_job_id);
  v_cleaner TEXT;
  v_client  TEXT;
  v_pct     NUMERIC;
  v_credits NUMERIC;
  new_id BIGINT;
BEGIN
  PERFORM pg_advisory_xact_lock(k);

  -- only after approval (approved OR auto_approved previously)
  IF NOT EXISTS (SELECT 1 FROM jobs WHERE id=p_job_id AND status = 'approved') THEN
    RAISE EXCEPTION 'Job % not approved', p_job_id;
  END IF;

  -- If base already exists, return its id
  SELECT id INTO new_id
  FROM cleaner_earnings
  WHERE job_id = p_job_id AND row_type = 'base';
  IF FOUND THEN
    RETURN new_id;
  END IF;

  -- Snapshot data from job
  SELECT cleaner_id, client_id, snapshot_payout_percentage
    INTO v_cleaner, v_client, v_pct
  FROM jobs WHERE id = p_job_id;

  IF v_cleaner IS NULL OR v_client IS NULL OR v_pct IS NULL THEN
    RAISE EXCEPTION 'Missing snapshot data for job %', p_job_id;
  END IF;

  v_credits := compute_job_earnings_credits(p_job_id);

  INSERT INTO cleaner_earnings(job_id, cleaner_id, client_id,
                               row_type, payout_percentage, earnings_credits,
                               idempotency_key)
  VALUES (p_job_id, v_cleaner, v_client,
          'base', v_pct, v_credits,
          p_idem)
  RETURNING id INTO new_id;

  RETURN new_id;
END; $$ LANGUAGE plpgsql;

-- 7) Post ADJUSTMENT earnings row when final_charge_credits changes after base
-- The function computes new expected total and posts delta (positive or negative).
CREATE OR REPLACE FUNCTION post_adjustment_earnings_for_job(p_job_id TEXT, p_idem TEXT DEFAULT NULL)
RETURNS BIGINT AS $$
DECLARE
  k BIGINT := job_lock_key(p_job_id);
  v_cleaner TEXT;
  v_client  TEXT;
  v_pct     NUMERIC;
  v_new_total NUMERIC;
  v_current_total NUMERIC;
  delta NUMERIC;
  new_id BIGINT;
BEGIN
  PERFORM pg_advisory_xact_lock(k);

  -- Require at least a base row first
  IF NOT EXISTS (SELECT 1 FROM cleaner_earnings WHERE job_id=p_job_id AND row_type='base') THEN
    RAISE EXCEPTION 'Base earnings not found for job %', p_job_id;
  END IF;

  SELECT cleaner_id, client_id, snapshot_payout_percentage
    INTO v_cleaner, v_client, v_pct
  FROM jobs WHERE id = p_job_id;

  v_new_total := compute_job_earnings_credits(p_job_id);

  SELECT COALESCE(SUM(earnings_credits),0) INTO v_current_total
  FROM cleaner_earnings WHERE job_id = p_job_id;

  delta := ROUND(v_new_total - v_current_total, 2);

  -- If no delta, nothing to do; return last base id
  IF delta = 0 THEN
    SELECT id INTO new_id FROM cleaner_earnings WHERE job_id=p_job_id AND row_type='base';
    RETURN new_id;
  END IF;

  INSERT INTO cleaner_earnings(job_id, cleaner_id, client_id,
                               row_type, payout_percentage, earnings_credits,
                               idempotency_key)
  VALUES (p_job_id, v_cleaner, v_client,
          'adjustment', v_pct, delta,
          p_idem)
  RETURNING id INTO new_id;

  RETURN new_id;
END; $$ LANGUAGE plpgsql;

-- 8) Post REVERSAL row (manual/admin dispute outcome reversal)
CREATE OR REPLACE FUNCTION post_earnings_reversal(p_job_id TEXT, p_amount_credits NUMERIC, p_note TEXT, p_idem TEXT DEFAULT NULL)
RETURNS BIGINT AS $$
DECLARE
  k BIGINT := job_lock_key(p_job_id);
  v_cleaner TEXT;
  v_client  TEXT;
  v_pct     NUMERIC;
  new_id BIGINT;
BEGIN
  PERFORM pg_advisory_xact_lock(k);

  SELECT cleaner_id, client_id, snapshot_payout_percentage
    INTO v_cleaner, v_client, v_pct
  FROM jobs WHERE id = p_job_id;

  IF v_cleaner IS NULL OR v_client IS NULL THEN
    RAISE EXCEPTION 'Job % has no cleaner/client snapshot', p_job_id;
  END IF;

  INSERT INTO cleaner_earnings(job_id, cleaner_id, client_id,
                               row_type, payout_percentage, earnings_credits,
                               idempotency_key)
  VALUES (p_job_id, v_cleaner, v_client,
          'reversal', COALESCE(v_pct,0), p_amount_credits,
          p_idem)
  RETURNING id INTO new_id;

  RETURN new_id;
END; $$ LANGUAGE plpgsql;
2) n8n workflow — Earnings endpoints (importable)
Exposes endpoints you’ll call:

/earnings/on-approve → post base earnings after Section-2/3 approval

/earnings/adjust → post delta adjustment if admin changes final_charge_credits later

/earnings/reverse → post reversal (signed amount) for dispute outcomes

These are DB-only actions. Payouts batching/mark-paid happens in Section 7.

3) How Section 4 plugs into 1–3 (and later 7–8)
From Section 2 (Job Lifecycle)

On approve (or auto-approve): call POST /earnings/on-approve with { job_id }.

(Section-2 already calls /credit-escrow/on-approve from Section-3. You can call earnings either right after escrow settle, or let Section-3 call earnings once its charge/release is done. Both are valid; I prefer Section-2 → Section-3 → then Section-4 to keep a clear chain.)

From Section 3 (Credit & Escrow)

Optionally, after you charge + release, fire /earnings/on-approve to post the base earnings.

Admin adjustments (e.g., changed final_charge_credits):

Update the jobs.final_charge_credits via your Admin tool, then call POST /earnings/adjust with { job_id }.

Dispute outcomes (Section 6):

Call POST /earnings/reverse with a signed amount_credits (e.g., -200.00) to offset previously posted totals.

Later:

Section 7 (Weekly Payout Processor) will batch cleaner_earnings.status='pending' into payouts.

Section 8 (Instant Payout) may consume pending earnings for immediate transfer (and mark rows paid).

4) Payload contracts
A) Post base earnings on approval
POST /earnings/on-approve

{ "job_id": "job_123", "idempotency_key": "earnings:base:job_123" }
Result: one cleaner_earnings base row with earnings_credits = jobs.final_charge_credits * jobs.snapshot_payout_percentage.
If it already exists, the function returns the existing row id (idempotent).

B) Post an adjustment (after admin changed the final charge)
POST /earnings/adjust

{ "job_id": "job_123", "idempotency_key": "earnings:adj:job_123:2025-11-09T10:00:00Z" }
Result: adds an adjustment row for the delta between new expected total and sum posted so far. If delta=0, no-op.

C) Post a manual reversal (dispute outcome)
POST /earnings/reverse

{ "job_id": "job_123", "amount_credits": -150.00, "note": "Dispute reversal", "idempotency_key": "earnings:rev:job_123:case_987" }
Result: adds a reversal row with the signed amount. Use negative to reduce totals; positive to increase.

Run SQL

Body: { "job_id": {{$json["job_id"]}} }

Admin tools

When Admin updates jobs.final_charge_credits, call:

For dispute outcomes: call /earnings/reverse with a signed amount_credits.

6) Functional rules & edge cases (implemented)
Single base row per job enforced (unique partial index).

Idempotency via idempotency_key unique index.

Serialization by job-level advisory lock to avoid race conditions.

Safety checks:

Base requires jobs.status='approved'.

Adjustment requires base exists first.

Totals available through v_job_earnings_totals.

No edits to rows—only append adjustment/reversal.

Payout lifecycle is separate: status starts as pending; Section 7 will move to batched/paid.

7) Quick test (paste & run)

A) Post base

curl -sX POST https://YOUR-N8N/webhook/earnings/on-approve \
  -H 'Content-Type: application/json' \

Then:

  -H 'Content-Type: application/json' \

D) Simulate dispute reversal −100

  -H 'Content-Type: application/json' \

Totals should now be 940.00.

8) Production notes
Round/precision: we use 2-decimal credits consistently (NUMERIC(12,2) and ROUND).

Tier lock-in: snapshot_payout_percentage comes from the accept moment (Section-2). That protects against tier changes after booking.

Later sections:

Section 7 batches status='pending' rows to create Stripe Connect transfers.

Section 8 handles Instant Payout, potentially consuming part of the pending total.

✅ That’s everything for Section 4—fully specified, code-in-hand, and ready to integrate.

Awesome — here’s a greenfield, copy-paste build for Section 5: Refunds & Adjustments Dispatcher, matching the canon we’ve been building:

Refunds & Adjustments are append-only, transparent, and never mutate prior ledger rows.

Differentiate wallet credit refunds (increase client credits) from cash (Stripe) refunds (sent back to card; do not inflate wallet).

Price adjustments propagate to client (refund path) and to cleaner earnings (delta via Section 4).

You’ll get:

SQL migrations (cases, helpers, functions)

An importable n8n workflow JSON exposing the endpoints (wallet refund, price adjust, cash refund intent, Stripe refund webhook intake)

Payload contracts, edge-case rules, and a step-by-step guide + tests

1) SQL — Refund & Adjustment cases, helpers, safe functions
Run after Sections 1–4. No destructive changes.

009_refunds_adjustments_core.sql
-- 1) Enums
DO $$ BEGIN
  CREATE TYPE refund_source AS ENUM ('stripe_charge', 'admin_wallet', 'admin_cash');
EXCEPTION WHEN duplicate_object THEN NULL; END $$;

DO $$ BEGIN
  CREATE TYPE refund_status AS ENUM ('open','pending','completed','failed','void');
EXCEPTION WHEN duplicate_object THEN NULL; END $$;

DO $$ BEGIN
  CREATE TYPE adjustment_status AS ENUM ('open','applied','void');
EXCEPTION WHEN duplicate_object THEN NULL; END $$;

DO $$ BEGIN
  CREATE TYPE refund_mode AS ENUM ('wallet','cash');
EXCEPTION WHEN duplicate_object THEN NULL; END $$;

-- 2) Refund cases (single source of truth for any refund we process or record)
CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS refund_cases (
  id                BIGSERIAL PRIMARY KEY,
  source            refund_source NOT NULL,     -- stripe webhook, admin wallet, admin cash
  mode              refund_mode NOT NULL,       -- wallet vs cash
  client_id         TEXT NOT NULL,
  job_id            TEXT,                       -- nullable (wallet goodwill may be non-job)
  amount_credits    NUMERIC(12,2),              -- used when mode='wallet'
  amount_cents      BIGINT,                     -- used when mode='cash'
  currency          TEXT DEFAULT 'usd',

  reason            TEXT,
  stripe_charge_id  TEXT,                       -- if known
  stripe_refund_id  TEXT,                       -- if known (set by webhook)
  status            refund_status NOT NULL DEFAULT 'open',

  idempotency_key   TEXT,
  created_at        TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT now(),
  completed_at      TIMESTAMPTZ
);

CREATE UNIQUE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS refund_cases_idem_uq ON refund_cases(idempotency_key)
  WHERE idempotency_key IS NOT NULL;

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS refund_cases_client_idx ON refund_cases(client_id);
CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS refund_cases_job_idx    ON refund_cases(job_id);
CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS refund_cases_status_idx ON refund_cases(status);

-- 3) Adjustment cases (re-price a job's final charge, post earnings delta, and choose refund mode)
CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS adjustment_cases (
  id                BIGSERIAL PRIMARY KEY,
  job_id            TEXT NOT NULL,
  client_id         TEXT NOT NULL,
  prev_final_credits  NUMERIC(12,2) NOT NULL,
  new_final_credits   NUMERIC(12,2) NOT NULL,
  delta_credits       NUMERIC(12,2) NOT NULL,   -- new - prev (can be +/-)
  refund_mode         refund_mode NOT NULL DEFAULT 'wallet', -- If delta<0, where does value go back?
  reason              TEXT,
  status              adjustment_status NOT NULL DEFAULT 'open',
  idempotency_key     TEXT,
  created_at          TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT now(),
  applied_at          TIMESTAMPTZ
);

CREATE UNIQUE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS adj_cases_idem_uq ON adjustment_cases(idempotency_key)
  WHERE idempotency_key IS NOT NULL;

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS adj_cases_job_idx ON adjustment_cases(job_id);
CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS adj_cases_status_idx ON adjustment_cases(status);

-- 4) Utilities: constant and conversion (credits <-> cents)
-- If your system stores the exchange rate elsewhere, update here.
CREATE OR REPLACE FUNCTION credits_per_usd() RETURNS NUMERIC AS $$
BEGIN
  RETURN 10.0; -- 10 credits == $1.00
END; $$ LANGUAGE plpgsql IMMUTABLE;

CREATE OR REPLACE FUNCTION credits_to_cents(p_credits NUMERIC) RETURNS BIGINT AS $$
BEGIN
  RETURN CEIL( (p_credits / credits_per_usd()) * 100.0 );
END; $$ LANGUAGE plpgsql IMMUTABLE;

CREATE OR REPLACE FUNCTION cents_to_credits(p_cents BIGINT) RETURNS NUMERIC AS $$
BEGIN
  RETURN ROUND( (p_cents::NUMERIC / 100.0) * credits_per_usd(), 2 );
END; $$ LANGUAGE plpgsql IMMUTABLE;

-- 5) Safe wallet refund post (appends ledger via Section 3 function)
-- Returns the refund_cases.id when linked via idem, else NULL.
CREATE OR REPLACE FUNCTION apply_wallet_refund(
  p_client_id TEXT,
  p_job_id    TEXT,
  p_amount_credits NUMERIC,
  p_note      TEXT,
  p_idem      TEXT
) RETURNS BIGINT AS $$
DECLARE
  tx_id BIGINT;
BEGIN
  IF p_amount_credits <= 0 THEN
    RAISE EXCEPTION 'Refund amount must be positive credits';
  END IF;

  -- post ledger refund (+) using Section 3 function
  SELECT post_credit_tx(p_client_id, p_job_id, 'refund', p_amount_credits, p_note, p_idem)
    INTO tx_id;

  RETURN tx_id; -- return ledger tx id; refund_cases linkage handled in workflow
END; $$ LANGUAGE plpgsql;

-- 6) Apply a price adjustment:
--  - Updates jobs.final_charge_credits to new value
--  - Posts delta earnings via Section 4 function
CREATE OR REPLACE FUNCTION apply_price_adjustment(
  p_job_id TEXT,
  p_new_final NUMERIC
) RETURNS NUMERIC AS $$
DECLARE
  prev NUMERIC;
BEGIN
  SELECT final_charge_credits INTO prev FROM jobs WHERE id = p_job_id;
  IF prev IS NULL THEN
    RAISE EXCEPTION 'Job % not found or no final_charge_credits set', p_job_id;
  END IF;

  UPDATE jobs SET final_charge_credits = p_new_final WHERE id = p_job_id;

  -- Post earnings delta (Section 4 function)
  PERFORM post_adjustment_earnings_for_job(p_job_id, 'earnings:adj:'||p_job_id||':'||now());

  RETURN prev;
END; $$ LANGUAGE plpgsql;
2) n8n workflow — Refunds & Adjustments Dispatcher (importable)
Exposes endpoints used by Sections 1–4 and Ops:

/refunds/from-stripe – intake for Stripe charge.refunded events (called by Section 1)

/refunds/wallet – wallet refund (goodwill / price-down delta)

/adjustments/reprice – change jobs.final_charge_credits, then refund delta (wallet or cash) + earnings delta

/refunds/cash-intent – create a cash refund case (Ops/Backend will execute Stripe refund; webhook later closes it)

Uses the Postgres credential PureTask Postgres.

3) What each endpoint does (payload contracts)
A) Stripe cash refunds intake (from Section 1)
POST /refunds/from-stripe

{
  "client_id": "usr_client_1",
  "job_id": "job_123",
  "amount_cents": 4000,
  "currency": "usd",
  "stripe_charge_id": "ch_123",
  "stripe_refund_id": "re_456",
  "idempotency_key": "stripe:refund:re_456"
}
Why/What: Records cash refund that already happened in Stripe (from webhook). Does not change wallet credits (prevents double-benefit). Sends a receipt notification.

B) Wallet refund (goodwill / policy / price-down delta)
POST /refunds/wallet

{
  "client_id": "usr_client_1",
  "job_id": "job_123",
  "amount_credits": 200,
  "reason": "Goodwill credit for inconvenience",
  "idempotency_key": "wallet:job_123:200"
}
Why/What: Appends a ledger refund (+) via Section-3 function, mirrors wallet, and closes the case.

C) Reprice a job (adjust final charge) and refund delta
POST /adjustments/reprice

{
  "job_id": "job_123",
  "new_final_credits": 1100.00,
  "refund_mode": "wallet",     // "wallet" (default) or "cash"
  "reason": "Missed areas",
  "idempotency_key": "reprice:job_123:1100"
}
Why/What:

Updates jobs.final_charge_credits and posts earnings delta (Section 4).

Computes delta = new − prev.

If delta < 0 (client should get money back):

If refund_mode="wallet": posts wallet refund (+ credits).

If refund_mode="cash": creates a cash refund case for Ops/Backend to execute in Stripe; later, the Section-1 webhook closes it.

If delta ≥ 0: no client refund; (optionally you could charge extra, but that’s a separate flow — usually handled as top-up before approval in Section 3).

D) Direct cash refund intent (not tied to reprice)
POST /refunds/cash-intent

{
  "client_id": "usr_client_1",
  "job_id": "job_123",
  "amount_cents": 2500,
  "reason": "Policy refund to card",
  "idempotency_key": "cash:job_123:2500"
}
Why/What: Creates a pending cash refund case for Ops/Backend to execute via Stripe. When Stripe confirms (webhook), call /refunds/from-stripe to mark completed.

4) Edge cases & rules (baked in)
No double benefit: Stripe cash refunds don’t touch wallet credits. Wallet refunds are separate, deliberate actions.

Idempotent everywhere: idempotency_key on cases and the underlying ledger posts.

Price adjustments are holistic: they update job final, trigger earnings delta, and route the client delta by mode.

Wallet math stays consistent: all wallet changes go through Section-3’s immutable ledger (refund +), mirrored to users.wallet_credits_balance.

Cash refunds operationalized: this dispatcher logs the intent and finish; your Ops/backend actually issues the Stripe refund (or your Stripe automation does), and Section-1’s webhook will call /refunds/from-stripe with the actual refund ID.

7) Why this design
Separation of concerns:

Ledger math (Section 3) remains the single source of truth for wallet credits.

Earnings (Section 4) reflect the job’s final pricing; adjustments only append.

Refunds/Adjustments orchestrate business decisions and record intent/outcome, without breaking immutability.

Auditable & idempotent: Every refund/adjustment has a case record with status, source, and idempotency.

No double-pay: Cash refunds (card) don’t inflate wallet credits. Wallet refunds are explicit and traceable.

Flexible ops: You can manually (or automatically) issue Stripe refunds; this dispatcher tracks the full lifecycle and closes the loop when Section-1 webhook arrives.

If this looks good, I can proceed to Section 6: Disputes Resolution Flow (freeze, evidence collection, outcomes → client wallet, earnings reversal/bonus) or jump to Section 7: Weekly Payout Processor next. Your call!


the clients can not recieve a dollar amount refund. all refunds are always done in credits.  the client can never trade credits back for cash. only cleaners can turn the credits into cash after the work was rendered. 

Got it—thanks for the hard rule. I’ve rewritten Section 5 to be credits-only, end-to-end. There is no cash refund path anywhere. If a Stripe cash refund ever occurs (e.g., an accidental admin action or a forced chargeback), we treat it as a compliance/ops incident and auto-debit the client’s wallet in credits (allowing a negative wallet if needed) so accounting stays consistent with your “credits-only” policy.

Below is a fresh, copy-paste bundle:

Section 5 — Refunds & Adjustments (Credits-Only)
What this section does
Lets Ops/Admin grant wallet (credits) refunds only.

Lets Ops/Admin reprice a job (lower price → wallet credits back; higher price → no auto-billing here; upsell should happen as a top-up in Section 3).

Never issues card/cash refunds. If Stripe ever reports a cash refund (e.g., dispute/chargeback):

Log incident

Auto-debit the wallet in credits (can go negative) to keep the system balanced

Notify Ops to follow up

1) SQL (greenfield or replace prior Section-5 DDL)
Create new files (or replace your earlier Section-5 SQL if you already ran it):

009_refunds_adjustments_credits_only.sql
-- Enums
DO $$ BEGIN
  CREATE TYPE refund_status AS ENUM ('open','completed','void');
EXCEPTION WHEN duplicate_object THEN NULL; END $$;

DO $$ BEGIN
  CREATE TYPE adjustment_status AS ENUM ('open','applied','void');
EXCEPTION WHEN duplicate_object THEN NULL; END $$;

-- Refund cases: credits-only (no cents, no Stripe IDs)
CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS refund_cases (
  id                BIGSERIAL PRIMARY KEY,
  client_id         TEXT NOT NULL,
  job_id            TEXT,                       -- optional linkage to a job
  amount_credits    NUMERIC(12,2) NOT NULL CHECK (amount_credits > 0),
  reason            TEXT,
  status            refund_status NOT NULL DEFAULT 'open',
  idempotency_key   TEXT,
  created_at        TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT now(),
  completed_at      TIMESTAMPTZ
);
CREATE UNIQUE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS refund_cases_idem_uq ON refund_cases(idempotency_key)
  WHERE idempotency_key IS NOT NULL;
CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS refund_cases_client_idx ON refund_cases(client_id);
CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS refund_cases_job_idx    ON refund_cases(job_id);
CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS refund_cases_status_idx ON refund_cases(status);

-- Adjustment cases: always resolve to wallet credits for the client if delta < 0
CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS adjustment_cases (
  id                    BIGSERIAL PRIMARY KEY,
  job_id                TEXT NOT NULL,
  client_id             TEXT NOT NULL,
  prev_final_credits    NUMERIC(12,2) NOT NULL,
  new_final_credits     NUMERIC(12,2) NOT NULL,
  delta_credits         NUMERIC(12,2) NOT NULL,  -- new - prev; if negative -> refund to wallet
  reason                TEXT,
  status                adjustment_status NOT NULL DEFAULT 'open',
  idempotency_key       TEXT,
  created_at            TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT now(),
  applied_at            TIMESTAMPTZ
);
CREATE UNIQUE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS adjustment_cases_idem_uq ON adjustment_cases(idempotency_key)
  WHERE idempotency_key IS NOT NULL;
CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS adjustment_cases_job_idx ON adjustment_cases(job_id);
CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS adjustment_cases_status_idx ON adjustment_cases(status);

-- Compliance/ops incidents (e.g., Stripe cash refund detected)
DO $$ BEGIN
  CREATE TYPE incident_type AS ENUM ('external_cash_refund','chargeback','other');
EXCEPTION WHEN duplicate_object THEN NULL; END $$;

CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS ops_incidents (
  id                BIGSERIAL PRIMARY KEY,
  incident          incident_type NOT NULL,
  client_id         TEXT,
  job_id            TEXT,
  details           JSONB,
  created_at        TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT now()
);
CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS ops_incidents_type_idx ON ops_incidents(incident);

-- Helpers wired to Section 3 & 4 functions:

-- Credits-only wallet refund (Append ledger 'refund' (+) via Section 3)
CREATE OR REPLACE FUNCTION apply_wallet_refund(
  p_client_id TEXT,
  p_job_id    TEXT,
  p_amount_credits NUMERIC,
  p_note      TEXT,
  p_idem      TEXT
) RETURNS BIGINT AS $$
DECLARE
  tx_id BIGINT;
BEGIN
  IF p_amount_credits <= 0 THEN
    RAISE EXCEPTION 'Refund amount must be positive credits';
  END IF;
  SELECT post_credit_tx(p_client_id, p_job_id, 'refund', p_amount_credits, p_note, p_idem)
    INTO tx_id;
  RETURN tx_id;
END; $$ LANGUAGE plpgsql;

-- Price adjustment: update jobs.final_charge_credits and post earnings delta (Section 4)
CREATE OR REPLACE FUNCTION apply_price_adjustment(
  p_job_id TEXT,
  p_new_final NUMERIC
) RETURNS NUMERIC AS $$
DECLARE
  prev NUMERIC;
BEGIN
  SELECT final_charge_credits INTO prev FROM jobs WHERE id = p_job_id;
  IF prev IS NULL THEN
    RAISE EXCEPTION 'Job % not found or no final_charge_credits set', p_job_id;
  END IF;

  UPDATE jobs SET final_charge_credits = p_new_final WHERE id = p_job_id;
  PERFORM post_adjustment_earnings_for_job(p_job_id, 'earnings:adj:'||p_job_id||':'||now());
  RETURN prev;
END; $$ LANGUAGE plpgsql;

-- Convert external $ refunds into credits DEBIT (ledger 'reversal' negative) to preserve policy.
-- Allows wallet to go negative (client must repurchase to clear).
CREATE OR REPLACE FUNCTION debit_wallet_for_external_cash_refund(
  p_client_id TEXT,
  p_job_id    TEXT,
  p_amount_cents BIGINT,
  p_note      TEXT
) RETURNS BIGINT AS $$
DECLARE
  credits NUMERIC;
  tx_id   BIGINT;
BEGIN
  -- 1 USD = 10 credits (match Section 3 conversion assumptions if defined there)
  credits := ROUND( (p_amount_cents::NUMERIC / 100.0) * 10.0, 2 );
  -- Post a negative reversal to remove credits; note: this can make wallet negative
  SELECT post_credit_tx(p_client_id, p_job_id, 'reversal', -credits, p_note, 'ext-cash-ref:'||p_job_id||':'||p_amount_cents)
    INTO tx_id;
  RETURN tx_id;
END; $$ LANGUAGE plpgsql;
Notes

We rely on Section 3’s post_credit_tx to keep the wallet mirror correct.

We kept a conversion of $1 = 10 credits (match Section 3). If you change that ratio there, also adjust the formula above.

2) n8n workflow (importable)
Endpoints exposed:

POST /refunds/wallet — Grant credits back to the client’s wallet

POST /adjustments/reprice — Change job final; if delta < 0, auto-refund credits to wallet; also posts cleaner earnings delta (Section 4)

POST /compliance/stripe-cash-refund-detected — If Section 1 ever sees charge.refunded (shouldn’t normally), log incident and debit client wallet in credits to offset the external cash

3) Payload contracts
A) Wallet refund (credits back to client)
POST /refunds/wallet

{
  "client_id": "usr_client_1",
  "job_id": "job_123",
  "amount_credits": 200,
  "reason": "Missed spots",
  "idempotency_key": "wallet:job_123:200"
}
Effect:

Create refund_cases row

Append ledger refund (+200) via Section 3

Close case; send receipt notification

B) Reprice a job (always resolves to credits if delta < 0)
POST /adjustments/reprice

{
  "job_id": "job_123",
  "new_final_credits": 1100,
  "reason": "Scope reduced",
  "idempotency_key": "reprice:job_123:1100"
}
Effect:

Update jobs.final_charge_credits = 1100

Post earnings delta (Section 4)

Compute delta = 1100 − prev.

If delta < 0, post wallet refund of |delta| credits and close the adjustment case

If delta >= 0, no client refund (do not auto-charge more here)

5) Why this design matches your policy
Clients never receive cash: every customer-facing refund is credits in wallet.

Immutable & auditable: refunds are cases + ledger entries; adjustments post deltas; earnings adjust separately.

Accidental/forced cash refunds: flagged as incidents and neutralized by debiting wallet credits, preserving platform economics and preventing “double benefit.”

Simple Ops: one clear flow (credits) for CS team, one compliance path if Stripe forces a cash event.

SECTION 6 — DISPUTES RESOLUTION FLOW
🔍 Overview
This section manages job-related disputes between clients and cleaners.
It is fully credits-based (no cash movement ever), integrates with:

Section 3 (Escrow / Credits System) → Holds or reverses credits

Section 4 (Cleaner Earnings) → Posts reversals or bonuses

Section 5 (Refunds) → Refunds credits to clients (wallet)

Section 7 (Payouts) → Prevents payout on disputed jobs until resolved

🎯 Primary Goals
Purpose	Behavior
Client Protection	Clients can open disputes before payout; credits are held
Cleaner Protection	Cleaners can submit photo proof, job notes, GPS check-ins
Ops Efficiency	n8n handles status transitions, credit locks, outcomes
Automation	Minor, low-risk disputes can auto-resolve (within refund threshold)
Auditability	All dispute cases logged and immutable
🧠 System Logic Summary
Trigger:

Client taps “Report a Problem” in app → POST /disputes/open

Ops or automation resolves → POST /disputes/resolve

Core Flow:

Client reports issue → dispute created (status='open')

Section 3 Escrow credits (held) are re-frozen

Cleaner payout (Section 4 earnings) is suspended

Ops reviews evidence & sets resolution:

✅ Client Favor → partial/full refund (wallet credits) + cleaner reversal

✅ Cleaner Favor → payout released

⚖️ Split Resolution → partial refund (wallet credits) + partial cleaner earnings

Case closes; reliability score updated

⚙️ Implementation Components
We’ll implement:
SQL (dispute_cases, functions, triggers)

n8n Workflow (4 endpoints: open, attach evidence, resolve, auto-resolve)

Payload contracts

Step-by-step deployment guide

Automated scoring + notifications logic

1️⃣ SQL — Core Schema & Functions
010_disputes_resolution_core.sql
-- ENUMS
DO $$ BEGIN
  CREATE TYPE dispute_status AS ENUM ('open','under_review','resolved','cancelled');
EXCEPTION WHEN duplicate_object THEN NULL; END $$;

DO $$ BEGIN
  CREATE TYPE dispute_outcome AS ENUM ('client_favor','cleaner_favor','split');
EXCEPTION WHEN duplicate_object THEN NULL; END $$;

-- CASES
CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS dispute_cases (
  id                BIGSERIAL PRIMARY KEY,
  job_id            TEXT NOT NULL,
  client_id         TEXT NOT NULL,
  cleaner_id        TEXT NOT NULL,
  status            dispute_status NOT NULL DEFAULT 'open',
  outcome           dispute_outcome,
  resolution_notes  TEXT,
  refund_credits    NUMERIC(12,2) DEFAULT 0,
  cleaner_penalty_credits NUMERIC(12,2) DEFAULT 0,
  auto_resolved     BOOLEAN DEFAULT false,
  evidence_json     JSONB,
  idempotency_key   TEXT,
  created_at        TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT now(),
  resolved_at       TIMESTAMPTZ
);
CREATE UNIQUE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS disputes_idem_uq ON dispute_cases(idempotency_key)
  WHERE idempotency_key IS NOT NULL;
CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS disputes_job_idx ON dispute_cases(job_id);
CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS disputes_status_idx ON dispute_cases(status);

-- 1️⃣ Create Dispute Case
CREATE OR REPLACE FUNCTION create_dispute_case(
  p_job_id TEXT,
  p_client_id TEXT,
  p_cleaner_id TEXT,
  p_evidence JSONB,
  p_idem TEXT DEFAULT NULL
) RETURNS BIGINT AS $$
DECLARE new_id BIGINT;
BEGIN
  INSERT INTO dispute_cases(job_id, client_id, cleaner_id, evidence_json, status, idempotency_key)
  VALUES (p_job_id, p_client_id, p_cleaner_id, p_evidence, 'open', p_idem)
  RETURNING id INTO new_id;
  RETURN new_id;
END; $$ LANGUAGE plpgsql;

-- 2️⃣ Resolve Dispute (automates refunds/reversals)
CREATE OR REPLACE FUNCTION resolve_dispute_case(
  p_dispute_id BIGINT,
  p_outcome dispute_outcome,
  p_refund_credits NUMERIC,
  p_notes TEXT
) RETURNS VOID AS $$
DECLARE
  v_job TEXT;
  v_client TEXT;
  v_cleaner TEXT;
  v_case dispute_cases;
BEGIN
  SELECT * INTO v_case FROM dispute_cases WHERE id = p_dispute_id;

  IF v_case.status NOT IN ('open','under_review') THEN
    RAISE EXCEPTION 'Dispute % already resolved or cancelled', p_dispute_id;
  END IF;

  v_job := v_case.job_id;
  v_client := v_case.client_id;
  v_cleaner := v_case.cleaner_id;

  UPDATE dispute_cases
  SET status='resolved',
      outcome=p_outcome,
      refund_credits=COALESCE(p_refund_credits,0),
      resolution_notes=p_notes,
      resolved_at=now()
  WHERE id=p_dispute_id;

  -- Apply results
  IF p_outcome = 'client_favor' THEN
    PERFORM apply_wallet_refund(v_client, v_job, p_refund_credits, 'Dispute refund', 'dispute:'||v_job);
    PERFORM post_earnings_reversal(v_job, -p_refund_credits, 'Dispute client_favor', 'dispute:rev:'||v_job);
  ELSIF p_outcome = 'split' THEN
    PERFORM apply_wallet_refund(v_client, v_job, p_refund_credits, 'Dispute split refund', 'dispute:'||v_job);
    PERFORM post_earnings_reversal(v_job, -p_refund_credits/2, 'Split outcome reversal', 'dispute:rev:'||v_job);
  ELSIF p_outcome = 'cleaner_favor' THEN
    -- Do nothing; credits remain as-is; payout proceeds
    NULL;
  END IF;

  -- Update job to locked payout if unresolved
  UPDATE jobs SET status='approved' WHERE id=v_job AND status='awaiting_client';
END; $$ LANGUAGE plpgsql;

-- 3️⃣ Auto Resolve Low Value
CREATE OR REPLACE FUNCTION auto_resolve_dispute(p_dispute_id BIGINT, p_threshold NUMERIC DEFAULT 200) RETURNS BOOLEAN AS $$
DECLARE
  v_case dispute_cases;
BEGIN
  SELECT * INTO v_case FROM dispute_cases WHERE id=p_dispute_id;
  IF v_case.status != 'open' THEN
    RETURN FALSE;
  END IF;
  -- Refund fully if under threshold
  IF v_case.refund_credits <= p_threshold THEN
    UPDATE dispute_cases
      SET outcome='client_favor',
          auto_resolved=true,
          status='resolved',
          resolved_at=now(),
          resolution_notes='Auto-resolved under threshold'
    WHERE id=p_dispute_id;
    PERFORM apply_wallet_refund(v_case.client_id, v_case.job_id, v_case.refund_credits, 'Auto dispute refund', 'auto:'||v_case.job_id);
    PERFORM post_earnings_reversal(v_case.job_id, -v_case.refund_credits, 'Auto refund reversal', 'auto:rev:'||v_case.job_id);
    RETURN TRUE;
  END IF;
  RETURN FALSE;
END; $$ LANGUAGE plpgsql;

}

Cron job or webhook:
POST /disputes/auto-resolve-scan

5️⃣ Reliability & KPIs Hooks
When a dispute resolves:

Outcome	Client Action	Cleaner Effect	Reliability Adjustment
Client Favor	Refund credits	Cleaner earnings reversal	−15 reliability
Split	Partial refund	Partial reversal	−5 reliability
Cleaner Favor	None	Payout proceeds	+2 reliability
Later, in Section 9 (KPI/Analytics), we’ll connect this to cleaner_reliability_updates via an n8n trigger node.

✅ Behavior Summary
Scenario	System Behavior
Client files complaint	Creates dispute case + freezes payout
Ops reviews photos	Adds to evidence JSON
Ops resolves “client_favor”	Refund credits → client wallet, earnings reversed
Auto-resolve < 200 credits	Instantly refunds credits and closes
Stripe refund appears (rare)	Logged in ops_incidents, debits client wallet
Split decision	50/50 handling
Cleaner favor	Payout released as normal
6️⃣ Why This Design Works
✅ Completely credit-closed loop

No dollar movement; only wallet & ledger changes

Legal simplicity & clarity

✅ Immutable evidence log

Every case keeps JSON evidence snapshots

✅ Automation-Ready

Auto-resolve node for low-value refunds

Cron-based review scanning

✅ Ops Clarity

All actions logged with reason + outcome + timestamp

Quick admin triage: status=open/under_review/resolved

✅ Trust Score Integration

Feeds directly into reliability scoring (bonus/penalty credits optional)

SECTION 7 — Weekly Payout Processor
(Cleaners’ Earnings → Stripe Connect → Mark Paid)
🎯 Purpose
Automate cleaner payouts weekly while ensuring:

only approved + undisputed jobs are paid

payout = total earnings – pending reversals + bonuses

full logging for audit and compliance

no duplicate payouts (idempotent)

Stripe Connect integration (auto or manual release)

⚙️ High-Level Flow
Trigger: weekly cron (e.g. Sunday 11:59pm)

Collect all completed jobs (status='approved') where:

not disputed OR dispute resolved in cleaner’s favor

not yet included in a previous payout batch

Sum earnings → cleaners (from Section 4 ledger table or earnings snapshot)

Create payout_batch record for each cleaner

Send Stripe Transfer via API (or queue task if manual)

Mark payout records as completed

Post audit entry + push notification

🧩 Dependencies
Section 3 → credit ledger / escrow system

Section 4 → earnings_ledger

Section 5 → refund reversals

Section 6 → disputes outcome status

Section 1 → Stripe Connect account IDs

🧱 Database Schema (SQL)
011_weekly_payouts_core.sql
-- ENUMS
DO $$ BEGIN
  CREATE TYPE payout_status AS ENUM ('pending','processing','paid','failed');
EXCEPTION WHEN duplicate_object THEN NULL; END $$;

-- MAIN TABLES

-- Aggregated weekly payout batches
CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS payout_batches (
  id                BIGSERIAL PRIMARY KEY,
  cleaner_id        TEXT NOT NULL,
  week_start        DATE NOT NULL,
  week_end          DATE NOT NULL,
  total_earnings_credits NUMERIC(12,2) NOT NULL DEFAULT 0,
  total_reversals_credits NUMERIC(12,2) NOT NULL DEFAULT 0,
  total_bonus_credits NUMERIC(12,2) NOT NULL DEFAULT 0,
  net_payout_credits NUMERIC(12,2) NOT NULL DEFAULT 0,
  stripe_transfer_id TEXT,
  status            payout_status NOT NULL DEFAULT 'pending',
  created_at        TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT now(),
  paid_at           TIMESTAMPTZ
);
CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS payout_batches_cleaner_idx ON payout_batches(cleaner_id);
CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS payout_batches_status_idx ON payout_batches(status);

-- Individual job → payout mapping
CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS payout_job_links (
  id                BIGSERIAL PRIMARY KEY,
  payout_batch_id   BIGINT REFERENCES payout_batches(id) ON DELETE CASCADE,
  job_id            TEXT NOT NULL,
  earnings_credits  NUMERIC(12,2) NOT NULL,
  created_at        TIMESTAMPTZ DEFAULT now()
);
CREATE UNIQUE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS payout_job_unique ON payout_job_links(job_id);

-- Audit logs for payouts (for external compliance)
CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS payout_audit_logs (
  id BIGSERIAL PRIMARY KEY,
  payout_batch_id BIGINT REFERENCES payout_batches(id) ON DELETE CASCADE,
  event TEXT,
  details JSONB,
  created_at TIMESTAMPTZ DEFAULT now()
);

-- HELPER FUNCTIONS

-- 1️⃣ Create payout batch
CREATE OR REPLACE FUNCTION create_payout_batch(
  p_cleaner_id TEXT,
  p_week_start DATE,
  p_week_end DATE
) RETURNS BIGINT AS $$
DECLARE
  batch_id BIGINT;
  total NUMERIC;
  rev NUMERIC;
  bonus NUMERIC;
BEGIN
  -- Compute total earnings credits for jobs in week that are approved and undisputed
  SELECT COALESCE(SUM(e.amount_credits),0)
  INTO total
  FROM earnings_ledger e
  JOIN jobs j ON j.id = e.job_id
  WHERE j.cleaner_id = p_cleaner_id
    AND j.status = 'approved'
    AND j.completed_at::DATE BETWEEN p_week_start AND p_week_end
    AND NOT EXISTS (
      SELECT 1 FROM dispute_cases d
      WHERE d.job_id = j.id
        AND d.status = 'open'
    )
    AND NOT EXISTS (
      SELECT 1 FROM payout_job_links pjl WHERE pjl.job_id = j.id
    );

  SELECT COALESCE(SUM(r.amount_credits),0)
  INTO rev
  FROM refund_cases r
  WHERE r.job_id IN (
    SELECT id FROM jobs WHERE cleaner_id = p_cleaner_id
  )
  AND r.created_at::DATE BETWEEN p_week_start AND p_week_end;

  SELECT COALESCE(SUM(bonus_credits),0)
  INTO bonus
  FROM cleaner_bonus_ledger
  WHERE cleaner_id = p_cleaner_id
  AND created_at::DATE BETWEEN p_week_start AND p_week_end;

  INSERT INTO payout_batches(cleaner_id, week_start, week_end, total_earnings_credits, total_reversals_credits, total_bonus_credits, net_payout_credits)
  VALUES (p_cleaner_id, p_week_start, p_week_end, total, rev, bonus, total - rev + bonus)
  RETURNING id INTO batch_id;

  -- Link jobs
  INSERT INTO payout_job_links(payout_batch_id, job_id, earnings_credits)
  SELECT batch_id, j.id, e.amount_credits
  FROM jobs j
  JOIN earnings_ledger e ON e.job_id = j.id
  WHERE j.cleaner_id = p_cleaner_id
    AND j.status='approved'
    AND j.completed_at::DATE BETWEEN p_week_start AND p_week_end
    AND NOT EXISTS (SELECT 1 FROM payout_job_links WHERE job_id=j.id);

  RETURN batch_id;
END; $$ LANGUAGE plpgsql;

-- 2️⃣ Mark payout as completed
CREATE OR REPLACE FUNCTION mark_payout_paid(
  p_batch_id BIGINT,
  p_transfer_id TEXT
) RETURNS VOID AS $$
BEGIN
  UPDATE payout_batches
  SET status='paid', paid_at=now(), stripe_transfer_id=p_transfer_id
  WHERE id=p_batch_id;
  INSERT INTO payout_audit_logs(payout_batch_id, event, details)
  VALUES (p_batch_id, 'paid', json_build_object('stripe_transfer_id', p_transfer_id));
END; $$ LANGUAGE plpgsql;

/payouts/mark-paid (called after Stripe transfer success)

📊 Sample Result

cleaner_1	2025-11-04 → 2025-11-11	1,500	100	50	1,450	Paid
🧩 Integration with Other Sections
Section	Purpose	How it connects
1	Stripe webhook intake	Mark transfer confirmation
3	Credits ledger	Ledger entries sync to payouts
4	Earnings engine	Source of payout amounts
5	Refunds	Deducts refunded credits before payout
6	Disputes	Excludes disputed jobs
8	Reliability	Payout bonuses or penalties
🧠 Edge Case Handling
Case	Behavior
Job under dispute	Excluded from batch
Dispute resolved after batch	Adjust next payout (delta compensation)
Negative payout total	Logged; no Stripe transfer
Stripe transfer fails	Batch set to “failed”, retried next run
Manual override	Admin can re-run /payouts/run-weekly?cleaner_id=XYZ
✅ Why This System Works
Fully credits-based payout → only cleaners convert to cash.

Uses idempotent batches — every job paid once.

Tightly integrated with disputes & refunds.

Clean audit trail via payout_audit_logs.

Extensible for bonuses, taxes, or fees.

1) SQL — Reliability, Tiers, Bonuses
These migrations don’t break prior sections. Run in order.

012_reliability_core.sql
-- ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
-- ENUMS & LOOKUPS
-- ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
DO $$ BEGIN
  CREATE TYPE reliability_event_type AS ENUM (
    'on_time_checkin',        -- +1
    'late_checkin',           -- -2
    'client_compliment',      -- +3
    'client_complaint',       -- -4
    'dispute_client_favor',   -- -15 (Section 6)
    'dispute_split',          -- -5
    'dispute_cleaner_favor',  -- +2
    'job_cancelled_by_cleaner'-- -8
  );
EXCEPTION WHEN duplicate_object THEN NULL; END $$;

DO $$ BEGIN
  CREATE TYPE cleaner_tier AS ENUM ('starter','standard','pro','elite');
EXCEPTION WHEN duplicate_object THEN NULL; END $$;

-- Payout % by tier used for NEW accepts (Section 2 snapshots this)
CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS cleaner_tier_policy (
  tier            cleaner_tier PRIMARY KEY,
  payout_pct      NUMERIC(4,2) NOT NULL,   -- e.g. 0.80 .. 0.88
  min_score       INT NOT NULL,            -- min reliability to qualify
  created_at      TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT now()
);

INSERT INTO cleaner_tier_policy(tier,payout_pct,min_score) VALUES
('starter',  0.80, 0),
('standard', 0.82, 60),
('pro',      0.85, 75),
('elite',    0.88, 90)
ON CONFLICT (tier) DO NOTHING;

-- ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
-- RELIABILITY EVENTS & SNAPSHOTS
-- ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS cleaner_reliability_events (
  id            BIGSERIAL PRIMARY KEY,
  cleaner_id    TEXT NOT NULL,
  job_id        TEXT,
  event_type    reliability_event_type NOT NULL,
  weight        INT NOT NULL,             -- signed integer effect on score
  notes         TEXT,
  occurred_at   TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT now(),
  idempotency_key TEXT
);
CREATE UNIQUE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS cre_idem_uq ON cleaner_reliability_events(idempotency_key)
  WHERE idempotency_key IS NOT NULL;
CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS cre_cleaner_idx ON cleaner_reliability_events(cleaner_id);
CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS cre_job_idx ON cleaner_reliability_events(job_id);

-- Live snapshot for quick reads
ALTER TABLE IF NOT EXISTS users
  ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS reliability_score INT NOT NULL DEFAULT 70,
  ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS reliability_updated_at TIMESTAMPTZ,
  ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS cleaner_tier cleaner_tier DEFAULT 'starter';

-- Rolling metrics for analytics
CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS cleaner_reliability_rollup (
  cleaner_id      TEXT PRIMARY KEY,
  jobs_30         INT  NOT NULL DEFAULT 0,
  jobs_90         INT  NOT NULL DEFAULT 0,
  disputes_90     INT  NOT NULL DEFAULT 0,
  late_30         INT  NOT NULL DEFAULT 0,
  compliments_90  INT  NOT NULL DEFAULT 0,
  score           INT  NOT NULL DEFAULT 70,
  tier            cleaner_tier NOT NULL DEFAULT 'starter',
  updated_at      TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT now()
);

-- ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
-- BONUSES LEDGER (feed into Section 7 payouts)
-- ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS cleaner_bonus_ledger (
  id              BIGSERIAL PRIMARY KEY,
  cleaner_id      TEXT NOT NULL,
  week_start      DATE NOT NULL,
  week_end        DATE NOT NULL,
  bonus_credits   NUMERIC(12,2) NOT NULL,
  reason          TEXT,
  idempotency_key TEXT,
  created_at      TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT now()
);
CREATE UNIQUE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS cbl_idem_uq ON cleaner_bonus_ledger(idempotency_key)
  WHERE idempotency_key IS NOT NULL;
CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS cbl_cleaner_idx ON cleaner_bonus_ledger(cleaner_id);

-- ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
-- FUNCTIONS
-- ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

-- Map event_type to default weight if not provided
CREATE OR REPLACE FUNCTION default_weight_for_event(t reliability_event_type)
RETURNS INT AS $$
BEGIN
  CASE t
    WHEN 'on_time_checkin'       THEN RETURN 1;
    WHEN 'late_checkin'          THEN RETURN -2;
    WHEN 'client_compliment'     THEN RETURN 3;
    WHEN 'client_complaint'      THEN RETURN -4;
    WHEN 'dispute_client_favor'  THEN RETURN -15;
    WHEN 'dispute_split'         THEN RETURN -5;
    WHEN 'dispute_cleaner_favor' THEN RETURN 2;
    WHEN 'job_cancelled_by_cleaner' THEN RETURN -8;
    ELSE RETURN 0;
  END CASE;
END; $$ LANGUAGE plpgsql IMMUTABLE;

-- Append a reliability event (idempotent), then recompute score & tier
CREATE OR REPLACE FUNCTION post_reliability_event(
  p_cleaner_id TEXT,
  p_job_id     TEXT,
  p_event      reliability_event_type,
  p_weight     INT DEFAULT NULL,
  p_notes      TEXT DEFAULT NULL,
  p_idem       TEXT DEFAULT NULL
) RETURNS BIGINT AS $$
DECLARE existing BIGINT; new_id BIGINT;
BEGIN
  IF p_idem IS NOT NULL THEN
    SELECT id INTO existing FROM cleaner_reliability_events WHERE idempotency_key=p_idem;
    IF FOUND THEN RETURN existing; END IF;
  END IF;

  INSERT INTO cleaner_reliability_events(cleaner_id,job_id,event_type,weight,notes,idempotency_key)
  VALUES (p_cleaner_id, p_job_id, p_event, COALESCE(p_weight, default_weight_for_event(p_event)), p_notes, p_idem)
  RETURNING id INTO new_id;

  PERFORM recompute_reliability_for_cleaner(p_cleaner_id);

  RETURN new_id;
END; $$ LANGUAGE plpgsql;

-- Recompute rolling metrics, score (0..100 clamp), and tier
CREATE OR REPLACE FUNCTION recompute_reliability_for_cleaner(p_cleaner_id TEXT)
RETURNS VOID AS $$
DECLARE
  s INT := 70;                -- base score
  add_sum INT;
  now_ts TIMESTAMPTZ := now();
  score_clamped INT;
  new_tier cleaner_tier;
BEGIN
  -- Rolling counts
  -- jobs completed counts use jobs table
  -- Count jobs in windows
  -- (assumes jobs.completed_at is set)
  -- For simplicity, treat 'approved' as completed & payable.
  WITH j AS (
    SELECT id, completed_at
    FROM jobs
    WHERE cleaner_id = p_cleaner_id
      AND status IN ('completed','awaiting_client','approved') -- include near-complete
  ),
  j30 AS (SELECT COUNT(*) c FROM j WHERE completed_at >= now() - INTERVAL '30 days'),
  j90 AS (SELECT COUNT(*) c FROM j WHERE completed_at >= now() - INTERVAL '90 days'),
  d90 AS (
    SELECT COUNT(*) c FROM dispute_cases d
    JOIN jobs j2 ON j2.id=d.job_id
    WHERE j2.cleaner_id = p_cleaner_id
      AND d.created_at >= now() - INTERVAL '90 days'
  ),
  late30 AS (
    SELECT COUNT(*) c
    FROM cleaner_reliability_events e
    WHERE e.cleaner_id=p_cleaner_id
      AND e.event_type='late_checkin'
      AND e.occurred_at >= now() - INTERVAL '30 days'
  ),
  comp90 AS (
    SELECT COUNT(*) c
    FROM cleaner_reliability_events e
    WHERE e.cleaner_id=p_cleaner_id
      AND e.event_type='client_compliment'
      AND e.occurred_at >= now() - INTERVAL '90 days'
  ),
  wsum AS (
    SELECT COALESCE(SUM(weight),0) AS w
    FROM cleaner_reliability_events
    WHERE cleaner_id=p_cleaner_id
      AND occurred_at >= now() - INTERVAL '90 days'
  )
  SELECT w INTO add_sum FROM wsum;

  s := s + COALESCE(add_sum,0);

  -- Clamp 0..100
  score_clamped := GREATEST(0, LEAST(100, s));

  -- Determine tier by policy thresholds
  SELECT tier INTO new_tier
  FROM (
    SELECT tier, min_score
    FROM cleaner_tier_policy
    ORDER BY min_score DESC
  ) t
  WHERE score_clamped >= t.min_score
  LIMIT 1;

  -- Update rollup table
  INSERT INTO cleaner_reliability_rollup(cleaner_id, jobs_30, jobs_90, disputes_90, late_30, compliments_90, score, tier, updated_at)
  VALUES (
    p_cleaner_id,
    (SELECT c FROM j30), (SELECT c FROM j90), (SELECT c FROM d90),
    (SELECT c FROM late30), (SELECT c FROM comp90),
    score_clamped, COALESCE(new_tier,'starter'), now_ts
  )
  ON CONFLICT (cleaner_id) DO UPDATE SET
    jobs_30 = EXCLUDED.jobs_30,
    jobs_90 = EXCLUDED.jobs_90,
    disputes_90 = EXCLUDED.disputes_90,
    late_30 = EXCLUDED.late_30,
    compliments_90 = EXCLUDED.compliments_90,
    score = EXCLUDED.score,
    tier = EXCLUDED.tier,
    updated_at = now_ts;

  -- Update users snapshot (used by Section 2 to snapshot payout % at accept)
  UPDATE users
  SET reliability_score = score_clamped,
      reliability_updated_at = now_ts,
      cleaner_tier = COALESCE(new_tier,'starter')
  WHERE id = p_cleaner_id;

END; $$ LANGUAGE plpgsql;

-- Compute weekly bonus credits from earnings (Section 7 reads this ledger)
-- policy:
--   score >= 90 → +5% of week earnings
--   score >= 80 → +2% of week earnings
--   else 0
CREATE OR REPLACE FUNCTION compute_and_post_weekly_bonus(
  p_cleaner_id TEXT,
  p_week_start DATE,
  p_week_end   DATE,
  p_idem       TEXT
) RETURNS NUMERIC AS $$
DECLARE
  wk_earn NUMERIC := 0;
  score INT := 0;
  rate NUMERIC := 0;
  bonus NUMERIC := 0;
BEGIN
  -- Sum earnings posted (Section 4 ledger) for jobs completed in the week and not yet batched to bonus
  SELECT COALESCE(SUM(e.earnings_credits),0)
  INTO wk_earn
  FROM cleaner_earnings e
  JOIN jobs j ON j.id = e.job_id
  WHERE e.cleaner_id = p_cleaner_id
    AND j.completed_at::DATE BETWEEN p_week_start AND p_week_end;

  SELECT reliability_score INTO score FROM users WHERE id=p_cleaner_id;

  IF score >= 90 THEN rate := 0.05;
  ELSIF score >= 80 THEN rate := 0.02;
  ELSE rate := 0.00;
  END IF;

  bonus := ROUND(wk_earn * rate, 2);

  IF bonus > 0 THEN
    INSERT INTO cleaner_bonus_ledger(cleaner_id, week_start, week_end, bonus_credits, reason, idempotency_key)
    VALUES (p_cleaner_id, p_week_start, p_week_end, bonus, 'weekly reliability bonus', p_idem)
    ON CONFLICT (idempotency_key) DO NOTHING;
  END IF;

  RETURN bonus;
END; $$ LANGUAGE plpgsql;
2) n8n Workflow — Reliability & Bonus Engine
Endpoints / routines:

/reliability/event — Post a reliability event (e.g., from Section 6 when dispute resolves)

/reliability/recompute — Recompute one (or all) cleaners’ reliability (daily)

/bonuses/run-weekly — Compute and post weekly bonus credits (feeds Section 7)

3) Business Rules (final)
Reliability score (0–100)

Base 70 + sum of event weights over last 90 days, clamped to 0..100.

Default weights (tunable):

on_time_checkin +1

late_checkin −2

client_compliment +3

client_complaint −4

dispute_client_favor −15

dispute_split −5

dispute_cleaner_favor +2

job_cancelled_by_cleaner −8

Tiers (snapshot at Accept in Section 2):

starter (≥0) → 0.80 payout%

standard (≥60) → 0.82

pro (≥75) → 0.85

elite (≥90) → 0.88

Bonuses (feed Section 7):

Weekly earnings bonus:

score ≥ 90 → +5% of week’s earnings

score ≥ 80 → +2%

else 0

Written to cleaner_bonus_ledger, which Section 7 already sums into net payout credits.

4) Payload Contracts
A) Post a reliability event
(Use from app/admin or from other sections e.g., Section 6 outcomes)
POST /reliability/event

{
  "cleaner_id": "usr_cleaner_9",
  "job_id": "job_123",
  "event_type": "dispute_client_favor",
  "notes": "Refunded 150 credits after review",
  "idempotency_key": "rel:job_123:client_favor"
}
Returns updated score and tier (via notification node).

B) Recompute reliability for one (or all) cleaners
POST /reliability/recompute

{ "cleaner_id": "usr_cleaner_9" }   // or omit cleaner_id to recompute all
C) Run weekly bonuses (cron or manual)
POST /bonuses/run-weekly
No body; the workflow computes last 7 days automatically.

Tier impact on new jobs

When a cleaner accepts a job (Section 2 /jobs/accept), fetch users.cleaner_tier, look up cleaner_tier_policy.payout_pct, and snapshot into jobs.snapshot_payout_percentage. (We already do this; now the tier stays fresh.)

7) Why this design works
Single source of truth for reliability (events → rollup → score & tier snapshot on users)

Tiered incentives that increase payout % for high performers (and are snapshotted at accept for fairness)

Bonuses integrate cleanly with weekly payouts (Section 7) via cleaner_bonus_ledger

Credits-only end-to-end; bonuses are credits that convert to cash only during cleaner payouts

Automation-friendly: endpoints for events, recompute, bonus runs; cron-ready

1) SQL — Templates, Prefs, Outbox, Attempts, Helpers
Run these in order. They’re additive and won’t break previous sections.

013_notifications_core.sql
-- Channel & priority enums
DO $$ BEGIN
  CREATE TYPE notify_channel AS ENUM ('email','sms','push');
EXCEPTION WHEN duplicate_object THEN NULL; END $$;

DO $$ BEGIN
  CREATE TYPE notify_priority AS ENUM ('low','normal','high','critical');
EXCEPTION WHEN duplicate_object THEN NULL; END $$;

-- Template registry
CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS notification_templates (
  id              BIGSERIAL PRIMARY KEY,
  key             TEXT UNIQUE NOT NULL,         -- e.g., booking_confirmation
  channel         notify_channel NOT NULL,      -- email|sms|push
  subject         TEXT,                         -- email subject (if email)
  body_markdown   TEXT NOT NULL,                -- markdown or plaintext with {{vars}}
  one_signal_heading TEXT,                      -- push heading/title
  enabled         BOOLEAN NOT NULL DEFAULT TRUE,
  created_at      TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT now(),
  updated_at      TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT now()
);

-- Per-user preferences (global + per-template overrides)
CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS user_notification_prefs (
  id              BIGSERIAL PRIMARY KEY,
  user_id         TEXT NOT NULL,
  channel         notify_channel NOT NULL,
  enabled         BOOLEAN NOT NULL DEFAULT TRUE,
  quiet_hours_tz  TEXT,                         -- e.g., 'America/Los_Angeles'
  quiet_start_min SMALLINT,                     -- minutes from 00:00, e.g., 22:00 -> 1320
  quiet_end_min   SMALLINT,                     -- minutes from 00:00
  UNIQUE (user_id, channel)
);

-- Optional per-template opt-outs
CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS user_notification_optouts (
  id              BIGSERIAL PRIMARY KEY,
  user_id         TEXT NOT NULL,
  template_key    TEXT NOT NULL,
  opted_out       BOOLEAN NOT NULL DEFAULT TRUE,
  UNIQUE (user_id, template_key)
);

-- Outbox queue
CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS notification_outbox (
  id              BIGSERIAL PRIMARY KEY,
  template_key    TEXT NOT NULL,
  user_id         TEXT NOT NULL,
  channel         notify_channel NOT NULL,
  priority        notify_priority NOT NULL DEFAULT 'normal',
  -- addresses (one or more can be populated; dispatcher picks)
  email_to        TEXT,
  phone_to        TEXT,
  push_player_id  TEXT,                         -- OneSignal player id
  -- data context for templating
  data_json       JSONB NOT NULL DEFAULT '{}'::jsonb,
  -- routing & idempotency
  dedupe_key      TEXT,                         -- ensure "at most once" per business event
  deliver_after   TIMESTAMPTZ,                  -- for scheduling or quiet-hours defer
  max_attempts    SMALLINT NOT NULL DEFAULT 5,
  attempts        SMALLINT NOT NULL DEFAULT 0,
  last_error      TEXT,
  status          TEXT NOT NULL DEFAULT 'queued',  -- queued|sending|sent|failed|dead
  created_at      TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT now(),
  updated_at      TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT now()
);
CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS notif_outbox_status_idx ON notification_outbox(status, priority);
CREATE UNIQUE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS notif_outbox_dedupe_uq ON notification_outbox(dedupe_key) WHERE dedupe_key IS NOT NULL;

-- Attempts / audit
CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS notification_attempts (
  id              BIGSERIAL PRIMARY KEY,
  outbox_id       BIGINT NOT NULL REFERENCES notification_outbox(id) ON DELETE CASCADE,
  channel         notify_channel NOT NULL,
  provider        TEXT NOT NULL,                -- sendgrid|twilio|onesignal|mock
  success         BOOLEAN NOT NULL,
  response_code   TEXT,
  response_body   TEXT,
  attempted_at    TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT now()
);

-- Helper: get local minutes from midnight for quiet-hour checks
CREATE OR REPLACE FUNCTION minutes_since_midnight_now(p_tz TEXT)
RETURNS INT AS $$
DECLARE t TIMESTAMPTZ;
BEGIN
  IF p_tz IS NULL THEN
    RETURN EXTRACT(HOUR FROM now())::INT * 60 + EXTRACT(MINUTE FROM now())::INT;
  END IF;
  t := (now() AT TIME ZONE p_tz);
  RETURN EXTRACT(HOUR FROM t)::INT * 60 + EXTRACT(MINUTE FROM t)::INT;
END; $$ LANGUAGE plpgsql STABLE;

-- Helper: enqueue (idempotent by dedupe_key)
CREATE OR REPLACE FUNCTION enqueue_notification(
  p_template_key TEXT,
  p_user_id      TEXT,
  p_channel      notify_channel,
  p_email_to     TEXT,
  p_phone_to     TEXT,
  p_push_id      TEXT,
  p_data         JSONB,
  p_priority     notify_priority DEFAULT 'normal',
  p_dedupe       TEXT DEFAULT NULL,
  p_deliver_after TIMESTAMPTZ DEFAULT NULL
) RETURNS BIGINT AS $$
DECLARE x BIGINT;
BEGIN
  IF p_dedupe IS NOT NULL THEN
    SELECT id INTO x FROM notification_outbox WHERE dedupe_key = p_dedupe;
    IF FOUND THEN RETURN x; END IF;
  END IF;

  INSERT INTO notification_outbox(
    template_key, user_id, channel, priority,
    email_to, phone_to, push_player_id,
    data_json, dedupe_key, deliver_after
  ) VALUES (
    p_template_key, p_user_id, p_channel, p_priority,
    p_email_to, p_phone_to, p_push_id,
    COALESCE(p_data,'{}'::jsonb), p_dedupe, p_deliver_after
  ) RETURNING id INTO x;

  RETURN x;
END; $$ LANGUAGE plpgsql;
