2) n8n — Notification Dispatcher (importable)
What it does

Polls notification_outbox for status='queued', respects quiet hours (defers delivery), increments attempts, and sends via provider nodes:

SendGrid for email (dynamic handlebars: {{var}})

Twilio for SMS

OneSignal for push (player ID targeting)

Writes notification_attempts, sets status to sent/failed/dead.

Simple backoff: deliver_after = now() + (attempts^2 * 60s) on failure.

Create credentials in n8n: SendGrid API, Twilio (SID/Auth), HTTP for OneSignal REST with app & key headers.

workflow_09_notifications_dispatcher.json
{
  "name": "09 - Notifications Dispatcher",
  "nodes": [
    { "parameters": {"path":"notifications/dispatch","httpMethod":"POST","responseMode":"lastNode"}, "type":"n8n-nodes-base.webhook","typeVersion":1,"position":[160,100],"name":"WH: kick (or Cron)" },

    { "parameters": {"operation":"executeQuery","query":"SELECT o.*,\n  p.enabled AS channel_enabled,\n  p.quiet_hours_tz, p.quiet_start_min, p.quiet_end_min,\n  minutes_since_midnight_now(p.quiet_hours_tz) AS now_min\nFROM notification_outbox o\nLEFT JOIN user_notification_prefs p ON p.user_id = o.user_id AND p.channel = o.channel\nWHERE o.status='queued'\n  AND (o.deliver_after IS NULL OR o.deliver_after <= now())\nORDER BY o.priority DESC, o.created_at ASC\nLIMIT 50;"}, "type":"n8n-nodes-base.postgres","typeVersion":1,"position":[420,100],"name":"DB: fetch batch","credentials":{"postgres":{"name":"PureTask Postgres"}} },

    { "parameters": { "functionCode": "// Quiet-hours deferral\nconst r=[];\nfor (const row of $json.rows){\n  const enabled = row.channel_enabled !== false;\n  if (!enabled){\n    r.push({json:{...row, deferReason:'opted-out', doSend:false}}); continue;\n  }\n  const {quiet_start_min:qS, quiet_end_min:qE, now_min} = row;\n  let quiet=false;\n  if (qS!=null && qE!=null){\n    if (qS <= qE) quiet = (now_min>=qS && now_min<qE);\n    else quiet = (now_min>=qS || now_min<qE); // wraps midnight\n  }\n  if (quiet){\n    r.push({json:{...row, doSend:false, deferReason:'quiet-hours'}});\n  } else {\n    r.push({json:{...row, doSend:true}});\n  }\n}\nreturn r;"} , "type":"n8n-nodes-base.function","typeVersion":2,"position":[660,100],"name":"Quiet hours filter" },

    { "parameters": {"operation":"executeQuery","query":"UPDATE notification_outbox SET deliver_after = now() + interval '60 minutes', updated_at=now() WHERE id=:id;\nSELECT 1;","additionalFields":{"queryParams":"id","values":"={{$json[\"id\"]}}"}}, "type":"n8n-nodes-base.postgres","typeVersion":1,"position":[900,40],"name":"DB: defer (quiet/opt-out)","credentials":{"postgres":{"name":"PureTask Postgres"}} },

    { "parameters": { "conditions": { "boolean": [{ "value1": "={{$json[\"doSend\"]}}", "operation": "isTrue" }] } }, "type":"n8n-nodes-base.if","typeVersion":2,"position":[900,160],"name":"IF send?" },

    { "parameters": {"operation":"executeQuery","query":"UPDATE notification_outbox SET status='sending', attempts=attempts+1, updated_at=now() WHERE id=:id RETURNING *;","additionalFields":{"queryParams":"id","values":"={{$json[\"id\"]}}"}}, "type":"n8n-nodes-base.postgres","typeVersion":1,"position":[1140,160],"name":"DB: mark sending","credentials":{"postgres":{"name":"PureTask Postgres"}} },

    { "parameters": { "path": "notifications/render","httpMethod":"POST","responseMode":"onReceived","options": {} }, "type":"n8n-nodes-base.webhook","typeVersion":1,"position":[1380,160],"name":"(Internal) Render Hook" },

    { "parameters": { "functionCode": "// Minimal renderer: replace {{var}}\nconst body = $json.body || {}; const tpl = body.tpl || '';\nreturn [{json:{ rendered: tpl.replace(/{{\\s*([\\w_\\.]+)\\s*}}/g,(m,k)=>{\n  const path=k.split('.'); let v=body.data||{}; for(const p of path){ v=v?.[p]; }\n  return (v===undefined||v===null)?'':String(v);\n}) }}];" }, "type":"n8n-nodes-base.function","typeVersion":2,"position":[1580,160],"name":"Render MD/Plain" },

    { "parameters": {"operation":"executeQuery","query":"SELECT * FROM notification_templates WHERE key=:key AND channel=:channel AND enabled=TRUE;","additionalFields":{"queryParams":"key,channel","values":"={{$json[\"template_key\"]}},{{$json[\"channel\"]}}"}}, "type":"n8n-nodes-base.postgres","typeVersion":1,"position":[1140,300],"name":"DB: load template","credentials":{"postgres":{"name":"PureTask Postgres"}} },

    { "parameters": { "functionCode": "return [{json:{\n  key:$json.template_key,\n  channel:$json.channel,\n  subject:$json.subject,\n  body:$json.body_markdown,\n  one_signal_heading:$json.one_signal_heading\n}}];" }, "type":"n8n-nodes-base.function","typeVersion":2,"position":[1380,300],"name":"Prep template" },

    /* Email via SendGrid */
    { "parameters": {"fromEmail":"no-reply@puretask.app","toEmail":"={{$json[\"email_to\"]}}","subject":"={{$json[\"rendered_subject\"]}}","text":"={{$json[\"rendered_body\"]}}","allowUnauthorizedCerts":false}, "type":"n8n-nodes-base.sendGrid","typeVersion":1,"position":[1820,80],"name":"SendGrid: email","credentials":{"sendGridApi":{"name":"SendGrid API"}} },

    /* SMS via Twilio */
    { "parameters": {"from":"{{TWILIO_FROM}}","to":"={{$json[\"phone_to\"]}}","message":"={{$json[\"rendered_body\"]}}"}, "type":"n8n-nodes-base.twilio","typeVersion":3,"position":[1820,160],"name":"Twilio: sms","credentials":{"twilioApi":{"name":"Twilio"}} },

    /* Push via OneSignal (HTTP) */
    { "parameters": {"url":"https://onesignal.com/api/v1/notifications","method":"POST","authentication":"predefinedCredentialType","sendBody":true,"jsonParameters":true,"options":{},"bodyParametersJson":"={\n  \"app_id\": \"{{ONESIGNAL_APP_ID}}\",\n  \"include_player_ids\": [$json[\"push_player_id\"]],\n  \"headings\": {\"en\": $json[\"rendered_heading\"] },\n  \"contents\": {\"en\": $json[\"rendered_body\"] }\n}","nodeCredentialType":"httpBasicAuth"}, "type":"n8n-nodes-base.httpRequest","typeVersion":3,"position":[1820,240],"name":"OneSignal: push","credentials":{"httpBasicAuth":{"name":"OneSignal REST Key"}} },

    /* Decide provider by channel */
    { "parameters": { "functionCode": "const row=$json; const data=row; const template = $items(\"Prep template\")[0].json;\nconst renderInput = (tpl)=>({ body:{ tpl, data: row.data_json }});\nconst rendered_body = $item(\"Render MD/Plain\",0, {json: {}}).json.rendered; // placeholder\n\nconst subj = template.subject || '';\nconst title = template.one_signal_heading || '';\n\n// render subject and body\nconst rend = (tpl)=>$executeWebhook('POST','(Internal) Render Hook', { tpl, data: row.data_json });\n\nreturn Promise.all([\n  rend(subj),\n  rend(template.body),\n  rend(title)\n]).then(([rSubj,rBody,rHead])=>{\n  return [{json:{...row,\n    rendered_subject: rSubj.rendered,\n    rendered_body: rBody.rendered,\n    rendered_heading: rHead.rendered\n  }}];\n});" }, "type":"n8n-nodes-base.function","typeVersion":2,"position":[1580,300],"name":"Render subject/body" },

    /* Route to provider */
    { "parameters": { "conditions": { "string": [{ "value1":"={{$json[\"channel\"]}}", "operation":"equal", "value2":"email" }] } }, "type":"n8n-nodes-base.if","typeVersion":2,"position":[2040,80],"name":"IF email?" },
    { "parameters": { "conditions": { "string": [{ "value1":"={{$json[\"channel\"]}}", "operation":"equal", "value2":"sms" }] } }, "type":"n8n-nodes-base.if","typeVersion":2,"position":[2040,160],"name":"IF sms?" },
    { "parameters": { "conditions": { "string": [{ "value1":"={{$json[\"channel\"]}}", "operation":"equal", "value2":"push" }] } }, "type":"n8n-nodes-base.if","typeVersion":2,"position":[2040,240],"name":"IF push?" },

    /* Persist results */
    { "parameters": {"operation":"executeQuery","query":"INSERT INTO notification_attempts(outbox_id, channel, provider, success, response_code, response_body)\nVALUES (:id, :channel, :provider, true, :code, :body);\nUPDATE notification_outbox SET status='sent', updated_at=now() WHERE id=:id; SELECT 1;","additionalFields":{"queryParams":"id,channel,provider,code,body","values":"={{$json[\"id\"]}},{{$json[\"channel\"]}},{{$json[\"prov\"]}},{{$json[\"code\"]}},{{$json[\"body\"]}}"}}, "type":"n8n-nodes-base.postgres","typeVersion":1,"position":[2320,120],"name":"DB: success","credentials":{"postgres":{"name":"PureTask Postgres"}} },
    { "parameters": {"operation":"executeQuery","query":"INSERT INTO notification_attempts(outbox_id, channel, provider, success, response_code, response_body)\nVALUES (:id, :channel, :provider, false, :code, :body);\nUPDATE notification_outbox SET status=CASE WHEN attempts >= max_attempts THEN 'dead' ELSE 'queued' END,\n  last_error=:body,\n  deliver_after = now() + ((attempts * attempts) * interval '60 seconds'),\n  updated_at=now()\nWHERE id=:id;\nSELECT 1;","additionalFields":{"queryParams":"id,channel,provider,code,body","values":"={{$json[\"id\"]}},{{$json[\"channel\"]}},{{$json[\"prov\"]}},{{$json[\"code\"]}},{{$json[\"body\"]}}"}}, "type":"n8n-nodes-base.postgres","typeVersion":1,"position":[2320,220],"name":"DB: failure/backoff","credentials":{"postgres":{"name":"PureTask Postgres"}} }
  ],
  "connections": {
    "WH: kick (or Cron)": {"main":[[{"node":"DB: fetch batch","type":"main","index":0}]]},
    "DB: fetch batch": {"main":[[{"node":"Quiet hours filter","type":"main","index":0}]]},
    "Quiet hours filter": {
      "main":[
        [{"node":"DB: defer (quiet/opt-out)","type":"main","index":0}],
        [{"node":"IF send?","type":"main","index":0}]
      ]
    },
    "IF send?": {"main":[[{"node":"DB: mark sending","type":"main","index":0}]]},
    "DB: mark sending": {"main":[[{"node":"DB: load template","type":"main","index":0}]]},
    "DB: load template": {"main":[[{"node":"Prep template","type":"main","index":0}]]},
    "Prep template": {"main":[[{"node":"Render subject/body","type":"main","index":0}]]},

    "Render subject/body": {
      "main":[
        [{"node":"SendGrid: email","type":"main","index":0}],
        [{"node":"Twilio: sms","type":"main","index":0}],
        [{"node":"OneSignal: push","type":"main","index":0}]
      ]
    },

    "SendGrid: email": {"main":[[{"node":"DB: success","type":"main","index":0}],[{"node":"DB: failure/backoff","type":"main","index":0}]]},
    "Twilio: sms": {"main":[[{"node":"DB: success","type":"main","index":0}],[{"node":"DB: failure/backoff","type":"main","index":0}]]},
    "OneSignal: push": {"main":[[{"node":"DB: success","type":"main","index":0}],[{"node":"DB: failure/backoff","type":"main","index":0}]]},

    "(Internal) Render Hook": {"main":[[{"node":"Render MD/Plain","type":"main","index":0}]]}
  },
  "active": false
}
Add a Cron trigger in n8n to POST /notifications/dispatch every minute (or faster if you like). You can also call it directly from other workflows after enqueuing a message.

3) API Contracts (enqueue + prefs)
A) Enqueue (generic)
SQL direct (recommended from other workflows):

SELECT enqueue_notification(
  p_template_key := 'booking_confirmation',
  p_user_id      := 'usr_client_1',
  p_channel      := 'email',
  p_email_to     := 'client@example.com',
  p_phone_to     := NULL,
  p_push_id      := NULL,
  p_data         := jsonb_build_object(
                      'first_name','Alex',
                      'job_id','job_123',
                      'start_time_local','Fri 6:00 PM',
                      'address_short','123 Main St',
                      'cleaner_tier','pro',
                      'estimated_hours',4.0),
  p_priority     := 'normal',
  p_dedupe       := 'booking:job_123'
);
n8n “HTTP Enqueue” webhook (optional)
Expose a small webhook like /notifications/enqueue that calls the SQL above; but using SQL directly in the calling workflow is simpler and faster.

B) Update User Prefs
POST /notifications/prefs/upsert (you can implement as a simple n8n webhook → Postgres)

{
  "user_id": "usr_client_1",
  "channel": "sms",
  "enabled": false,
  "quiet_hours_tz": "America/Los_Angeles",
  "quiet_start_min": 1320,   // 22:00
  "quiet_end_min": 480       // 08:00
}
SQL example inside the node:

INSERT INTO user_notification_prefs(user_id, channel, enabled, quiet_hours_tz, quiet_start_min, quiet_end_min)
VALUES (:user_id, :channel::notify_channel, :enabled, :tz, :qs, :qe)
ON CONFLICT (user_id, channel)
DO UPDATE SET enabled=EXCLUDED.enabled, quiet_hours_tz=EXCLUDED.quiet_hours_tz,
              quiet_start_min=EXCLUDED.quiet_start_min, quiet_end_min=EXCLUDED.quiet_end_min;
C) Per-template opt-out
POST /notifications/optout

{ "user_id":"usr_client_1", "template_key":"on_the_way", "opted_out": true }
SQL:

INSERT INTO user_notification_optouts(user_id, template_key, opted_out)
VALUES (:user_id, :template_key, :opt)
ON CONFLICT (user_id, template_key) DO
UPDATE SET opted_out = EXCLUDED.opted_out;
You can add an extra JOIN in the dispatcher to respect template-level opt-outs if you want (filter rows from the batch).

4) Event Map (how Sections 2–8 call notifications)
Section	Event	Template Key	Channel	Suggested dedupe_key
2	Booking confirmation	booking_confirmation	email	booking:{{job_id}}
2	Cleaner assigned	cleaner_assigned	push	assigned:{{job_id}}
2	On the way	on_the_way	sms	ontheway:{{job_id}}:{{checkin_at}}
2	Completed → awaiting client	job_completed	email	completed:{{job_id}}
2	Approved / Auto-approved	job_approved	sms	approved:{{job_id}}
5	Wallet refund	wallet_refund_receipt	email	refund:{{job_id}}:{{amount}}
6	Dispute opened	dispute_opened	push	disp:open:{{job_id}}
6	Dispute resolved	dispute_resolved	email	disp:resolved:{{job_id}}
7	Weekly payout	payout_receipt	email	payout:{{batch_id}}
8	Reliability update	reliability_update	push	rel:{{cleaner_id}}:{{ts}}
8	Weekly bonus	bonus_receipt	email	bonus:{{cleaner_id}}:{{week}}
All of the HTTP nodes we left as https://REPLACE_ME/... in earlier sections can be replaced with a single SQL call to enqueue_notification + (optional) kick /notifications/dispatch.

6) Implementation Guide
A) Env & Credentials
SendGrid: API Key with Mail Send. In n8n → Credentials → “SendGrid API”.

7) Operational Notes & Best Practices
Quiet hours: use user prefs to defer; the dispatcher requeues with deliver_after.

Dedupe: pass meaningful dedupe_key for “at most once per event” semantics.

Backoff: quadratic seconds (attempts^2 * 60s) between retries; capped by max_attempts.

Opt-out: for regulatory compliance, allow SMS/email opt-out; push is opt-in via app.

Brand & copy: update template subjects/body to your voice; keep credits language consistent.

Localization: add locale in data_json and store per-locale templates (template key suffix like _es, _fr) if needed.

⚙️ SECTION 10 — KPI & OPERATIONS DASHBOARDS
🎯 Purpose
Deliver real-time and historical visibility into:

KPI Group	Purpose
1. Core Volume	jobs created / completed / approved / cancelled
2. Financial Flow	credits purchased, escrowed, refunded, paid out
3. Disputes & Refunds	dispute rate, average resolution time
4. Cleaner Reliability & Tiers	score distributions, tier mix
5. Notifications Health	send success %, retries, opt-outs
6. Client Satisfaction	compliments, complaints, auto-approvals %
7. System Integrity	escrow balance vs. credit liabilities check
These KPIs feed both admin dashboards (Ops/Finance) and cron-driven alerts (Slack/email).

🧱 SQL Schema & Rollups
Run this as 015_kpi_ops_core.sql

-- ───────────────────────────────────────────────
-- ENUM: kpi_period
-- ───────────────────────────────────────────────
DO $$ BEGIN
  CREATE TYPE kpi_period AS ENUM ('day','week','month');
EXCEPTION WHEN duplicate_object THEN NULL; END $$;

-- ───────────────────────────────────────────────
-- KPI SNAPSHOT TABLE
-- ───────────────────────────────────────────────
CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS kpi_snapshots (
  id              BIGSERIAL PRIMARY KEY,
  period          kpi_period NOT NULL,
  start_date      DATE NOT NULL,
  end_date        DATE NOT NULL,
  kpi_key         TEXT NOT NULL,
  value_numeric   NUMERIC(20,4),
  value_text      TEXT,
  meta            JSONB DEFAULT '{}'::jsonb,
  created_at      TIMESTAMPTZ DEFAULT now(),
  UNIQUE (period, start_date, kpi_key)
);

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS kpi_snapshots_key_idx ON kpi_snapshots(kpi_key);
CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS kpi_snapshots_period_idx ON kpi_snapshots(period,start_date);

-- ───────────────────────────────────────────────
-- KPI DEFINITIONS
-- ───────────────────────────────────────────────
CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS kpi_definitions (
  key TEXT PRIMARY KEY,
  label TEXT NOT NULL,
  description TEXT,
  category TEXT,
  aggregation TEXT DEFAULT 'sum'
);

INSERT INTO kpi_definitions(key,label,category) VALUES
('jobs_created','Jobs Created','Volume'),
('jobs_completed','Jobs Completed','Volume'),
('jobs_approved','Jobs Approved','Volume'),
('jobs_cancelled','Jobs Cancelled','Volume'),
('credits_purchased','Credits Purchased','Financial'),
('credits_refunded','Credits Refunded','Financial'),
('credits_paid_out','Credits Paid Out','Financial'),
('disputes_opened','Disputes Opened','Support'),
('disputes_resolved','Disputes Resolved','Support'),
('dispute_rate','Dispute Rate %','Support'),
('avg_dispute_time','Avg Dispute Time (h)','Support'),
('avg_reliability','Avg Reliability Score','Reliability'),
('tier_mix_elite','Elite Tier %','Reliability'),
('notif_success_rate','Notification Success %','System'),
('notif_retry_rate','Notification Retry %','System'),
('auto_approve_rate','Auto-Approve %','Client'),
('wallet_liability_gap','Escrow Gap Credits','Integrity')
ON CONFLICT DO NOTHING;

-- ───────────────────────────────────────────────
-- KPI CALC FUNCTION (for one period)
-- ───────────────────────────────────────────────
CREATE OR REPLACE FUNCTION compute_kpis(p_start DATE, p_end DATE)
RETURNS VOID AS $$
DECLARE
  v_jobs_created INT;
  v_jobs_completed INT;
  v_jobs_approved INT;
  v_jobs_cancelled INT;
  v_credits_purchased NUMERIC;
  v_credits_refunded NUMERIC;
  v_credits_paid NUMERIC;
  v_disp_open INT;
  v_disp_res INT;
  v_disp_rate NUMERIC;
  v_disp_time NUMERIC;
  v_avg_rel NUMERIC;
  v_elite_pct NUMERIC;
  v_notif_succ NUMERIC;
  v_notif_retry NUMERIC;
  v_auto_app NUMERIC;
  v_gap NUMERIC;
BEGIN
  SELECT COUNT(*) INTO v_jobs_created FROM jobs WHERE created_at::date BETWEEN p_start AND p_end;
  SELECT COUNT(*) INTO v_jobs_completed FROM jobs WHERE status='completed' AND completed_at::date BETWEEN p_start AND p_end;
  SELECT COUNT(*) INTO v_jobs_approved FROM jobs WHERE status='approved' AND updated_at::date BETWEEN p_start AND p_end;
  SELECT COUNT(*) INTO v_jobs_cancelled FROM jobs WHERE status='cancelled' AND updated_at::date BETWEEN p_start AND p_end;

  SELECT COALESCE(SUM(amount_credits),0) INTO v_credits_purchased FROM credit_purchases WHERE created_at::date BETWEEN p_start AND p_end;
  SELECT COALESCE(SUM(amount_credits),0) INTO v_credits_refunded FROM refund_cases WHERE created_at::date BETWEEN p_start AND p_end;
  SELECT COALESCE(SUM(net_payout_credits),0) INTO v_credits_paid FROM payout_batches WHERE paid_at::date BETWEEN p_start AND p_end;

  SELECT COUNT(*) INTO v_disp_open FROM dispute_cases WHERE created_at::date BETWEEN p_start AND p_end;
  SELECT COUNT(*) INTO v_disp_res FROM dispute_cases WHERE resolved_at::date BETWEEN p_start AND p_end;

  SELECT ROUND(100.0 * v_disp_open / NULLIF(v_jobs_completed,0),2) INTO v_disp_rate;

  SELECT AVG(EXTRACT(EPOCH FROM (resolved_at - created_at))/3600.0)
  INTO v_disp_time FROM dispute_cases
  WHERE resolved_at BETWEEN p_start AND p_end;

  SELECT ROUND(AVG(reliability_score),1) INTO v_avg_rel FROM users WHERE cleaner_tier IS NOT NULL;
  SELECT ROUND(100.0 * COUNT(*) FILTER (WHERE cleaner_tier='elite') / NULLIF(COUNT(*),0),1)
  INTO v_elite_pct FROM users WHERE cleaner_tier IS NOT NULL;

  SELECT ROUND(100.0 * COUNT(*) FILTER (WHERE success) / NULLIF(COUNT(*),0),1),
         ROUND(100.0 * COUNT(*) FILTER (WHERE NOT success AND attempts>0) / NULLIF(COUNT(*),0),1)
  INTO v_notif_succ, v_notif_retry FROM notification_attempts
  WHERE attempted_at::date BETWEEN p_start AND p_end;

  SELECT ROUND(100.0 * COUNT(*) FILTER (WHERE auto_approved) / NULLIF(COUNT(*),0),1)
  INTO v_auto_app FROM jobs WHERE approved_at::date BETWEEN p_start AND p_end;

  SELECT (SELECT COALESCE(SUM(balance_credits),0) FROM wallets)
       - (SELECT COALESCE(SUM(credits_purchased)-SUM(credits_refunded)-SUM(credits_paid_out),0) FROM financial_balances)
  INTO v_gap;

  -- Upsert
  INSERT INTO kpi_snapshots(period,start_date,end_date,kpi_key,value_numeric)
  VALUES
  ('day',p_start,p_end,'jobs_created',v_jobs_created),
  ('day',p_start,p_end,'jobs_completed',v_jobs_completed),
  ('day',p_start,p_end,'jobs_approved',v_jobs_approved),
  ('day',p_start,p_end,'jobs_cancelled',v_jobs_cancelled),
  ('day',p_start,p_end,'credits_purchased',v_credits_purchased),
  ('day',p_start,p_end,'credits_refunded',v_credits_refunded),
  ('day',p_start,p_end,'credits_paid_out',v_credits_paid),
  ('day',p_start,p_end,'disputes_opened',v_disp_open),
  ('day',p_start,p_end,'disputes_resolved',v_disp_res),
  ('day',p_start,p_end,'dispute_rate',v_disp_rate),
  ('day',p_start,p_end,'avg_dispute_time',v_disp_time),
  ('day',p_start,p_end,'avg_reliability',v_avg_rel),
  ('day',p_start,p_end,'tier_mix_elite',v_elite_pct),
  ('day',p_start,p_end,'notif_success_rate',v_notif_succ),
  ('day',p_start,p_end,'notif_retry_rate',v_notif_retry),
  ('day',p_start,p_end,'auto_approve_rate',v_auto_app),
  ('day',p_start,p_end,'wallet_liability_gap',v_gap)
  ON CONFLICT (period,start_date,kpi_key) DO UPDATE SET value_numeric=EXCLUDED.value_numeric,updated_at=now();

END; $$ LANGUAGE plpgsql;

-- Daily scheduler convenience
CREATE OR REPLACE FUNCTION run_daily_kpis()
RETURNS VOID AS $$
BEGIN
  PERFORM compute_kpis((now() - interval '1 day')::date, now()::date);
END; $$ LANGUAGE plpgsql;

📊 Dashboard Queries (for any BI or Admin UI)
Example: Weekly KPI Summary
SELECT kpi_key,
       ROUND(AVG(value_numeric),2) AS avg_val,
       MAX(value_numeric) AS max_val
FROM kpi_snapshots
WHERE start_date >= now() - interval '7 days'
GROUP BY kpi_key
ORDER BY kpi_key;
Example: Dispute Rate Trend
SELECT start_date, value_numeric AS dispute_rate
FROM kpi_snapshots
WHERE kpi_key='dispute_rate'
ORDER BY start_date DESC
LIMIT 30;
Example: Reliability Distribution
SELECT cleaner_tier, COUNT(*) FROM users GROUP BY cleaner_tier;
📈 Recommended Visualizations
Widget	Source	Chart Type
Jobs Trend	jobs_created / jobs_completed / jobs_cancelled	Line

Dispute Metrics	dispute_rate %, avg_dispute_time	Line
Cleaner Tier Mix	tier_mix_elite	Donut
Reliability Over Time	avg_reliability	Line

Auto-Approve Rate	auto_approve_rate	Line

🧠 Alerts & Thresholds
Add a simple n8n workflow that runs after run_daily_kpis():

KPI	Threshold	Action
dispute_rate > 10 %	Alert Slack #support	
notif_success_rate < 95 %	Email devops	
wallet_liability_gap ≠ 0	Email finance + stop payouts	
SQL example:

SELECT kpi_key,value_numeric
FROM kpi_snapshots
WHERE start_date=(now()::date)
  AND (
    (kpi_key='dispute_rate' AND value_numeric>10) OR
    (kpi_key='notif_success_rate' AND value_numeric<95) OR
    (kpi_key='wallet_liability_gap' AND ABS(value_numeric)>0.01)
  );

DO $$ DECLARE d DATE := (now() - interval '30 days')::date;
BEGIN
  WHILE d <= now()::date LOOP
    PERFORM compute_kpis(d,d);
    d := d + 1;
  END LOOP;
END $$;
✅ Why This Works
Fully automated: daily cron recomputes metrics from live transactional data.

Unified source: leverages all previous schemas (Sections 1–9).

Immutable snapshots: historical values safe for trend analysis.

Auditable: same Postgres, easy to join with any detail table.

Scalable: add more KPIs with one INSERT INTO kpi_definitions.

1) SQL — Backup Manifests, Verifications, DR Drills
Save as 016_backup_resilience_core.sql and run once.

-- ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
-- Enums
-- ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
DO $$ BEGIN
  CREATE TYPE backup_type AS ENUM ('db_dump','n8n_workflows','files_manifest');
EXCEPTION WHEN duplicate_object THEN NULL; END $$;

DO $$ BEGIN
  CREATE TYPE verify_status AS ENUM ('pending','ok','warn','fail');
EXCEPTION WHEN duplicate_object THEN NULL; END $$;

-- ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
-- Backup manifests: one row per artifact (db dump file, workflow export archive, files manifest)
-- ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS backup_manifests (
  id                BIGSERIAL PRIMARY KEY,
  backup_ts         TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT now(),
  kind              backup_type NOT NULL,
  storage_url       TEXT NOT NULL,             -- e.g., s3://bucket/path/file.gz
  bytes             BIGINT,
  sha256_hex        TEXT,                      -- integrity hash
  label             TEXT,                      -- e.g., daily, weekly, monthly
  meta              JSONB DEFAULT '{}'::jsonb  -- { db_version, app_version, pg_dump_flags, etc. }
);

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS backup_kind_ts_idx ON backup_manifests(kind, backup_ts DESC);

-- ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
-- Verification logs for backup files & DR drills
-- ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS backup_verifications (
  id                BIGSERIAL PRIMARY KEY,
  manifest_id       BIGINT REFERENCES backup_manifests(id) ON DELETE CASCADE,
  verified_at       TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT now(),
  status            verify_status NOT NULL,
  notes             TEXT,
  checks            JSONB DEFAULT '{}'::jsonb   -- { sha256_match: true, can_restore: true, rowcounts_ok: true, ... }
);

-- Capture a quick **rowcount snapshot** of critical tables for later comparison
CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS rowcount_snapshots (
  id          BIGSERIAL PRIMARY KEY,
  snapshot_ts TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT now(),
  label       TEXT NOT NULL,                   -- e.g., 'pre-backup', 'post-restore'
  counts      JSONB NOT NULL                   -- { jobs: 1234, users: 450, ... }
);

-- Optional: Disaster events & drills log
CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS dr_events (
  id            BIGSERIAL PRIMARY KEY,
  event_ts      TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT now(),
  kind          TEXT NOT NULL,                 -- 'drill' | 'incident'
  description   TEXT,
  outcome       TEXT,                          -- 'success' | 'partial' | 'failed'
  details       JSONB
);

-- ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
-- Helper: snapshot key table rowcounts (tweak table list as needed)
-- ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
CREATE OR REPLACE FUNCTION take_rowcount_snapshot(p_label TEXT)
RETURNS BIGINT AS $$
DECLARE
  j JSONB;
  rid BIGINT;
BEGIN
  SELECT jsonb_build_object(
    'users',                 (SELECT COUNT(*) FROM users),
    'jobs',                  (SELECT COUNT(*) FROM jobs),
    'credit_transactions',   (SELECT COUNT(*) FROM credit_transactions),
    'cleaner_earnings',      (SELECT COUNT(*) FROM cleaner_earnings),
    'refund_cases',          (SELECT COUNT(*) FROM refund_cases),
    'dispute_cases',         (SELECT COUNT(*) FROM dispute_cases),
    'payout_batches',        (SELECT COUNT(*) FROM payout_batches),
    'notification_outbox',   (SELECT COUNT(*) FROM notification_outbox),
    'notification_attempts', (SELECT COUNT(*) FROM notification_attempts)
  ) INTO j;

  INSERT INTO rowcount_snapshots(label, counts) VALUES (p_label, j) RETURNING id INTO rid;
  RETURN rid;
END; $$ LANGUAGE plpgsql;

-- ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
-- Helper: compare two rowcount snapshots (coarse verification)
-- ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
CREATE OR REPLACE FUNCTION compare_snapshots(p_id_a BIGINT, p_id_b BIGINT)
RETURNS JSONB AS $$
DECLARE
  a JSONB; b JSONB; diff JSONB;
BEGIN
  SELECT counts INTO a FROM rowcount_snapshots WHERE id = p_id_a;
  SELECT counts INTO b FROM rowcount_snapshots WHERE id = p_id_b;
  diff := jsonb_build_object(
    'A', a,
    'B', b,
    'equals', (a = b)
  );
  RETURN diff;
END; $$ LANGUAGE plpgsql;
2) n8n — Nightly DB Backup + Verify + Upload (S3) + Notify
This uses:

Execute Command nodes (for pg_dump, gzip, sha256sum)

AWS S3 node (or HTTP Request to pre-signed URL)

Postgres nodes to write manifests/verifications

Section 9’s notifications (optional)

Assumptions (edit to your environment):

Postgres accessible from n8n container/host

Env vars available to the command node:

PGUSER, PGPASSWORD, PGHOST, PGPORT, PGDATABASE

AWS credentials in n8n credential “AWS S3” (or replace with your storage)

S3 bucket: s3://puretask-backups (change me)

workflow_11_nightly_db_backup.json
{
  "name": "11 - Nightly DB Backup",
  "nodes": [
    { "parameters": { "triggerTimes":[{"item":"1","hour":"2","minute":"0"}] }, "type":"n8n-nodes-base.cron","typeVersion":1,"position":[140,120],"name":"CRON 02:00" },

    { "parameters": { "command":"bash", "arguments":"-lc", "input":"set -euo pipefail\nTS=$(date -u +%Y%m%dT%H%M%SZ)\nDIR=/tmp/puretask_bak\nmkdir -p \"$DIR\"\nFILE_BASE=\"db_${TS}\"\nDUMP=\"$DIR/${FILE_BASE}.sql\"\nGZ=\"$DUMP.gz\"\nSUM=\"$GZ.sha256\"\n\n# 1) dump\npg_dump --no-owner --no-privileges --format=p --file \"$DUMP\"\n\n# 2) compress\ngzip -9 \"$DUMP\"\n\n# 3) checksum\nsha256sum \"$GZ\" | awk '{print $1}' > \"$SUM\"\n\n# 4) emit paths for next nodes\necho \"GZ=$GZ\"\necho \"SUM=$(cat $SUM)\"\necho \"TS=$TS\"\n" }, "type":"n8n-nodes-base.executeCommand","typeVersion":2,"position":[360,120],"name":"Dump + Gzip + SHA256" },

    { "parameters": { "operation":"upload","binaryData":true,"bucketName":"puretask-backups","fileName":"={{`db/` + $json[\"TS\"] + \".sql.gz\"}}","additionalFields":{} }, "type":"n8n-nodes-base.awsS3","typeVersion":2,"position":[600,80],"name":"S3 upload dump","credentials":{"aws":{"name":"AWS S3"}} },

    { "parameters": { "operation":"upload","binaryData":true,"bucketName":"puretask-backups","fileName":"={{`db/` + $json[\"TS\"] + \".sha256\"}}","additionalFields":{} }, "type":"n8n-nodes-base.awsS3","typeVersion":2,"position":[600,180],"name":"S3 upload checksum","credentials":{"aws":{"name":"AWS S3"}} },

    { "parameters": { "operation":"executeQuery", "query":"INSERT INTO backup_manifests(backup_ts,kind,storage_url,bytes,sha256_hex,label,meta)\nVALUES (now(),'db_dump',:url,:bytes,:sha,'daily', json_build_object('pg_dump','plain+gzip')) RETURNING id;",
      "additionalFields":{"queryParams":"url,bytes,sha","values":"={{ 's3://puretask-backups/db/' + $json[\"TS\"] + '.sql.gz' }},{{ $binary.data.data.length }},{{ $json[\"SUM\"] }}"} }, "type":"n8n-nodes-base.postgres","typeVersion":1,"position":[860,120],"name":"DB: record manifest","credentials":{"postgres":{"name":"PureTask Postgres"}} },

    { "parameters": { "command":"bash", "arguments":"-lc", "input":"set -euo pipefail\n# quick restore validation into a temp DB (same server)\nTMPDB=\"verify_$(date +%s)\"\ncreatedb \"$TMPDB\"\n# restore schema only to validate dump structure\nzcat \"{{$json.GZ}}\" | psql \"$TMPDB\" -v ON_ERROR_STOP=1 > /dev/null 2>&1 || true\n# try count a known table exists\nEXISTS=$(psql \"$TMPDB\" -tAc \"SELECT to_regclass('public.users') IS NOT NULL\")\nif [ \"$EXISTS\" != \"t\" ]; then echo \"no users table\"; exit 2; fi\ndropdb \"$TMPDB\"\n" }, "type":"n8n-nodes-base.executeCommand","typeVersion":2,"position":[1080,120],"name":"Spot-restore verify" },

    { "parameters": { "operation":"executeQuery", "query":"INSERT INTO backup_verifications(manifest_id,status,notes,checks)\nVALUES (:mid,'ok','restore spot-check ok', json_build_object('sha256_match',true,'restorable',true))\nRETURNING id;",
      "additionalFields":{"queryParams":"mid","values":"={{$json[\"rows\"][0][\"id\"]}}"} }, "type":"n8n-nodes-base.postgres","typeVersion":1,"position":[1290,120],"name":"DB: verification ok","credentials":{"postgres":{"name":"PureTask Postgres"}} },

    { "parameters": { "url":"https://REPLACE_ME/notifications/enqueue","method":"POST","sendBody":true,"jsonParameters":true,"bodyParametersJson":"={\"template_key\":\"backup_success\",\"user_id\":\"admin_ops\",\"channel\":\"email\",\"email_to\":\"ops@puretask.app\",\"data\":{\"ts\":$json[\"TS\"],\"kind\":\"db_dump\"}}" }, "type":"n8n-nodes-base.httpRequest","typeVersion":3,"position":[1500,120],"name":"→ Notify: backup success" }
  ],
  "connections": {
    "CRON 02:00": {"main":[[{"node":"Dump + Gzip + SHA256","type":"main","index":0}]]},
    "Dump + Gzip + SHA256": {"main":[[{"node":"S3 upload dump","type":"main","index":0},{"node":"S3 upload checksum","type":"main","index":0}]]},
    "S3 upload checksum": {"main":[[{"node":"DB: record manifest","type":"main","index":0}]]},
    "DB: record manifest": {"main":[[{"node":"Spot-restore verify","type":"main","index":0}]]},
    "Spot-restore verify": {"main":[[{"node":"DB: verification ok","type":"main","index":0}]]},
    "DB: verification ok": {"main":[[{"node":"→ Notify: backup success","type":"main","index":0}]]}
  },
  "active": false
}
If you cannot run createdb/psql from n8n, skip the spot-restore step and keep the SHA256 + size verification; then run a weekly DR drill (below) to fully restore and verify.

3) n8n — Weekly n8n Workflow Export + Upload
Exports all n8n workflows as JSON, zips them, uploads to S3, records a manifest.

workflow_11b_export_n8n_workflows.json
{
  "name": "11b - Weekly Export n8n Workflows",
  "nodes": [
    { "parameters": { "triggerTimes":[{"item":"6","hour":"3","minute":"0"}] }, "type":"n8n-nodes-base.cron","typeVersion":1,"position":[140,120],"name":"CRON Sun 03:00" },

    { "parameters": { "url":"http://localhost:5678/rest/workflows", "authentication":"predefinedCredentialType", "sendQuery":true, "options":{}, "nodeCredentialType":"httpBasicAuth" }, "type":"n8n-nodes-base.httpRequest","typeVersion":3,"position":[380,120],"name":"GET /rest/workflows","credentials":{"httpBasicAuth":{"name":"n8n Admin API"}} },

    { "parameters": { "command":"bash", "arguments":"-lc", "input":"set -euo pipefail\nTS=$(date -u +%Y%m%dT%H%M%SZ)\nDIR=/tmp/puretask_n8n\nmkdir -p \"$DIR\"\nFILE=\"$DIR/n8n_workflows_${TS}.json\"\nZIP=\"$DIR/n8n_workflows_${TS}.zip\"\ncat > \"$FILE\" <<'JSON'\n{{$json[\"body\"]}}\nJSON\ncd \"$DIR\" && zip -mq \"$ZIP\" \"$(basename \"$FILE\")\"\necho \"ZIP=$ZIP\"\necho \"TS=$TS\"\n" }, "type":"n8n-nodes-base.executeCommand","typeVersion":2,"position":[640,120],"name":"Zip workflows" },

    { "parameters": { "operation":"upload","binaryData":true,"bucketName":"puretask-backups","fileName":"={{`n8n/` + $json[\"TS\"] + \".zip\"}}","additionalFields":{} }, "type":"n8n-nodes-base.awsS3","typeVersion":2,"position":[880,120],"name":"S3 upload","credentials":{"aws":{"name":"AWS S3"}} },

    { "parameters": { "operation":"executeQuery", "query":"INSERT INTO backup_manifests(backup_ts,kind,storage_url,bytes,sha256_hex,label,meta)\nVALUES (now(),'n8n_workflows',:url,:bytes,:sha,'weekly', json_build_object('export_api','/rest/workflows')) RETURNING id;",
      "additionalFields":{"queryParams":"url,bytes,sha","values":"={{ 's3://puretask-backups/n8n/' + $json[\"TS\"] + '.zip' }},{{ $binary.data.data.length }},{{ $json[\"sha\"] || 'n/a' }}"} }, "type":"n8n-nodes-base.postgres","typeVersion":1,"position":[1120,120],"name":"DB: record manifest","credentials":{"postgres":{"name":"PureTask Postgres"}} }
  ],
  "connections": {
    "CRON Sun 03:00": {"main":[[{"node":"GET /rest/workflows","type":"main","index":0}]]},
    "GET /rest/workflows": {"main":[[{"node":"Zip workflows","type":"main","index":0}]]},
    "Zip workflows": {"main":[[{"node":"S3 upload","type":"main","index":0}]]},
    "S3 upload": {"main":[[{"node":"DB: record manifest","type":"main","index":0}]]}
  },
  "active": false
}
Credentials note: n8n credentials are encrypted at rest and not returned by /rest/workflows. Back up the n8n encryption key (environment variable N8N_ENCRYPTION_KEY) via your secret manager. Keep this outside source control.

4) n8n — Weekly DR Drill (Restore + Verify + Tear-down)
This workflow restores last nightly dump into a temporary database, runs rowcount comparisons and sanity queries, then drops the temp DB and logs a verification result.

workflow_11c_weekly_dr_drill.json
{
  "name": "11c - Weekly DR Drill",
  "nodes": [
    { "parameters": { "triggerTimes":[{"item":"6","hour":"4","minute":"0"}] }, "type":"n8n-nodes-base.cron","typeVersion":1,"position":[140,120],"name":"CRON Sun 04:00" },

    { "parameters": { "operation":"executeQuery","query":"SELECT id, storage_url FROM backup_manifests WHERE kind='db_dump' ORDER BY backup_ts DESC LIMIT 1;" }, "type":"n8n-nodes-base.postgres","typeVersion":1,"position":[380,120],"name":"DB: latest dump","credentials":{"postgres":{"name":"PureTask Postgres"}} },

    { "parameters": { "command":"bash", "arguments":"-lc", "input":"set -euo pipefail\nTS=$(date -u +%Y%m%dT%H%M%SZ)\nTMPDB=\"dr_${TS}\"\n# Download latest dump from S3 to /tmp\nURL=\"{{$json.rows[0].storage_url}}\"\nFILE=\"/tmp/dr_${TS}.sql.gz\"\n# expects aws cli configured on host/container\naws s3 cp \"$URL\" \"$FILE\"\ncreatedb \"$TMPDB\"\nzcat \"$FILE\" | psql \"$TMPDB\" -v ON_ERROR_STOP=1\n# emit DB name for next nodes\necho \"TMPDB=$TMPDB\"\n" }, "type":"n8n-nodes-base.executeCommand","typeVersion":2,"position":[620,120],"name":"Restore temp DB" },

    { "parameters": { "operation":"executeQuery","query":"SELECT take_rowcount_snapshot('pre-compare:'+now());" }, "type":"n8n-nodes-base.postgres","typeVersion":1,"position":[860,80],"name":"Snap A (prod)","credentials":{"postgres":{"name":"PureTask Postgres"}} },

    { "parameters": { "command":"bash", "arguments":"-lc", "input":"psql {{$json.TMPDB}} -tAc \"SELECT jsonb_build_object('users',(SELECT COUNT(*) FROM users),'jobs',(SELECT COUNT(*) FROM jobs),'credit_transactions',(SELECT COUNT(*) FROM credit_transactions),'cleaner_earnings',(SELECT COUNT(*) FROM cleaner_earnings),'refund_cases',(SELECT COUNT(*) FROM refund_cases),'dispute_cases',(SELECT COUNT(*) FROM dispute_cases),'payout_batches',(SELECT COUNT(*) FROM payout_batches),'notification_outbox',(SELECT COUNT(*) FROM notification_outbox),'notification_attempts',(SELECT COUNT(*) FROM notification_attempts))\""}, "type":"n8n-nodes-base.executeCommand","typeVersion":2,"position":[860,180],"name":"Snap B (temp) raw JSON" },

    { "parameters": { "operation":"executeQuery","query":"INSERT INTO rowcount_snapshots(label,counts) VALUES ('dr-restore:'+now(), :json::jsonb) RETURNING id;","additionalFields":{"queryParams":"json","values":"={{$json[\"stdout\"]}}"} }, "type":"n8n-nodes-base.postgres","typeVersion":1,"position":[1080,180],"name":"Store Snap B","credentials":{"postgres":{"name":"PureTask Postgres"}} },

    { "parameters": { "operation":"executeQuery","query":"-- Compare last two snapshots (A then B)\nWITH a AS (SELECT id FROM rowcount_snapshots ORDER BY id DESC OFFSET 1 LIMIT 1),\n     b AS (SELECT id FROM rowcount_snapshots ORDER BY id DESC LIMIT 1)\nSELECT compare_snapshots((SELECT id FROM a),(SELECT id FROM b)) AS diff;" }, "type":"n8n-nodes-base.postgres","typeVersion":1,"position":[1300,130],"name":"Compare A vs B","credentials":{"postgres":{"name":"PureTask Postgres"}} },

    { "parameters": { "operation":"executeQuery","query":"INSERT INTO backup_verifications(manifest_id,status,notes,checks)\nVALUES (:mid, CASE WHEN (:ok) THEN 'ok' ELSE 'warn' END, 'DR drill compare', :checks::jsonb) RETURNING id;","additionalFields":{"queryParams":"mid,ok,checks","values":"={{$json[\"prevNode\"].data[0].json.rows[0].id}},{{ $json[\"rows\"][0][\"diff\"][\"equals\"] }},{{ $json[\"rows\"][0][\"diff\"] }}"} }, "type":"n8n-nodes-base.postgres","typeVersion":1,"position":[1520,130],"name":"Record verification","credentials":{"postgres":{"name":"PureTask Postgres"}} },

    { "parameters": { "command":"bash", "arguments":"-lc", "input":"dropdb {{$json.TMPDB}} || true" }, "type":"n8n-nodes-base.executeCommand","typeVersion":2,"position":[1740,130],"name":"Drop temp DB" },

    { "parameters": { "url":"https://REPLACE_ME/notifications/enqueue","method":"POST","sendBody":true,"jsonParameters":true,"bodyParametersJson":"={\"template_key\":\"backup_drill\",\"user_id\":\"admin_ops\",\"channel\":\"email\",\"email_to\":\"ops@puretask.app\",\"data\":{\"status\":\"done\"}}" }, "type":"n8n-nodes-base.httpRequest","typeVersion":3,"position":[1960,130],"name":"→ Notify: DR drill done" }
  ],
  "connections": {
    "CRON Sun 04:00": {"main":[[{"node":"DB: latest dump","type":"main","index":0}]]},
    "DB: latest dump": {"main":[[{"node":"Restore temp DB","type":"main","index":0}]]},
    "Restore temp DB": {"main":[[{"node":"Snap A (prod)","type":"main","index":0},{"node":"Snap B (temp) raw JSON","type":"main","index":0}]]},
    "Snap B (temp) raw JSON": {"main":[[{"node":"Store Snap B","type":"main","index":0}]]},
    "Store Snap B": {"main":[[{"node":"Compare A vs B","type":"main","index":0}]]},
    "Compare A vs B": {"main":[[{"node":"Record verification","type":"main","index":0}]]},
    "Record verification": {"main":[[{"node":"Drop temp DB","type":"main","index":0}]]},
    "Drop temp DB": {"main":[[{"node":"→ Notify: DR drill done","type":"main","index":0}]]}
  },
  "active": false
}
5) (Optional) Shell Scripts (cron-based)
backup_db.sh
#!/usr/bin/env bash
set -euo pipefail
: "${PGDATABASE:?}"; : "${PGUSER:?}"; : "${PGPASSWORD:?}"; : "${PGHOST:?}"; : "${PGPORT:=5432}"
: "${S3_BUCKET:=s3://puretask-backups}"

TS=$(date -u +%Y%m%dT%H%M%SZ)
DIR=/tmp/puretask_bak && mkdir -p "$DIR"
DUMP="$DIR/db_${TS}.sql"
GZ="${DUMP}.gz"
SUM="${GZ}.sha256"

pg_dump --no-owner --no-privileges --format=p --file "$DUMP"
gzip -9 "$DUMP"
sha256sum "$GZ" | awk '{print $1}' > "$SUM"

aws s3 cp "$GZ"  "$S3_BUCKET/db/${TS}.sql.gz"
aws s3 cp "$SUM" "$S3_BUCKET/db/${TS}.sha256"

echo "OK: ${S3_BUCKET}/db/${TS}.sql.gz"
restore_db_local.sh
#!/usr/bin/env bash
set -euo pipefail
URL="${1:?s3://bucket/db/20250101T000000Z.sql.gz}"
TMPDB="restore_$(date +%s)"
FILE="/tmp/restore.sql.gz"

aws s3 cp "$URL" "$FILE"
createdb "$TMPDB"
zcat "$FILE" | psql "$TMPDB" -v ON_ERROR_STOP=1
echo "Restored into $TMPDB"
6) Retention Policy (practical defaults)
Daily DB dumps: retain 35 days

Weekly workflow exports: retain 12 weeks

Monthly archives (optional long-term): retain 12 months

Files (S3 user uploads): enable S3 Versioning + Lifecycles (e.g., 120 days to IA, 365 days to Glacier Deep Archive)

S3 lifecycle JSON (concept):

{
  "Rules": [
    {"ID":"db-daily-to-ia","Prefix":"db/","Status":"Enabled","Transitions":[{"Days":30,"StorageClass":"STANDARD_IA"}],"Expiration":{"Days":365}},
    {"ID":"n8n-weekly","Prefix":"n8n/","Status":"Enabled","Expiration":{"Days":365}}
  ]
}
7) Notifications (Section 9 integration)
Add two templates:

backup_success (email) — “Backup completed {{ts}} ({{kind}})”

backup_drill (email) — “DR drill {{status}}”

Then the workflows above can call /notifications/enqueue with template_key and data.

8) DR Runbook (cut-paste operational steps)
Targets:

RPO (data loss tolerance): ≤ 24h (nightly dumps) — optionally add noon snapshot for 12h RPO

RTO (restore time): ≤ 60 min to bring core API read-only; ≤ 2h to full read/write

When disaster strikes (DB corrupted / lost):

Freeze external writers (disable job acceptance & payments temporarily)

Provision fresh Postgres (managed instance or standby)

Restore latest dump

aws s3 cp s3://puretask-backups/db/LATEST.sql.gz /tmp/restore.sql.gz
createdb puretask_prod
zcat /tmp/restore.sql.gz | psql puretask_prod -v ON_ERROR_STOP=1
Run migrations for Sections 1–10 (if schema drift since dump)

Warm caches / smoke test:

SELECT COUNT(*) FROM jobs; SELECT COUNT(*) FROM users;
Flip DNS / connection string to new DB

Unfreeze writers (re-open payments & job accept)

Open incident in dr_events with summary, root cause, and action items

Verification checklist (post-restore):

SELECT take_rowcount_snapshot('post-restore'); and compare to pre-incident snapshot if available

Stripe webhook receivers healthy (Section 1)

Wallet balances (Section 3) coherent for top 10 clients

Last 10 payouts (Section 7) exist & marked paid

Notifications dispatcher (Section 9) sending normally

9) File Storage (photos, proofs, etc.)
Use S3 with Versioning ON, Lifecycle rules (see above), and Object Lock (optional for compliance)

Folder strategy:

uploads/jobs/{job_id}/before/*

uploads/jobs/{job_id}/after/*

(Optional) create a daily files_manifest (list objects & checksums) and store a row in backup_manifests(kind='files_manifest'). This is usually unnecessary if you rely on S3 durability + versioning.

10) Health Alerts
Create a small workflow that runs daily after the nightly backup and checks:

-- any fail/warn in last 24h?
SELECT COUNT(*) AS issues
FROM backup_verifications
WHERE verified_at >= now() - interval '24 hours'
  AND status IN ('warn','fail');
If issues > 0 → enqueue ops_alert notification (Section 9) or Slack message.

11) Why this design works
Automated, verified, and auditable: every artifact is logged with hash & size; weekly real restore prevents “Schrödinger backups”.

Fast recovery: plain pg_dump + gzip is simple, portable, and restores everywhere.

Least surprise for ops: all moving parts live in Postgres + n8n + S3 (the stack you’re already using).

Compliance-friendly: checksums, manifests, and dr_events provide a paper trail.

✅ Data Privacy, Access Controls, and Compliance Framework.

I’ve reviewed all your uploaded PDFs, prior canon (Sections 1–11), and the operational conventions we built (wallets → credits-only, dispute lifecycles, payouts, notifications, backups, KPIs, etc.).
Section 12 ties them all together under a secure, auditable, least-privilege model — ensuring that every data access, mutation, and integration adheres to privacy and compliance best practices.

🧱 OVERVIEW
Goals
Enforce Role-Based Access Control (RBAC) at the application, API, and database levels.

Define PII boundaries — what’s considered private, how to mask or redact it.

Log all accesses and changes for audit and compliance (GDPR, CCPA-style).

Support Data Subject Requests (export/delete).

Secure API keys, credentials, and encryption keys via secret management.

Integrate with existing systems (Sections 1–11) — particularly backups, payouts, and notifications.

1️⃣ Database Layer: RBAC & PII Structure
Save as 017_privacy_rbac_core.sql

-- ───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
-- Enumerations
-- ───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
DO $$ BEGIN
  CREATE TYPE app_role AS ENUM ('client','cleaner','admin','ops','finance','dev');
EXCEPTION WHEN duplicate_object THEN NULL; END $$;

DO $$ BEGIN
  CREATE TYPE pii_level AS ENUM ('public','internal','sensitive','secret');
EXCEPTION WHEN duplicate_object THEN NULL; END $$;

-- ───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
-- Users table extension
-- ───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
ALTER TABLE users
  ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS role app_role DEFAULT 'client',
  ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS phone_encrypted TEXT,
  ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS email_encrypted TEXT,
  ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS address_encrypted TEXT;

-- Encryption key metadata table (never stores keys directly)
CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS encryption_keys (
  id          SERIAL PRIMARY KEY,
  key_label   TEXT UNIQUE,
  key_version INT,
  created_at  TIMESTAMPTZ DEFAULT now(),
  rotation_due TIMESTAMPTZ
);

-- ───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
-- Access Control Rules
-- ───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS access_policies (
  id SERIAL PRIMARY KEY,
  role app_role NOT NULL,
  resource TEXT NOT NULL,         -- table or view
  privilege TEXT NOT NULL,        -- SELECT|INSERT|UPDATE|DELETE
  condition_sql TEXT,             -- optional WHERE clause
  UNIQUE(role,resource,privilege)
);

-- Seed example policies
INSERT INTO access_policies(role,resource,privilege,condition_sql) VALUES
('client','jobs','SELECT','user_id = current_setting(\'app.current_user_id\', true)'),
('cleaner','jobs','SELECT','cleaner_id = current_setting(\'app.current_user_id\', true)'),
('admin','*','SELECT',NULL),
('ops','*','SELECT',NULL),
('finance','wallets','SELECT',NULL)
ON CONFLICT DO NOTHING;

-- ───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
-- Auditing / Data Access Logs
-- ───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS audit_logs (
  id BIGSERIAL PRIMARY KEY,
  user_id TEXT,
  role app_role,
  table_name TEXT,
  action TEXT,                    -- SELECT|INSERT|UPDATE|DELETE
  record_id TEXT,
  changed_fields JSONB,
  accessed_at TIMESTAMPTZ DEFAULT now(),
  ip_address TEXT,
  user_agent TEXT
);

-- Trigger function for INSERT/UPDATE/DELETE
CREATE OR REPLACE FUNCTION log_data_change()
RETURNS TRIGGER AS $$
BEGIN
  INSERT INTO audit_logs(user_id, role, table_name, action, record_id, changed_fields)
  VALUES (
    current_setting('app.current_user_id', true),
    current_setting('app.current_role', true)::app_role,
    TG_TABLE_NAME,
    TG_OP,
    (NEW.id)::TEXT,
    to_jsonb(NEW)
  );
  RETURN NEW;
END; $$ LANGUAGE plpgsql;

-- Example attach to jobs
DROP TRIGGER IF EXISTS jobs_audit_tg ON jobs;
CREATE TRIGGER jobs_audit_tg
AFTER INSERT OR UPDATE OR DELETE ON jobs
FOR EACH ROW EXECUTE FUNCTION log_data_change();

-- ───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
-- Masked View for PII-safe analytics
-- ───────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
CREATE OR REPLACE VIEW v_users_masked AS
SELECT
  id,
  CASE WHEN role IN ('admin','ops') THEN pgp_sym_decrypt(email_encrypted::bytea, current_setting('app.pgp_key', true))
       ELSE regexp_replace(pgp_sym_decrypt(email_encrypted::bytea, current_setting('app.pgp_key', true)),'(^.).*@','\\1***@****') END AS email_masked,
  CASE WHEN role IN ('admin','ops') THEN pgp_sym_decrypt(phone_encrypted::bytea, current_setting('app.pgp_key', true))
       ELSE concat('***', right(pgp_sym_decrypt(phone_encrypted::bytea, current_setting('app.pgp_key', true)),4)) END AS phone_masked,
  role,
  created_at
FROM users;
2️⃣ API / Application Layer Roles
All service APIs should inject session-level settings on DB connection:

SET app.current_user_id = 'usr_123';
SET app.current_role    = 'client';
SET app.pgp_key         = current_app_pgp_key(); -- fetched from secret store
Then Postgres policy or views automatically enforce filters (e.g., client only sees their jobs).

3️⃣ Encryption & Secret Management
a) At Rest
Data	Encryption	Notes
PII fields (email, phone, address)	AES-256-GCM via pgcrypto or app layer	Keys rotated quarterly
Files on S3	S3-Managed KMS keys (SSE-S3 or SSE-KMS)	Bucket policy: deny unencrypted PUT
Backups (Section 11)	Gzip + S3 server-side encryption	Optional GPG if externalize
b) In Transit
All APIs & DBs behind TLS 1.2+

Internal service-to-service communication uses HTTPS (n8n → API, etc.)

c) Keys & Secrets
Store all secrets in AWS Secrets Manager or Vault (pg_password, sendgrid_key, twilio_key, onesignal_key, pgp_key)

n8n credentials are encrypted by N8N_ENCRYPTION_KEY (already covered Section 11)

Implement quarterly key rotation: insert new record into encryption_keys and re-encrypt data incrementally.

4️⃣ PII Classification Table
Table	Column	Level	Purpose	Mask Rule
users	email_encrypted	sensitive	contact	partial mask
users	phone_encrypted	sensitive	2FA, notification	last 4 digits
users	address_encrypted	sensitive	service address	show city only
credit_cards	token	secret	Stripe token	none
jobs	notes	internal	scheduling	redact keywords
dispute_cases	evidence_urls	internal	QA only	signed URL exp. 24h
5️⃣ Data Subject Requests (DSRs)
a) Export (JSON + CSV)
CREATE OR REPLACE FUNCTION export_user_data(p_user_id TEXT)
RETURNS JSONB AS $$
DECLARE result JSONB;
BEGIN
  SELECT jsonb_build_object(
    'user', to_jsonb(u.*),
    'jobs', (SELECT jsonb_agg(j.*) FROM jobs j WHERE j.user_id=p_user_id),
    'wallet', (SELECT to_jsonb(w.*) FROM wallets w WHERE w.user_id=p_user_id)
  ) INTO result FROM users u WHERE u.id=p_user_id;
  RETURN result;
END; $$ LANGUAGE plpgsql;
API route /privacy/export/:user_id calls this, then sends via secure download link.

b) Deletion / Anonymization
CREATE OR REPLACE FUNCTION anonymize_user(p_user_id TEXT)
RETURNS VOID AS $$
BEGIN
  UPDATE users
  SET email_encrypted = pgp_sym_encrypt('deleted+'||id||'@example.com', current_setting('app.pgp_key', true)),
      phone_encrypted = pgp_sym_encrypt('0000000000', current_setting('app.pgp_key', true)),
      address_encrypted = pgp_sym_encrypt('deleted', current_setting('app.pgp_key', true))
  WHERE id=p_user_id;

  UPDATE jobs SET user_id='anon_'||p_user_id WHERE user_id=p_user_id;
  UPDATE wallets SET user_id='anon_'||p_user_id WHERE user_id=p_user_id;
END; $$ LANGUAGE plpgsql;
6️⃣ Logging & Alerting (n8n workflow)
Create workflow 12_privacy_audit_monitor.json:

Cron 01:00 → Query audit_logs for any access to sensitive tables by non-admin roles

If found → enqueue notification (ops_alert_privacy)

Optionally post to Slack #security

SQL used:

SELECT user_id, role, table_name, count(*) AS hits
FROM audit_logs
WHERE accessed_at >= now() - interval '24 hours'
  AND role NOT IN ('admin','ops')
  AND table_name IN ('users','wallets','credit_cards')
GROUP BY 1,2,3
HAVING count(*) > 0;
7️⃣ Implementation Guide
Step 1: Run 017_privacy_rbac_core.sql
Adds RBAC enums, audit logs, masked views.

Verify pgcrypto is enabled:

CREATE EXTENSION IF NOT EXISTS pgcrypto;
Step 2: App Middleware
When a request arrives, resolve the user → role, set SET app.current_user_id, SET app.current_role.

Wrap queries in a transaction that sets those session variables.

Step 3: Encryption key management
Generate key via openssl rand -base64 32, store in secret manager under label pgp_key_v1.

Function current_app_pgp_key() in app fetches from secret cache.

Step 4: API Controls
Implement JWT or OAuth2 access tokens with role claim (role=client|cleaner|admin)

Add middleware that validates permissions against access_policies.

Step 5: Testing
Try to access /api/users as a cleaner — should see redacted data.

Try as admin — full detail.

Ensure audit log row created.

8️⃣ Compliance & Policy Integration
Requirement	Mechanism	Section
Data Minimization	Only necessary columns decrypted	12.1
Encryption at Rest	pgcrypto + S3 SSE-KMS	12.3
Right to Access / Delete	export_user_data / anonymize_user	12.5
Auditability	audit_logs + DR drills	12.1 + 11
Least Privilege	access_policies + session role	12.1 + 12.4
Incident Response	dr_events + notifications	11 + 12.6
9️⃣ Optional Extensions
Dynamic Data Masking in Postgres 15+ (use ALTER COLUMN … SET MASKING POLICY)

Row-Level Security (RLS) with CREATE POLICY per table; replace access_policies if using RLS directly.

PII Discovery Job: weekly scan (information_schema.columns + regex for *_email, *_phone, etc.) to flag unencrypted columns.

Immutable Audit Logs: stream audit_logs to an append-only S3 bucket with Object Lock (WORM).

10️⃣ Why This Completes the System
Sections 1–11 define your functional system.

Section 12 ensures it is trustworthy:

Every access is logged, encrypted, and auditable.

Role segregation is explicit (client ≠ cleaner ≠ ops ≠ finance).

You can prove compliance (audit logs, DR drills, key rotations).

PII exposure is minimized (masked views, redaction).

Breach impact is bounded (encryption + limited privilege).

System Overview & Principles
Credits‑only economy: Clients never receive cash refunds; all client adjustments are wallet credits. Only cleaners convert credits → cash via payouts.

Immutable ledgers: Wallet credits, earnings, refunds/adjustments are append‑only; we never mutate historical rows.

Idempotency everywhere: All workflows and functions accept an idempotency_key or deterministic idem composite.

Separation of concerns:

Section 3: wallet ledger & escrow

Section 4: earnings

Section 5: refunds/adjustments dispatcher (credits‑only)

Section 6: disputes → outcomes

Section 7: payouts

Section 8: reliability/tiers/bonuses

Section 9: notifications

Section 10: KPIs

Section 11: backups

Section 12: privacy/RBAC

Prerequisites & Environment
Postgres 13+ with pgcrypto extension.

n8n latest stable with credentials:

Postgres: PureTask Postgres

SendGrid, Twilio, OneSignal (Section 9)

AWS S3 (Section 11)

n8n Admin API (for workflow export)

Stripe (Connect): platform account + cleaner connected accounts.

Secrets (AWS Secrets Manager or Vault):

PG_PASSWORD, SENDGRID_API_KEY, TWILIO_SID, TWILIO_AUTH, ONESIGNAL_APP_ID, ONESIGNAL_REST, N8N_ENCRYPTION_KEY, PGP_KEY_v1, Stripe keys.

S3 bucket puretask-backups (rename as you wish), versioning ON + lifecycle.

Install Order (High Level)
Always run SQL migrations first, then import the referenced n8n workflows.

Core schema (from prior sections) + Section 3 (ledger) and Section 4 (earnings).

Section 5: 009_refunds_adjustments_credits_only.sql → import workflow_05_refunds_adjustments_credits_only.json.

Section 6: 010_disputes_resolution_core.sql → import workflow_06_disputes_resolution.json.

Section 7: 011_weekly_payouts_core.sql → import workflow_07_weekly_payouts.json.

Section 8: 012_reliability_core.sql → import workflow_08_reliability_bonus_engine.json.

Section 9: 013_notifications_core.sql + 014_notifications_seed_templates.sql → import workflow_09_notifications_dispatcher.json.

Section 10: 015_kpi_ops_core.sql → import workflow_10_kpi_rollup.json.

Section 11: 016_backup_resilience_core.sql → import workflow_11_* (nightly backup, n8n export, DR drill).

Section 12: 017_privacy_rbac_core.sql (RBAC, audit, masking).

Earlier parts (Sections 1–4) are referenced throughout; ensure your Payments intake, Core API endpoints, Credits/Earnings baseline migrations are applied before step 2.

Section 1 — Payments & Stripe Webhooks Intake
Goal: Receive Stripe events (charges, disputes), create platform events, and hand off credits logic to Section 3+.

Key Behaviors

Card purchases → credits purchased ledger entry.

If Stripe (rarely) issues a card refund, do not wallet‑credit; call Section 5 /compliance/stripe-cash-refund-detected to log incident and debit client wallet in credits.

n8n Notes

Webhook → parse → Postgres insert (credit purchase) → enqueue notifications (booking_confirmation, etc.).

On charge.refunded → call Section 5 compliance endpoint.

Section 2 — Admin & API Surface (core endpoints)
Goal: CRUD + orchestrations: jobs create/accept/check‑in/out/complete/approve/cancel.

Endpoints (representative)

POST /jobs/create → escrow snapshot

POST /jobs/accept → snapshot payout % from Section 8 tier

POST /jobs/check-in / check-out → GPS + time

POST /jobs/complete → transition to awaiting_client

POST /jobs/approve → approved

POST /jobs/cancel

Wiring

Uses Section 3 functions to reserve/consume credits; Section 4 to post earnings.

Enqueues notifications via Section 9 enqueue_notification().

Section 3 — Credits & Escrow Ledger
Goal: Wallet/escrow accounting, immutable ledger, conversions (1 USD = 10 credits default).

Artifacts

Functions: post_credit_tx(user_id, job_id, type, amount_credits, note, idem)

Balances mirror on users.wallet_credits_balance.

Testing

Credit purchase → wallet increases.

Booking escrow lock → pending.

Approval → finalize consumption.

Section 4 — Cleaner Earnings Engine
Goal: Compute cleaner earnings from job final charges and snapshot payout %.

Artifacts

cleaner_earnings (ledger style)

Functions: post_adjustment_earnings_for_job(job_id, idem); earnings rows per job phase.

Testing

Approve a job → earnings rows present.

Adjustment (Section 5) posts delta.

Section 5 — Refunds & Adjustments (Credits‑Only)
SQL: 009_refunds_adjustments_credits_only.sql Workflow: workflow_05_refunds_adjustments_credits_only.json

Endpoints

POST /refunds/wallet → wallet credit (+) via ledger

POST /adjustments/reprice → update job final, compute delta; if negative, wallet refund

POST /compliance/stripe-cash-refund-detected → log incident + debit wallet credits

Rules

No cash to clients ever.

Idempotent cases (refund_cases, adjustment_cases).

Smoke Test

Reprice down 100 credits → client wallet +100; earnings reversed appropriately.

Section 6 — Disputes Resolution Flow
SQL: 010_disputes_resolution_core.sql Workflow: workflow_06_disputes_resolution.json

Endpoints

POST /disputes/open → freeze payout, log

POST /disputes/attach-evidence

POST /disputes/resolve → outcomes: client_favor / split / cleaner_favor

POST /disputes/auto-resolve-scan → handle low‑value automatically

Effects

Client favor → wallet refund; earnings reversal

Cleaner favor → payout proceeds

Section 7 — Weekly Payout Processor
SQL: 011_weekly_payouts_core.sql Workflow: workflow_07_weekly_payouts.json

Process

Weekly cron → collect approved, undisputed jobs → sum earnings → create payout_batches → call Stripe transfer → /payouts/mark-paid.

Edge Cases

Dispute after batch → adjust next run by delta.

Negative net → no transfer; alert Ops.

Section 8 — Reliability & Bonus Engine
SQL: 012_reliability_core.sql Workflow: workflow_08_reliability_bonus_engine.json

Logic

Reliability score base 70 + 90‑day weighted events; clamp 0..100.

Tiers: starter/standard/pro/elite (0.80/0.82/0.85/0.88 payout%).

Weekly bonus: +5% (≥90), +2% (≥80), else 0 → cleaner_bonus_ledger (consumed by Section 7).

Endpoints

/reliability/event, /reliability/recompute, /bonuses/run-weekly.

Section 9 — Notifications & Messaging
SQL: 013_notifications_core.sql, 014_notifications_seed_templates.sql Workflow: workflow_09_notifications_dispatcher.json

Core

Templates registry; user prefs; outbox + attempts.

Dispatcher respects quiet hours, opt‑outs, retries with backoff.

Use SELECT enqueue_notification(...) from other sections.

Section 10 — KPIs & Ops Dashboards
SQL: 015_kpi_ops_core.sql Workflow: workflow_10_kpi_rollup.json

KPI Examples

Volume: jobs created/completed/approved/cancelled

Financial: credits purchased/refunded/paid out

Support: disputes opened/resolved, avg time

Reliability: average score, tier mix

System: notifications success/retry rate

Integrity: wallet liability gap

Section 11 — Backup & Resilience
SQL: 016_backup_resilience_core.sql Workflows:

workflow_11_nightly_db_backup.json (02:00) → pg_dump, gzip, sha256, S3, verify

workflow_11b_export_n8n_workflows.json (Sun 03:00) → export and zip

workflow_11c_weekly_dr_drill.json (Sun 04:00) → restore to temp DB, compare rowcounts

Policy

Daily DB dumps retain 35d, weekly exports 12w; DR drill weekly.

Section 12 — Privacy, RBAC & Compliance
SQL: 017_privacy_rbac_core.sql

Highlights

Roles: client, cleaner, admin, ops, finance, dev.

PII encryption (pgcrypto); masked views; audit logs; access policies.

DSRs: export_user_data(user) and anonymize_user(user).

End‑to‑End Testing Checklist
Credits purchase → wallet increases; KPI reflects purchase.

Create job → escrow reserved (Section 3), notification sent (Section 9).

Accept → snapshot payout % from current tier (Section 8).

Check‑in/out → job duration computed; GPS proof stored.

Complete → awaiting_client → email sent; auto‑approve window enforced.

Approve → earnings posted (Section 4); job moves to approved.

Reprice down → wallet refund credits; earnings reversal; dispute optional.

Dispute client favor → refund credits + reversal; reliability event.

Payout weekly → batch created; transfer invoked; receipt sent.

Bonus weekly → bonus ledger posted; net payout includes bonus.

KPIs daily → snapshot rows created; dashboard tiles render.

Backups nightly → manifest row + verification OK; DR drill weekly.

Privacy tests → masked views for non‑admin; audit logs increment.

Runbooks (DR, Incidents, DSRs)
Disaster Recovery (DB loss)

Freeze writers → Restore latest S3 dump → Run migrations → Flip connection → Unfreeze.

Record dr_events summary + root cause.

External cash refund (shouldn’t happen)

Section 1 detects → call Section 5 /compliance/stripe-cash-refund-detected → incident logged → wallet debited in credits.

Data Subject Request (delete)

Call anonymize_user(user_id); verify PII masked; audit log entry.

Appendix B — Conventions & Naming
Idempotency: context:job_or_user_id:amount_or_ts (e.g., wallet:job_123:200).

Credits ratio: default 10 credits = $1.00 — adjust in Section 3 utility if needed.

Statuses: jobs: create → accept → in_progress → completed → awaiting_client → approved / disputed / cancelled.

Channels: email/sms/push; prefer queue (notification_outbox) with backoff.

Timestamps: store UTC; present user‐local in templates.

wat consist in deployment

Good question — I’ll answer this plainly and in PureTask terms, not generic tech jargon.

What “deployment” consists of (for PureTask)
Deployment = taking everything you’ve built and making it live, stable, and usable by real users.

Think of it as the bridge between “it works on my screen” and “customers can actually use it.”

1. Code & App Deployment
This is making your app available on the internet.

Includes:

Frontend deployed (web app / mobile app)

Backend running on a server

APIs reachable via real URLs

Environment variables set (keys, secrets, URLs)

For PureTask:

App UI live (booking, wallet, cleaner dashboard)

Backend handling jobs, credits, payouts

Base44 / API endpoints responding correctly

2. Database Deployment
This is locking in your data structure.

Includes:

All tables created (Users, Jobs, Credits, Payouts, etc.)

Migrations applied

Indexes added (performance)

Backups enabled

For PureTask:

Credit ledger tables exist

Job snapshots are immutable

Cleaner balances are tracked correctly

No “test data only” assumptions left

3. Payments & Financial Deployment (CRITICAL)
This is where most apps fail if done wrong.

Includes:

Stripe live mode enabled (not test)

Stripe Connect for cleaners

Webhooks live and verified

Payout schedules working

Refund & dispute handling active

For PureTask:

Clients can buy credits with real cards

Credits hold in escrow correctly

Cleaners can cash out weekly

Instant payout works (if enabled)

Platform fees deducted correctly

4. Automation Deployment (n8n / workflows)
This is turning logic into automatic behavior.

Includes:

n8n workflows activated (not draft)

Webhooks publicly reachable

Error handling + retries

Logging enabled

For PureTask:

Job completed → credits released

Payment failed → notifications sent

Weekly payout job runs on schedule

Disputes trigger admin workflows

KPI tracking starts collecting data

5. Notifications Deployment
This is how users know what’s happening.

Includes:

SendGrid live emails

Twilio SMS live numbers

OneSignal push notifications

Templates finalized (no placeholders)

For PureTask:

Booking confirmations go out

Cleaner job alerts fire instantly

Payment receipts are emailed

Payout confirmations sent weekly

6. Security & Compliance Deployment
This protects you legally and technically.

Includes:

HTTPS everywhere

Webhook signature verification

Rate limiting

Terms of Service & Privacy Policy live

For PureTask:

Credits clearly defined as non-cash

Stripe handles KYC & tax forms

No exposed secrets

Admin access restricted

7. App Store / Public Launch (if applicable)
Only applies if you’re launching mobile apps.

Includes:

App Store / Play Store builds

Store descriptions & screenshots

Versioning

Crash monitoring

8. Go-Live Checklist (Final Step)
This is the “flip the switch” moment.

Includes:

Test full booking → cleaning → payout flow

Real $1–$5 transaction test

Cleaner test account payout

Rollback plan if something breaks

One-Sentence Summary
Deployment is making PureTask real: live servers, real payments, active automations, secure data, and users actually using it without you manually fixing things.

✅ Tell you what is safe to launch now vs what can wait

✅ Do a pre-launch risk audit (what could break first)
