Absolutely. Below is the final PureTask V1 API Contract Doc assuming:

✅ Cookie-based auth (HttpOnly access/refresh cookies)
✅ CSRF header (double-submit token)
✅ Idempotency-Key for critical writes
…and using your existing route style (/auth, /jobs, /credits, /payments, /messages, /stripe, /events).

PureTask V1 API Contract Doc (Final)
0) Global standards
Base URL
https://api.puretask.com

Auth model (cookie-based)
Backend sets cookies:

pt_access (HttpOnly, Secure, SameSite=Lax, short-lived)

pt_refresh (HttpOnly, Secure, SameSite=Lax, longer-lived)

Frontend behavior:

every request must send cookies:

fetch(url, { credentials: "include" })

CSRF model (required for writes)
Backend sets a non-HttpOnly cookie:

pt_csrf (readable by JS)

Frontend must include header on all state-changing requests:

X-CSRF-Token: <value of pt_csrf cookie>

Required headers by request type
Read-only endpoints

Content-Type: application/json (optional for GET)

Cookies sent via credentials: include

State-changing endpoints (POST/PATCH/DELETE)

Content-Type: application/json

X-CSRF-Token: <pt_csrf>

Idempotency-Key: <uuid> (only on “critical writes”, listed below)

Standard response envelope
Use direct JSON objects (no “data” wrapper) but return consistent error shape.

Standard error shape
{
  "error": {
    "code": "SOME_CODE",
    "message": "Human readable message",
    "details": { "optional": true }
  }
}
Canonical error codes
UNAUTHORIZED (401) – not logged in / missing access cookie

FORBIDDEN (403) – wrong role or not owner

NOT_FOUND (404)

VALIDATION_ERROR (400)

CSRF_REQUIRED (403) – missing/invalid CSRF

IDEMPOTENCY_REQUIRED (400) – missing Idempotency-Key where required

IDEMPOTENCY_CONFLICT (409) – same key, different payload

INVALID_STATE (409) – invalid job transition

RATE_LIMITED (429)

INTERNAL_ERROR (500)

1) Idempotency rules
Idempotency-Key required on these endpoints
POST /jobs

POST /jobs/:jobId/offer

POST /jobs/:jobId/transition (especially approval/dispute/resolve)

POST /credits/checkout

(optional) POST /messages/job/:jobId if you want message dedupe

Idempotency behavior
Same key + same endpoint + same payload → return original success response

Same key + same endpoint + different payload → 409 IDEMPOTENCY_CONFLICT

Keys should be stored with: (key, endpoint, request_hash, response_json, created_at, user_id)

2) Internal events (emitted by workflows)
Canonical event names
Job lifecycle:

job.created

job.offer.sent

job.accepted

job.on_my_way

job.started

job.completed

job.approved

job.disputed

job.dispute_resolved.refund

job.dispute_resolved.no_refund

job.cancelled

Credits:

credits.hold.created

credits.hold.released

credits.charge.finalized

credits.refund.issued

credits.purchase.initiated

credits.purchase.confirmed

Messaging:

message.sent

Notifications (optional to track):

notify.sent

notify.failed

Minimum event payload keys (recommended):

{
  "event_id": "uuid",
  "occurred_at": "ISO-8601",
  "actor": { "type": "client|cleaner|admin|system", "id": "..." },
  "job_id": "j_...",
  "idempotency_key": "optional",
  "payload": {}
}
3) Auth endpoints (/auth)
3.1 POST /auth/login
Purpose: login/signup and set cookies
Write: yes → requires CSRF? (not necessary if login is same-site + you don’t have cookies yet; you can skip CSRF here)
Workflow: auth.login_or_signup
Emits: user.logged_in (optional)

Request

{ "provider": "google", "id_token": "..." }
Response

{
  "user": { "id": "u_123", "role": "client", "name": "Sam", "email": "sam@x.com" }
}
(Set cookies server-side: pt_access, pt_refresh, pt_csrf)

3.2 GET /auth/me
Purpose: session bootstrap for Lovable
Workflow: none (read-only)

Response

{ "user": { "id": "u_123", "role": "client", "name": "Sam", "email": "sam@x.com" } }
3.3 POST /auth/logout
Purpose: clear cookies
Requires: CSRF
Workflow: auth.logout (optional)
Response

{ "ok": true }
3.4 POST /auth/refresh
Purpose: rotate access token using refresh cookie
CSRF: recommended
Response

{ "ok": true }
(Server sets a fresh pt_access cookie)

5.7 POST /jobs/:jobId/transition ✅ CSRF + IDEMPOTENCY REQUIRED
Purpose: single state machine transition endpoint
Workflow: routes by event_type:

status updates → job.status.update

approval → job.approve + credits.settle_for_job

dispute → job.dispute.open

resolve → job.dispute.resolve_* (+ refund path if needed)

}

{
  "job": { "id": "j_100", "status": "approved" },
  "credits": { "charged": 83, "refunded": 13 }
}
Errors

INVALID_STATE (409) (bad transition)

FORBIDDEN (403) (wrong actor role)

IDEMPOTENCY_REQUIRED (400)

CSRF_REQUIRED (403)

Emits (by event_type)

job.* corresponding to the transition

if approval: credits.charge.finalized, credits.refund.issued

if cancel: credits.hold.released

Awesome — here is Deliverable B: Endpoint → Base44 Workflow Blueprint Pack in the cookie auth + CSRF header + Idempotency-Key model, using your existing route style.

I’m going to give you a build-ready blueprint for every write endpoint in V1:

Trigger → Workflow(s)

Required headers

Validations (role/state/ownership)

Deliverable B — Workflow Blueprint Pack
Shared building blocks (used by all workflows)
B0.1 Required middleware order (write endpoints)
Cookie auth (validate pt_access)

CSRF validation (check X-CSRF-Token == pt_csrf cookie)

Idempotency gate (only for endpoints marked “IDEMPOTENT REQUIRED”)

Request body validation

Workflow execution (Base44)

Persist response for idempotency replay (if applicable)

Emit events

Return response

B0.2 Idempotency gate (exact behavior)
When required, the endpoint must:

Input

Idempotency-Key header

user_id

endpoint

request_hash (hash of body + critical params)

Logic

If no key → 400 IDEMPOTENCY_REQUIRED

If key exists with same endpoint + user_id:

If request_hash matches → return saved response

Else → 409 IDEMPOTENCY_CONFLICT

Else → create idempotency record in “processing” state and proceed

On success

store response_json, set status = completed

On failure

store status = failed, plus error payload (optional)

allow retry safely

Recommended idempotency record fields

idempotency_key, user_id, endpoint, request_hash, status, response_json, created_at

B0.3 Event publishing standard
Every workflow emits an internal event with:

event_id, occurred_at, actor, job_id (if relevant), idempotency_key (if present), payload

1) Auth workflows
1.1 POST /auth/login
Purpose: create session cookies (pt_access, pt_refresh, pt_csrf) and return user
Headers: none special (CSRF not required)
Workflow: auth.login_or_signup
Emits: user.logged_in (+ user.created if new)

Validations
provider token valid (Google id_token)

role choice must be present at signup (client vs cleaner), then locked

DB reads
users by provider subject/email

DB writes
If new user:

insert users

insert user_roles

Always:

insert/update sessions (or token version)

generate pt_csrf token record (optional)

Response
{ "user": { "id":"u_123","role":"client","name":"Sam","email":"sam@x.com" } }
Cookies set
pt_access (HttpOnly)

pt_refresh (HttpOnly)

pt_csrf (not HttpOnly)

1.2 POST /auth/logout
Headers: X-CSRF-Token required
Workflow: auth.logout (or simple session deletion)
Emits: user.logged_out

Validations
must be logged in

CSRF valid

DB writes
revoke refresh session / delete session row

clear cookies

Response
{ "ok": true }
1.3 POST /auth/refresh
Headers: CSRF recommended (do it)
Workflow: auth.refresh_session
Emits: user.session_refreshed

Validations
refresh cookie exists + valid + not revoked

DB writes
rotate refresh token/session

set new pt_access

optionally rotate pt_csrf

2) Booking / Jobs workflows
2.1 POST /jobs ✅ (CSRF + IDEMPOTENCY REQUIRED)
Purpose: create job + hold credits
Workflow chain:

job.create

credits.hold.for_job

(optional) notify.client.job_updates → “booking created”
Emits:

job.created

credits.hold.created

notify.sent (optional)

Required headers
X-CSRF-Token

Idempotency-Key

Validations
actor role = client

client profile complete enough (name/email at least)

scheduled_start_at < scheduled_end_at

requested credits/hold amount is within allowed bounds

client has available credits ≥ hold_credits

(optional) geo fields present if required for matching

DB reads
wallet / credits balance (available/held)

pricing config (buffer %, min hold) if you compute holds dynamically

DB writes (transaction required)
Insert into jobs

include: schedule, address, lat/lng, credit_amount (hold target), client_notes

set status: requested (or created)

Insert into job_events

job_created

Insert into credits_ledger

type HOLD

amount -hold_credits

reference job_id

Update wallet cache fields (optional)

available decreases, held increases

Response (canonical)
{
  "job": { "id":"j_100", "status":"requested", "scheduled_start_at":"...", "scheduled_end_at":"...", "credit_amount":96 },
  "credits": { "held": 96 }
}
Failure behavior
If any DB write fails, rollback and mark idempotency record as failed

2.2 POST /jobs/:jobId/offer ✅ (CSRF + IDEMPOTENCY REQUIRED)
Purpose: send offer to one or more cleaners
Workflow: job.request_sent
Emits:

job.offer.sent

notify.sent (cleaner notified)

Headers
X-CSRF-Token

Idempotency-Key

Validations
actor role = client

job exists and belongs to client

job status allows offers (ex: requested / pending_acceptance)

cleaner_ids not empty

each cleaner is active/eligible (not suspended, in region, available)

DB reads
job by jobId

cleaners by ids

existing offers for this job (avoid re-offering same cleaner)

DB writes (transaction recommended)
Insert job_offers rows (job_id, cleaner_id, offered_at, status=pending)

Insert job_events: offer_sent (optional) OR keep as workflow event only

Trigger notification fanout (Base44 → n8n OR internal provider)

Response
{ "ok": true }
2.3 POST /jobs/:jobId/transition ✅ (CSRF + IDEMPOTENCY REQUIRED)
Purpose: single state machine entrypoint for all job lifecycle actions
Workflow router based on event_type:

Router mapping
job_accepted → job.accept (or handled inside job.status.update)

cleaner_on_my_way → job.status.update

job_started → job.status.update

job_completed → job.status.update (+ enforce after photos required)

client_approved → job.approve + credits.settle_for_job (+ cleaner earnings)

client_disputed → job.dispute.open

dispute_resolved_refund → job.dispute.resolve_refund (+ maybe refund.process)

dispute_resolved_no_refund → job.dispute.resolve_no_refund

job_cancelled → job.cancel (+ credits.hold.released)

Headers
X-CSRF-Token

Idempotency-Key

Universal validations (all transitions)
job exists

actor is permitted:

client can only do client events (client_approved, client_disputed, maybe job_cancelled)

cleaner can only do cleaner events (job_accepted, cleaner_on_my_way, job_started, job_completed)

admin can do dispute resolve events

state transition is valid from current job status (finite state machine)

Universal DB writes
insert job_events row with event_type and payload

update jobs.status + any timestamps (started_at, completed_at)

2.3.a Workflow: job.status.update (merged)
Handles: job_accepted, cleaner_on_my_way, job_started, job_completed, job_cancelled (if cleaner-initiated cancel exists)

Validations (per event)
job_accepted

ensure no cleaner already assigned (or allow reassignment rules)

ensure offer exists for this cleaner (if using offers)

job_started

require GPS present (lat/lng)

ensure within geo radius of job location (optional rule)

job_completed

require check-out GPS (optional)

require after-photos uploaded (recommended hard requirement)

compute time worked:

from started_at to completed_at (or explicit payload minutes)

DB writes
update jobs:

set cleaner_id when accepted

set status

set on_my_way_at, started_at, completed_at

insert job_events (already done by universal step)

trigger notify.client.job_updates (client gets status updates)

Emits
corresponding job events: job.accepted, job.on_my_way, job.started, job.completed

2.3.b Workflow: job.approve (client approval)
Triggered by event_type = client_approved

Validations
actor role = client, owns job

job status is awaiting_approval (or equivalent)

required proof exists:

before photos present

after photos present

time worked computed and frozen (no changes after approval)

approval window not expired (optional)

DB writes (transaction required)
update jobs.status = approved

insert job_events: client_approved

freeze final bill inputs in jobs:

time_worked_minutes

final_charge_credits

refunded_credits

Then call settlement workflow:
credits.settle_for_job

Emits
job.approved

2.3.c Workflow: credits.settle_for_job (charge + refund remainder)
Triggered after approval.

Inputs
job_id

hold amount (from ledger or job.credit_amount)

final bill (time * rate, bounded by hold rules)

Validations
there is an active HOLD ledger entry for this job not yet settled

settlement has not been executed before (idempotent on job_id)

DB writes (transaction required)
Create ledger entry: CHARGE (negative)

Create ledger entry: RELEASE_HOLD or mark hold as settled

If remainder > 0, create ledger entry: REFUND (positive)

Update wallet cached balances (if you keep cache)

Update cleaner earnings:

credit earnings record for cleaner tied to job (if your model uses that)

Emits
credits.charge.finalized

credits.refund.issued (if applicable)

credits.hold.released (optional)

2.3.d Workflow: job.dispute.open
Triggered by event_type = client_disputed

Validations
client owns job

job status is awaiting_approval OR approved within window (your policy choice)

dispute reason provided (type + optional note)

DB writes
insert disputes record (job_id, client_id, cleaner_id, type, note, status=open)

update jobs.status = disputed

insert job_events: client_disputed

lock settlement if not done yet (do not release funds)

Emits
job.disputed

support.ticket.created (optional)

2.3.e Workflow: job.dispute.resolve_refund
Triggered by event_type = dispute_resolved_refund (admin only)

Validations
actor role = admin

dispute exists + open

settlement status check:

if already charged, compute refund amount

if still held, release hold back to client

DB writes (transaction)
update dispute status = resolved_refund

update job status = completed_resolved (or similar)

ledger:

if charged → create REFUND entry

if only held → release hold back to available

optionally create Stripe refund via n8n if fiat was involved

Emits
job.dispute_resolved.refund

credits.refund.issued

n8n handoff (only if fiat/Stripe charge exists)
call n8n: refund.process

2.3.f Workflow: job.dispute.resolve_no_refund
Triggered by event_type = dispute_resolved_no_refund (admin only)

Validations
admin only

dispute exists + open

DB writes
dispute status resolved_no_refund

job status finalized

if hold exists and not settled, proceed to settle (or release to cleaner) per your policy

Emits
job.dispute_resolved.no_refund

2.3.g Workflow: job.cancel
Triggered by event_type = job_cancelled

Validations
actor allowed:

client cancel allowed only before certain states

cleaner cancel allowed only before start (if allowed)

job not already completed/approved

DB writes (transaction)
update job status = cancelled

insert job_events = cancelled

release hold:

ledger entry to reverse hold effect (HOLD_RELEASE or REFUND_HOLD)

notify cleaner/client

Emits
job.cancelled

credits.hold.released

Deliverable B — Base44 workflow blueprints (1:1)
Shared foundations (applies to every workflow)
Neon tables (from your schema)
users, client_profiles, cleaner_profiles

jobs (status enum: requested | accepted | on_my_way | in_progress | awaiting_approval | completed | disputed | cancelled)

job_events

credit_ledger (reason enum includes things like hold/charge/refund/purchase/etc.)

payment_intents, stripe_events, payouts

disputes

kpi_snapshots, notification_failures

Add 1 missing table (recommended for idempotency)
Create a tiny table in Neon (Base44 can write/read it):

idempotency_keys

idempotency_key TEXT PRIMARY KEY

user_id TEXT NOT NULL

endpoint TEXT NOT NULL

request_hash TEXT NOT NULL

response_json JSONB

status TEXT NOT NULL (processing|completed|failed)

created_at TIMESTAMPTZ DEFAULT now()

Why: without this, you will eventually double-hold/double-charge under retries.

Universal event logging rule
Every workflow that changes anything writes one row to:

job_events (for job-related flows)
…and optionally emits a normalized event to /events and/or /n8n/events.

Deliverable D — Ownership map (who does what)
One-page truth table
Layer	Owns	Does NOT Own
Lovable (Frontend)	UI/UX, screen state display, calling APIs, showing timeline/wallet/chat	Any business rules, job state transitions, credits math, Stripe verification
Backend/API (Express)	Auth (cookies), CSRF validation, idempotency gate, request validation, routing to Base44/n8n, shaping responses	Core product logic calculations (should be Base44), Stripe retry logic
Base44 (Product Brain)	Job state machine, credit ledger rules, dispute policy rules, reliability scoring, admin ops actions, event emission	Stripe webhook ingest, long retry loops, scheduled tasks (best in n8n)
n8n (Integrations Engine)	Stripe webhook ingest + signature verify + retries, refunds/chargebacks, scheduled jobs (backups/weekly summary), message delivery if desired	Source-of-truth state (that’s Neon/Base44), job transition authority
Neon (Database)	Source of truth tables: jobs, job_events, credit_ledger, disputes, stripe_events, etc.	Any logic execution
Deliverable E — Integration checklist (“did we wire it correctly?”)
E1) Frontend safety
 Lovable never connects to Neon directly

 Lovable uses fetch(..., { credentials: "include" }) everywhere

 Lovable includes X-CSRF-Token for every POST/PATCH/DELETE

 Lovable includes Idempotency-Key for critical writes:

 create job

 send offer

 transition (approve/dispute/resolve/cancel)

 credits checkout

E2) Auth + CSRF correctness
 pt_access and pt_refresh cookies are HttpOnly + Secure

 pt_csrf cookie exists and matches header checks

 CORS allows credentials only from your app domain(s)

E3) Job transitions sanity
 Only one path changes job status (recommended: /jobs/:id/transition)

 Every transition writes a row in job_events

 jobs.status always matches the latest allowed state

E4) Ledger integrity
 credit_ledger is append-only (no updates, no deletes)

 Holds are created once per job

 Approval settlement writes:

 a charge entry

 a hold release/settlement marker (via reason)

 a refund entry when applicable

 Available credits are computed from ledger consistently (or cached safely)

E5) Stripe replay safety
 Stripe webhook ingest is in n8n

 Every Stripe event is deduped via stripe_events.stripe_event_id UNIQUE

 Webhooks are safe to retry without double-crediting

E6) Observability / debugging
 Every critical action emits a canonical event to /events

 Failures create rows in notification_failures (and any other failure tables you add)

 You can reconstruct any job’s story from job_events

E7) “Done means done”
 End-to-end scenario passes:

create job → hold credits

offer sent → accept

on_my_way → started → completed → awaiting_approval

approve → ledger settles → job completed

messages work for both sides

Stripe purchase adds credits safely

If you want, paste your Base44 workflow builder constraints (what connectors/actions it supports for Postgres + HTTP), and I’ll convert each workflow above into click-by-click Base44 build sheets (nodes, conditions, SQL snippets) with zero ambiguity.


Base44 workflows are implemented as Deno Deploy backend functions. These functions directly support:

Postgres (via Base44 SDK entities): Full CRUD operations (create, read, update, delete) on all defined entities (which map directly to Postgres tables).
HTTP (via Base44 SDK integrations and native Deno fetch): Calling external APIs (like Stripe, notifications, etc.) using base44.integrations for pre-built functionality (e.g., sending emails, invoking LLMs, file uploads) or directly using the fetch API for any custom HTTP requests.

Perfect — that means we can finish this properly as production-grade Deno Deploy functions using:

Base44 SDK entities for Postgres CRUD

base44.integrations / fetch() for HTTP calls (n8n, Stripe, notifications, etc.)

Below is the implementation pack you need to complete Deliverable B in a way that’s copy/paste-able and consistent across every workflow.

Base44 Workflow Implementation Standard
A) Shared primitives (you’ll reuse in every workflow)
A1) Idempotency helper (required for critical writes)
Entity/table: idempotency_keys (create this in Neon and expose as Base44 entity)

Fields:

idempotency_key (PK)

user_id

endpoint

request_hash

status (processing|completed|failed)

response_json

created_at

Helper pattern

import { base44 } from "@/base44.ts";

export async function idempotencyGate(opts: {
  key: string | null;
  userId: string;
  endpoint: string;
  requestHash: string;
}) {
  const { key, userId, endpoint, requestHash } = opts;

  if (!key) {
    return { ok: false, status: 400, error: { code: "IDEMPOTENCY_REQUIRED", message: "Missing Idempotency-Key" } };
  }

  const existing = await base44.entities.idempotency_keys.get(key).catch(() => null);

  if (existing) {
    if (existing.endpoint !== endpoint || existing.user_id !== userId) {
      return { ok: false, status: 409, error: { code: "IDEMPOTENCY_CONFLICT", message: "Idempotency key already used for another request" } };
    }
    if (existing.request_hash !== requestHash) {
      return { ok: false, status: 409, error: { code: "IDEMPOTENCY_CONFLICT", message: "Idempotency key used with different payload" } };
    }
    if (existing.status === "completed" && existing.response_json) {
      return { ok: true, replay: true, response: existing.response_json };
    }
    // If processing/failed, you can allow retry logic here.
  }

  await base44.entities.idempotency_keys.create({
    idempotency_key: key,
    user_id: userId,
    endpoint,
    request_hash: requestHash,
    status: "processing",
    response_json: null,
  });

  return { ok: true, replay: false };
}

export async function idempotencyComplete(key: string, responseJson: unknown) {
  await base44.entities.idempotency_keys.update(key, {
    status: "completed",
    response_json: responseJson,
  });
}

export async function idempotencyFail(key: string, errorJson: unknown) {
  await base44.entities.idempotency_keys.update(key, {
    status: "failed",
    response_json: errorJson,
  });
}
A2) Event emitter (your canonical /events + /n8n/events)
export async function emitEvent(name: string, data: any) {
  const event = {
    event_id: crypto.randomUUID(),
    occurred_at: new Date().toISOString(),
    name,
    actor: data.actor,
    job_id: data.job_id ?? null,
    idempotency_key: data.idempotency_key ?? null,
    payload: data.payload ?? {},
  };

  // internal event bus
  await fetch(`${Deno.env.get("API_BASE_URL")}/events`, {
    method: "POST",
    headers: { "Content-Type": "application/json", "X-Internal-Token": Deno.env.get("INTERNAL_TOKEN")! },
    body: JSON.stringify(event),
  });

  // fanout to n8n (optional per event)
  if (data.fanoutToN8n) {
    await fetch(`${Deno.env.get("API_BASE_URL")}/n8n/events`, {
      method: "POST",
      headers: { "Content-Type": "application/json", "X-Internal-Token": Deno.env.get("INTERNAL_TOKEN")! },
      body: JSON.stringify(event),
    });
  }

  return event;
}
A3) Notifications wrapper (Base44 integrations or n8n)
Best: Base44 decides what to send, n8n handles delivery/retries.

export async function notifyViaN8n(template: string, to: any, vars: any) {
  await fetch(Deno.env.get("N8N_NOTIFY_URL")!, {
    method: "POST",
    headers: { "Content-Type": "application/json", "X-Signature": Deno.env.get("N8N_HMAC")! },
    body: JSON.stringify({ template, to, vars }),
  });
}

1) job.create (and calls credits.hold.for_job)
Trigger: POST /jobs
Idempotency: REQUIRED

Validations
actor.role = client

scheduled_start < scheduled_end

client has enough available credits

Reads
users, client_profiles

credit balance (computed from credit_ledger)

Writes (transaction-style sequencing)
create jobs row (status requested)

create job_events row (job_created)

create ledger HOLD row (credit_ledger)

Emits
job.created

credits.hold.created

Notifications
optional: “Booking created” to client

Implementation skeleton

export default async function handler(req: Request) {
  const body = await req.json();
  const actor = await getActorFromCookie(req); // your auth helper
  const idKey = req.headers.get("Idempotency-Key");

  const requestHash = await hashJson({ body, actorId: actor.id });
  const gate = await idempotencyGate({ key: idKey, userId: actor.id, endpoint: "POST /jobs", requestHash });
  if (!gate.ok) return json(gate.error, gate.status);
  if (gate.replay) return json(gate.response, 200);

  try {
    // 1) validations
    assert(actor.role === "client", "FORBIDDEN");
    assert(new Date(body.scheduled_start_at) < new Date(body.scheduled_end_at), "VALIDATION_ERROR");

    // 2) compute available credits
    const available = await computeAvailableCredits(actor.id);

    assert(available >= body.credit_amount, "INSUFFICIENT_CREDITS");

    // 3) create job
    const job = await base44.entities.jobs.create({
      client_id: actor.id,
      status: "requested",
      scheduled_start_at: body.scheduled_start_at,
      scheduled_end_at: body.scheduled_end_at,
      address: body.address,
      latitude: body.latitude,
      longitude: body.longitude,
      credit_amount: body.credit_amount,
      client_notes: body.client_notes ?? null,
    });

    // 4) job event
    await base44.entities.job_events.create({
      job_id: job.id,
      type: "job_created",
      payload: {},
    });

    // 5) hold credits
    await base44.entities.credit_ledger.create({
      user_id: actor.id,
      job_id: job.id,
      delta_credits: -body.credit_amount,
      reason: "hold_for_job",
    });

    const response = { job, credits: { held: body.credit_amount } };

    await emitEvent("job.created", {
      actor: { type: "client", id: actor.id },
      job_id: job.id,
      idempotency_key: idKey,
      payload: { credit_amount: body.credit_amount },
      fanoutToN8n: false,
    });

    await emitEvent("credits.hold.created", {
      actor: { type: "client", id: actor.id },
      job_id: job.id,
      idempotency_key: idKey,
      payload: { delta_credits: -body.credit_amount, reason: "hold_for_job" },
      fanoutToN8n: false,
    });

    await idempotencyComplete(idKey!, response);
    return json(response, 200);
  } catch (e) {
    await idempotencyFail(idKey!, { error: String(e) }).catch(() => {});
    return json({ error: { code: "INTERNAL_ERROR", message: "Failed to create job" } }, 500);
  }
}

Yep — here’s a clean, complete Admin system for PureTask that fits Base44’s strengths (internal ops + rules + workflows), stays lean for V1, and maps directly to your job/credits/disputes/stripe/events architecture.

I’ll describe:

Admin roles + permissions

Admin navigation (modules)

Exact pages (V1) with purpose + actions + data shown

What workflows each page triggers

What to build first (so it’s actually usable)

1) Admin roles for PureTask (simple V1)
Admin (Ops)
Can view/modify jobs

Can resolve disputes

Can adjust credits (controlled)

Can message users (templated)

Finance Admin
Read-only on jobs

Can process refunds/chargebacks

Can view payouts, revenue, ledger, Stripe events

Trust & Safety
Can view risk flags

Can suspend cleaners/clients

Can review incidents + disputes

Super Admin
Full permissions including config changes

Implementation tip: In Base44, implement a admin_roles table and a simple “gate” function used in every admin workflow.

2) Admin system navigation (Base44 sidebar)
Core modules (V1):

Dashboard

Jobs Console

Disputes

Users (Clients / Cleaners)

Credits & Ledger

Payments (Stripe)

Notifications Log

Event Log / Audit

Config (Super Admin only)

3) Admin pages (V1) — what each page does
A) Admin Dashboard
Goal: “What needs attention today?”

Widgets

Active jobs today

Jobs awaiting approval (stuck)

Open disputes

Failed notifications

Stripe webhook failures / unprocessed events

Risk flags count (if enabled)

Primary actions

Jump into Jobs Console filtered views

Data sources

jobs + job_events

disputes

notification_failures

stripe_events

B) Jobs Console
This is your “mission control.”

Table columns

Job ID

Status (requested/accepted/on_my_way/in_progress/awaiting_approval/completed/disputed/cancelled)

Client

Cleaner

Scheduled time

Location

Credits held

Last event timestamp

Flags (late, dispute, missing photos)

Filters

Status

Date range

Cleaner id / Client id

“Awaiting approval > 6 hours”

“In progress > X hours”

“Disputed”

“Missing after photos”

Row actions

View Job Detail

Force cancel (with reason)

Reassign cleaner (if your model allows)

Trigger “Resend notifications”

Create dispute (rare, admin-initiated)

Mark job “needs review”

Workflows triggered

job.cancel (admin initiated)

job.status.update (only if you allow admin to force transitions)

notify.client.job_updates (resend)

alerts.raise_and_route (flag)

C) Job Detail (Admin View)
This is where admins actually solve problems.

Sections

Summary (status, schedule, addresses, client/cleaner)

Timeline (from job_events)

Proof (before/after photos)

Credits (ledger entries for this job)

Messages (thread tied to job)

Actions panel (admin-only)

Actions panel (safe V1 set)

Add internal note

Resend messages/notifications

Open dispute

Resolve dispute (refund / no refund)

Release hold manually (rare, super admin only)

Lock job (prevent further transitions) (optional)

Workflows triggered

job.dispute.open

job.dispute.resolve_refund

job.dispute.resolve_no_refund

refund.process (n8n)

messages.send (templated)

analytics.capture_event (admin actions)

Views

Actions

alerts.raise_and_route (if repeated failures)

J) Event Log / Audit
Goal: “Reconstruct what happened.”

Data

job_events

/events bus stored logs (if you store events)

admin action events (recommended)

Actions

View event payload

Replay event (super admin only, very carefully)

Workflows

analytics.capture_event

events.replay (optional; later)

K) System Config (Super Admin only)
Goal: “Change thresholds without code deploy.”

Config items (V1):

credit hold buffer %

max dispute window hours

min photo count before completion

SLA thresholds (awaiting approval > X)

notification templates toggles

Store in a system_config table.

Workflows

config.update

emits config.changed

4) What to build first (practical order)
If you build these 5 things, you’ll have a real admin system:

Jobs Console

Job Detail (Admin)

Disputes Inbox

Credits & Ledger Console

Stripe Events Feed

Everything else can come after.

5) Base44 implementation notes (so it’s easy)
Use “Admin views” as read-only + action buttons
Tables + filters are Base44’s sweet spot

Action buttons trigger Deno workflows:

cancel job

resolve dispute

resend notifications

manual credit adjustment (gated)

Every admin action must emit an audit event
Write a row to a simple admin_audit_log table:

admin_id

action_type

target_type/job_id/user_id

payload

timestamp

This prevents “mystery changes.”

Locked ✅ — here is the Locked Admin V1 Spec for PureTask in Base44 (pages, columns, filters, actions, workflows, permissions, audit requirements). This is what you build and don’t deviate from until V1 ships.

PureTask Admin V1 Spec
Admin V1 goals
See what’s happening today

Resolve disputes fast

Intervene in jobs safely

Audit credits + Stripe without guessing

Never break money/state (idempotency + audit on every admin action)

1) Roles & permissions (V1)
Roles
Ops Admin

Finance Admin

Trust & Safety

Super Admin

Permission matrix (truth table)
Capability	Ops	Finance	Trust/Safety	Super Admin
View jobs + job detail	✅	✅	✅	✅
Resend notifications	✅	✅	✅	✅
Cancel job (pre-start)	✅	❌	✅	✅
Force transition (dangerous)	❌	❌	❌	✅
View credits ledger	✅	✅	✅	✅
Manual credit adjust	❌	✅ (refund only)	❌	✅
View Stripe events/intents	✅	✅	✅	✅
Trigger refund	❌	✅	❌	✅
Resolve dispute	✅	✅	✅	✅
Suspend user	❌	❌	✅	✅
Change system config	❌	❌	❌	✅
Rule: any action that changes ledger/state requires:

Idempotency-Key (admin action id)

Admin audit log entry

A) Dashboard

“Disputes: Open”

“Notifications: Failed”

“Stripe: Unprocessed”

No write actions on dashboard.

4) Admin workflows (names + triggers + required inputs)
Job actions
admin.job.cancel

input: { job_id, reason }

admin.job.force_transition (Super Admin)

input: { job_id, event_type, payload }

admin.job.add_note

input: { job_id, note }

Disputes
admin.dispute.open

input: { job_id, type, note }

admin.dispute.resolve_refund

input: { dispute_id, refund_credits, note }

admin.dispute.resolve_no_refund

input: { dispute_id, note }

Users
admin.user.suspend

input: { user_id, reason }

admin.user.unsuspend

input: { user_id }

admin.cleaner.set_tier (Super Admin)

input: { cleaner_id, tier, note }

Credits
admin.credits.adjust (Finance/Super Admin)

input: { user_id, delta_credits, reason, note }

writes ledger entry + emits credits.adjusted.admin

Notifications
admin.notify.resend_job_status

input: { job_id }

admin.notify.resend

input: { failure_id }

admin.notify.mark_resolved

input: { failure_id }

Stripe
admin.stripe.reprocess_event

input: { stripe_event_id } → calls n8n

admin.refund.process

input: { payment_intent_id, amount_usd|credits } → calls n8n

Config
admin.config.update

input: { key, value }

5) Non-negotiables for Admin actions
Every Admin action must:
pass role gate

write to admin_audit_log

be idempotent (use Idempotency-Key or an action_id)

emit canonical event to /events and (if external) /n8n/events

yes

Great — here are the exact Base44 page specs for Admin V1: for each page you’ll get

Entity query (primary table + joins)

Filters (exact fields + operators)

Columns (exact)

Row click behavior

Action buttons (workflow + payload)

Permissions (role gates)

Notes (computed fields / helpful views)

I’m assuming your Base44 Entities map 1:1 to Neon tables (e.g. jobs, job_events, disputes, credit_ledger, stripe_events, payment_intents, notification_failures, users, cleaner_profiles, client_profiles). If any entity name differs in Base44, just rename in-place.

Base44 Admin V1 Page Specs
Global Admin UX rules
Sidebar sections as locked earlier.

Default filter state: last 7 days (where applicable).

Row click opens a detail page (Job/Dispute/User).

All write actions must require an Admin Action ID (Idempotency-Key) auto-generated in UI and passed to workflow:

payload includes action_id: uuid

Every workflow writes to admin_audit_log.

1) Dashboard Page
Data blocks (each is a query widget)
Widget A: Jobs Today by status
Entity: jobs

Filter: scheduled_start_at between start/end of today

Group by: status

Display: counts

Widget B: Awaiting Approval > X hours
Entity: jobs

Filter: status = 'awaiting_approval' AND updated_at < now() - interval 'X hours' (or based on last job_event timestamp)

Display: count + link to Jobs Console with filter applied

Widget C: Open disputes
Entity: disputes

Filter: status = 'open'

Display: count + link to Disputes Inbox

Widget D: Failed notifications (24h)
Entity: notification_failures

Filter: created_at > now() - 24h AND resolved = false

Display: count + link

Widget E: Stripe events unprocessed
Entity: stripe_events

Filter: processed = false

Display: count + link

No actions on dashboard.

2) Jobs Console Page
Primary query
Entity: jobs

Joins:

users as client (jobs.client_id → users.id)

users as cleaner (jobs.cleaner_id → users.id) (if cleaner_id is user_id; else join cleaner_profiles then users)

optional: cleaner_profiles (cleaner_id → cleaner_profiles.user_id)

Default filter
scheduled_start_at >= now() - 7 days

Filters (exact)
status (multi-select)

scheduled_start_at date range

client_id (text exact)

cleaner_id (text exact)

Flags (multi-select):

is_disputed

awaiting_approval_gt_sla

in_progress_gt_threshold

missing_after_photos

has_notification_failures

Flag computation (how Base44 should compute)
If Base44 supports computed fields: create “views”; if not, implement in UI using secondary queries:

is_disputed: jobs.status = 'disputed'

awaiting_approval_gt_sla: status awaiting_approval AND last_event_at < now - SLA

in_progress_gt_threshold: status in_progress AND started_at < now - threshold

missing_after_photos: after photo count < config MIN_AFTER_PHOTOS

has_notification_failures: exists notification_failures where job_id = jobs.id and resolved=false

Columns (exact)
id (Job ID)

status (badge)

scheduled_start_at

scheduled_end_at

client.name + client_id

cleaner.name + cleaner_id (or Unassigned)

address (truncate)

credit_amount

last_event_at (derived: latest job_events timestamp)

flags (icons)

Row click
Open Job Detail (Admin) with job_id

Row actions (buttons)
Action 1: Resend status notification
Workflow: admin.notify.resend_job_status

Payload:

{ "action_id":"<uuid>", "job_id":"<job_id>" }
Permissions: Ops, Finance, Trust/Safety, Super Admin

Action 2: Cancel job (pre-start)
Workflow: admin.job.cancel

Payload:

{ "action_id":"<uuid>", "job_id":"<job_id>", "reason":"<text>" }
Permissions: Ops, Trust/Safety, Super Admin

Guard: status in requested|accepted|on_my_way

Action 3: Open dispute
Workflow: admin.dispute.open

Payload:

{ "action_id":"<uuid>", "job_id":"<job_id>", "type":"<enum>", "note":"<text>" }
Permissions: Ops, Finance, Trust/Safety, Super Admin

Action 4: View Ledger
Navigation: Credits & Ledger page with filter job_id=<job_id>

Super Admin only: Force transition
Workflow: admin.job.force_transition

Payload:

{ "action_id":"<uuid>", "job_id":"<job_id>", "event_type":"<allowed>", "payload":{} }
3) Job Detail (Admin)
Inputs
job_id route param

Queries (tabs)
Tab A: Overview
jobs.get(job_id)

Client lookup: users.get(jobs.client_id)

Cleaner lookup: users.get(jobs.cleaner_id) + cleaner_profiles.get(cleaner_id) if exists

Display:

job summary fields

client summary + quick link

cleaner summary + quick link

Tab B: Timeline
Entity: job_events

Filter: job_id = <job_id>

Sort: created_at desc
Columns:

created_at

type

payload preview (expandable)

Tab C: Proof
Entity: your photos entity/table

Filter: job_id = <job_id>

Group by: kind=before|after

Show grid and counts

Tab D: Credits
Entity: credit_ledger

Filter: job_id = <job_id>

Sort: created_at asc
Columns:

created_at

reason

delta_credits

user_id

ledger_id

Tab E: Messages
Entity: messages table (job thread)

Filter: job_id = <job_id>

Sort: created_at asc
Action: send templated message → workflow below

Action panel (buttons)
Add internal note
Workflow: admin.job.add_note

Payload:

{ "action_id":"<uuid>", "job_id":"<job_id>", "note":"<text>" }
Permission: all admin roles

Resend notifications
Workflow: admin.notify.resend_job_status

Payload: { "action_id":"<uuid>", "job_id":"<job_id>" }

Cancel job
Workflow: admin.job.cancel

Payload: { "action_id":"<uuid>", "job_id":"<job_id>", "reason":"<text>" }

Guard as above

Open dispute
Workflow: admin.dispute.open

Resolve dispute (Refund)
Workflow: admin.dispute.resolve_refund

Payload:

{ "action_id":"<uuid>", "dispute_id":"<id>", "refund_credits": <number>, "note":"<text>" }
Permission: Ops, Finance, Trust/Safety, Super Admin

Resolve dispute (No refund)
Workflow: admin.dispute.resolve_no_refund

Payload:

{ "action_id":"<uuid>", "dispute_id":"<id>", "note":"<text>" }
Send templated message
Workflow: admin.messages.send_template

Payload:

{ "action_id":"<uuid>", "job_id":"<job_id>", "to":"client|cleaner", "template":"<key>", "vars":{} }

8) Credits & Ledger Console

Part 1 — Admin workflow code stubs (Base44 Deno Deploy)
Assumptions / Entities

Shared helpers (copy into /_shared.ts)
import { base44 } from "@/base44.ts";

type Role = "ops" | "finance" | "trust_safety" | "super_admin";
type ActorType = "admin" | "system";

export function json(body: unknown, status = 200) {
  return new Response(JSON.stringify(body), {
    status,
    headers: { "Content-Type": "application/json" },
  });
}

export function assert(cond: unknown, code: string, message?: string): asserts cond {
  if (!cond) throw Object.assign(new Error(message ?? code), { code });
}

export async function getAdminActor(req: Request) {
  // Implement using your session/cookie auth context.
  // Base44 usually gives you a current user context; if not, parse cookie and verify.
  const user = (req as any).user ?? null; // replace
  assert(user, "UNAUTHORIZED", "Not logged in");
  assert(user.role && user.role.startsWith("admin"), "FORBIDDEN", "Not an admin");
  return {
    id: user.id as string,
    role: user.admin_role as Role, // ops/finance/trust_safety/super_admin
    type: "admin" as ActorType,
  };
}

export function requireRole(actor: { role: Role }, allowed: Role[]) {
  assert(allowed.includes(actor.role), "FORBIDDEN", "Insufficient admin role");
}

/** Hash request payload for idempotency comparisons */
export async function hashJson(input: unknown): Promise<string> {
  const bytes = new TextEncoder().encode(JSON.stringify(input));
  const digest = await crypto.subtle.digest("SHA-256", bytes);
  return Array.from(new Uint8Array(digest)).map((b) => b.toString(16).padStart(2, "0")).join("");
}

// ---- Idempotency (admin actions) ----
export async function idempotencyGate(opts: {
  key: string | null;
  adminId: string;
  endpoint: string;
  requestHash: string;
}) {
  const { key, adminId, endpoint, requestHash } = opts;
  assert(key, "IDEMPOTENCY_REQUIRED", "Missing Idempotency-Key (action_id)");

  const existing = await base44.entities.idempotency_keys.get(key!).catch(() => null);
  if (existing) {
    if (existing.endpoint !== endpoint || existing.user_id !== adminId) {
      throw Object.assign(new Error("Idempotency key conflict"), { code: "IDEMPOTENCY_CONFLICT" });
    }
    if (existing.request_hash !== requestHash) {
      throw Object.assign(new Error("Idempotency key reused with different payload"), { code: "IDEMPOTENCY_CONFLICT" });
    }
    if (existing.status === "completed" && existing.response_json) {
      return { replay: true, response: existing.response_json };
    }
  }

  await base44.entities.idempotency_keys.create({
    idempotency_key: key!,
    user_id: adminId,
    endpoint,
    request_hash: requestHash,
    status: "processing",
    response_json: null,
  });

  return { replay: false, response: null };
}

export async function idempotencyComplete(key: string, responseJson: unknown) {
  await base44.entities.idempotency_keys.update(key, {
    status: "completed",
    response_json: responseJson,
  });
}
export async function idempotencyFail(key: string, errorJson: unknown) {
  await base44.entities.idempotency_keys.update(key, {
    status: "failed",
    response_json: errorJson,
  });
}

// ---- Audit log (mandatory) ----
export async function auditLog(opts: {
  action_id: string;
  admin_id: string;
  action: string;
  target_type: "job" | "dispute" | "user" | "ledger" | "config" | "stripe" | "notification";
  target_id: string;
  payload: Record<string, unknown>;
}) {
  await base44.entities.admin_audit_log.create({
    id: opts.action_id,
    admin_id: opts.admin_id,
    action: opts.action,
    target_type: opts.target_type,
    target_id: opts.target_id,
    payload: opts.payload,
    created_at: new Date().toISOString(),
  });
}

// ---- Canonical event emitter ----
export async function emitEvent(name: string, data: {
  actor: { type: "admin" | "system"; id: string };
  job_id?: string | null;
  idempotency_key?: string | null;
  payload?: Record<string, unknown>;
  fanoutToN8n?: boolean;
}) {
  const event = {
    event_id: crypto.randomUUID(),
    occurred_at: new Date().toISOString(),
    name,
    actor: data.actor,
    job_id: data.job_id ?? null,
    idempotency_key: data.idempotency_key ?? null,
    payload: data.payload ?? {},
  };

  // Store in Neon for unified tracking (Deliverable “track everything”)
  await base44.entities.observability_events.create({
    event_id: event.event_id,
    occurred_at: event.occurred_at,
    name: event.name,
    actor_type: event.actor.type,
    actor_id: event.actor.id,
    job_id: event.job_id,
    idempotency_key: event.idempotency_key,
    payload: event.payload,
    source: "base44",
  });

  // Optional: also post to your internal API bridges if you want
  // await fetch(`${Deno.env.get("API_BASE_URL")}/events`, { ... })

  if (data.fanoutToN8n) {
    await fetch(Deno.env.get("N8N_EVENTS_URL")!, {
      method: "POST",
      headers: { "Content-Type": "application/json", "X-Signature": Deno.env.get("N8N_HMAC")! },
      body: JSON.stringify(event),
    });
  }

  return event;
}

export function toErrorResponse(err: any) {
  const code = err?.code ?? "INTERNAL_ERROR";
  const status =
    code === "UNAUTHORIZED" ? 401 :
    code === "FORBIDDEN" ? 403 :
    code === "NOT_FOUND" ? 404 :
    code === "VALIDATION_ERROR" ? 400 :
    code === "CSRF_REQUIRED" ? 403 :
    code === "IDEMPOTENCY_REQUIRED" ? 400 :
    code === "IDEMPOTENCY_CONFLICT" ? 409 :
    code === "INVALID_STATE" ? 409 :
    500;

  return json({ error: { code, message: err?.message ?? "Error" } }, status);
}
1) admin.job.cancel (Ops / Trust&Safety / SuperAdmin)
/workflows/admin_job_cancel.ts

import { base44 } from "@/base44.ts";
import {
  json, toErrorResponse, getAdminActor, requireRole,
  idempotencyGate, idempotencyComplete, idempotencyFail,
  auditLog, emitEvent, hashJson, assert
} from "./_shared.ts";

export default async function handler(req: Request) {
  const actor = await getAdminActor(req);
  requireRole(actor, ["ops", "trust_safety", "super_admin"]);

  const body = await req.json(); // { action_id, job_id, reason }
  const actionId = body.action_id || req.headers.get("Idempotency-Key");
  const endpoint = "admin.job.cancel";
  const requestHash = await hashJson({ body, actor: actor.id });

  try {
    const gate = await idempotencyGate({ key: actionId, adminId: actor.id, endpoint, requestHash });
    if (gate.replay) return json(gate.response, 200);

    assert(body.job_id, "VALIDATION_ERROR", "Missing job_id");
    assert(body.reason, "VALIDATION_ERROR", "Missing reason");

    const job = await base44.entities.jobs.get(body.job_id).catch(() => null);
    assert(job, "NOT_FOUND", "Job not found");

    // Guard: only cancel pre-start for V1
    const allowed = ["requested", "accepted", "on_my_way"];
    assert(allowed.includes(job.status), "INVALID_STATE", `Cannot cancel job in status ${job.status}`);

    // Update job + event
    await base44.entities.jobs.update(job.id, { status: "cancelled" });
    await base44.entities.job_events.create({
      job_id: job.id,
      type: "job_cancelled",
      payload: { reason: body.reason, by: "admin", admin_id: actor.id },
    });

    // Release hold (ledger reversal). We assume HOLD exists; if not, still succeed.
    // Strategy: Insert release entry (append-only).
    await base44.entities.credit_ledger.create({
      user_id: job.client_id,
      job_id: job.id,
      delta_credits: Math.abs(job.credit_amount),
      reason: "hold_released_on_cancel",
    }).catch(() => null);

    await auditLog({
      action_id: actionId,
      admin_id: actor.id,
      action: "admin.job.cancel",
      target_type: "job",
      target_id: job.id,
      payload: { reason: body.reason },
    });

    await emitEvent("job.cancelled", {
      actor: { type: "admin", id: actor.id },
      job_id: job.id,
      idempotency_key: actionId,
      payload: { reason: body.reason },
      fanoutToN8n: true, // so n8n can notify client/cleaner
    });

    await emitEvent("credits.hold.released", {
      actor: { type: "admin", id: actor.id },
      job_id: job.id,
      idempotency_key: actionId,
      payload: { user_id: job.client_id, delta_credits: Math.abs(job.credit_amount), reason: "hold_released_on_cancel" },
      fanoutToN8n: false,
    });

    const response = { ok: true, job_id: job.id, status: "cancelled" };
    await idempotencyComplete(actionId, response);
    return json(response, 200);
  } catch (err) {
    if (actionId) await idempotencyFail(actionId, { error: String(err) }).catch(() => {});
    return toErrorResponse(err);
  }
}
2) admin.dispute.open
/workflows/admin_dispute_open.ts

import { base44 } from "@/base44.ts";
import {
  json, toErrorResponse, getAdminActor, requireRole,
  idempotencyGate, idempotencyComplete, idempotencyFail,
  auditLog, emitEvent, hashJson, assert
} from "./_shared.ts";

export default async function handler(req: Request) {
  const actor = await getAdminActor(req);
  requireRole(actor, ["ops", "finance", "trust_safety", "super_admin"]);

  const body = await req.json(); // { action_id, job_id, type, note }
  const actionId = body.action_id || req.headers.get("Idempotency-Key");
  const endpoint = "admin.dispute.open";
  const requestHash = await hashJson({ body, actor: actor.id });

  try {
    const gate = await idempotencyGate({ key: actionId, adminId: actor.id, endpoint, requestHash });
    if (gate.replay) return json(gate.response, 200);

    assert(body.job_id, "VALIDATION_ERROR", "Missing job_id");
    assert(body.type, "VALIDATION_ERROR", "Missing dispute type");

    const job = await base44.entities.jobs.get(body.job_id).catch(() => null);
    assert(job, "NOT_FOUND", "Job not found");

    // Prevent duplicate open disputes
    const existing = await base44.entities.disputes.findMany({
      where: { job_id: job.id, status: "open" },
      limit: 1,
    }).catch(() => []);
    assert(!existing?.length, "CONFLICT", "Dispute already open for this job");

    const dispute = await base44.entities.disputes.create({
      job_id: job.id,
      client_id: job.client_id,
      cleaner_id: job.cleaner_id ?? null,
      status: "open",
      type: body.type,
      note: body.note ?? null,
      created_at: new Date().toISOString(),
    });

    await base44.entities.jobs.update(job.id, { status: "disputed" });
    await base44.entities.job_events.create({
      job_id: job.id,
      type: "client_disputed",
      payload: { by: "admin", admin_id: actor.id, type: body.type, note: body.note ?? null },
    });

    await auditLog({
      action_id: actionId,
      admin_id: actor.id,
      action: "admin.dispute.open",
      target_type: "dispute",
      target_id: dispute.id,
      payload: { job_id: job.id, type: body.type, note: body.note ?? null },
    });

    await emitEvent("job.disputed", {
      actor: { type: "admin", id: actor.id },
      job_id: job.id,
      idempotency_key: actionId,
      payload: { dispute_id: dispute.id, type: body.type },
      fanoutToN8n: true,
    });

    const response = { ok: true, dispute_id: dispute.id, job_id: job.id };
    await idempotencyComplete(actionId, response);
    return json(response, 200);
  } catch (err) {
    if (actionId) await idempotencyFail(actionId, { error: String(err) }).catch(() => {});
    return toErrorResponse(err);
  }
}
3) admin.dispute.resolve_refund
/workflows/admin_dispute_resolve_refund.ts

import { base44 } from "@/base44.ts";
import {
  json, toErrorResponse, getAdminActor, requireRole,
  idempotencyGate, idempotencyComplete, idempotencyFail,
  auditLog, emitEvent, hashJson, assert
} from "./_shared.ts";

export default async function handler(req: Request) {
  const actor = await getAdminActor(req);
  requireRole(actor, ["ops", "finance", "trust_safety", "super_admin"]);

  const body = await req.json(); // { action_id, dispute_id, refund_credits, note }
  const actionId = body.action_id || req.headers.get("Idempotency-Key");
  const endpoint = "admin.dispute.resolve_refund";
  const requestHash = await hashJson({ body, actor: actor.id });

  try {
    const gate = await idempotencyGate({ key: actionId, adminId: actor.id, endpoint, requestHash });
    if (gate.replay) return json(gate.response, 200);

    assert(body.dispute_id, "VALIDATION_ERROR", "Missing dispute_id");
    assert(typeof body.refund_credits === "number" && body.refund_credits >= 0, "VALIDATION_ERROR", "Invalid refund_credits");

    const dispute = await base44.entities.disputes.get(body.dispute_id).catch(() => null);
    assert(dispute, "NOT_FOUND", "Dispute not found");
    assert(dispute.status === "open", "INVALID_STATE", "Dispute not open");

    const job = await base44.entities.jobs.get(dispute.job_id).catch(() => null);
    assert(job, "NOT_FOUND", "Job not found");

    // Append-only ledger refund
    if (body.refund_credits > 0) {
      await base44.entities.credit_ledger.create({
        user_id: dispute.client_id,
        job_id: job.id,
        delta_credits: body.refund_credits,
        reason: "dispute_refund",
      });
    }

    await base44.entities.disputes.update(dispute.id, {
      status: "resolved_refund",
      resolved_at: new Date().toISOString(),
      resolution_note: body.note ?? null,
      resolved_by_admin_id: actor.id,
    });

    await base44.entities.job_events.create({
      job_id: job.id,
      type: "dispute_resolved_refund",
      payload: { refund_credits: body.refund_credits, note: body.note ?? null, admin_id: actor.id },
    });

    await base44.entities.jobs.update(job.id, { status: "completed" });

    await auditLog({
      action_id: actionId,
      admin_id: actor.id,
      action: "admin.dispute.resolve_refund",
      target_type: "dispute",
      target_id: dispute.id,
      payload: { refund_credits: body.refund_credits, note: body.note ?? null, job_id: job.id },
    });

    await emitEvent("job.dispute_resolved.refund", {
      actor: { type: "admin", id: actor.id },
      job_id: job.id,
      idempotency_key: actionId,
      payload: { dispute_id: dispute.id, refund_credits: body.refund_credits },
      fanoutToN8n: true,
    });

    if (body.refund_credits > 0) {
      await emitEvent("credits.refund.issued", {
        actor: { type: "admin", id: actor.id },
        job_id: job.id,
        idempotency_key: actionId,
        payload: { user_id: dispute.client_id, delta_credits: body.refund_credits, reason: "dispute_refund" },
        fanoutToN8n: false,
      });
    }

    // If you ever refund fiat: call n8n here (optional)
    // await fetch(N8N_REFUND_URL, ...)

    const response = { ok: true, dispute_id: dispute.id, job_id: job.id, refund_credits: body.refund_credits };
    await idempotencyComplete(actionId, response);
    return json(response, 200);
  } catch (err) {
    if (actionId) await idempotencyFail(actionId, { error: String(err) }).catch(() => {});
    return toErrorResponse(err);
  }
}

6) admin.credits.adjust (Finance / SuperAdmin only)
/workflows/admin_credits_adjust.ts

import { base44 } from "@/base44.ts";
import {
  json, toErrorResponse, getAdminActor, requireRole,
  idempotencyGate, idempotencyComplete, idempotencyFail,
  auditLog, emitEvent, hashJson, assert
} from "./_shared.ts";

export default async function handler(req: Request) {
  const actor = await getAdminActor(req);
  requireRole(actor, ["finance", "super_admin"]);

  const body = await req.json(); // { action_id, user_id, delta_credits, reason, note }
  const actionId = body.action_id || req.headers.get("Idempotency-Key");
  const endpoint = "admin.credits.adjust";
  const requestHash = await hashJson({ body, actor: actor.id });

  try {
    const gate = await idempotencyGate({ key: actionId, adminId: actor.id, endpoint, requestHash });
    if (gate.replay) return json(gate.response, 200);

    assert(body.user_id, "VALIDATION_ERROR", "Missing user_id");
    assert(typeof body.delta_credits === "number" && body.delta_credits !== 0, "VALIDATION_ERROR", "Invalid delta_credits");
    assert(body.reason, "VALIDATION_ERROR", "Missing reason");

    const user = await base44.entities.users.get(body.user_id).catch(() => null);
    assert(user, "NOT_FOUND", "User not found");

    // Append-only ledger entry
    const entry = await base44.entities.credit_ledger.create({
      user_id: user.id,
      job_id: null,
      delta_credits: body.delta_credits,
      reason: "admin_adjustment",
      meta: { reason: body.reason, note: body.note ?? null, admin_id: actor.id },
    });

    await auditLog({
      action_id: actionId,
      admin_id: actor.id,
      action: "admin.credits.adjust",
      target_type: "ledger",
      target_id: entry.id,
      payload: { user_id: user.id, delta_credits: body.delta_credits, reason: body.reason, note: body.note ?? null },
    });

    await emitEvent("credits.adjusted.admin", {
      actor: { type: "admin", id: actor.id },
      job_id: null,
      idempotency_key: actionId,
      payload: { user_id: user.id, delta_credits: body.delta_credits, reason: body.reason },
      fanoutToN8n: false,
    });

    const response = { ok: true, ledger_id: entry.id };
    await idempotencyComplete(actionId, response);
    return json(response, 200);
  } catch (err) {
    if (actionId) await idempotencyFail(actionId, { error: String(err) }).catch(() => {});
    return toErrorResponse(err);
  }
}
7) admin.user.suspend / admin.user.unsuspend (Trust&Safety / SuperAdmin)
(Stub: set users.status = suspended|active, log, emit)

admin_user_suspend.ts

admin_user_unsuspend.ts

8) admin.cleaner.set_tier (SuperAdmin)
(Stub: update cleaner_profiles.tier, emit tier.changed)

9) admin.stripe.reprocess_event (Finance / SuperAdmin)
(Stub: emit event to n8n to reprocess stripe_event_id)

10) admin.config.update (SuperAdmin)
(Stub: update system_config, emit config.changed)

If you want, I’ll output those remaining stubs too — but the pattern above is identical and you can replicate quickly.

Part 2 — Track anything/everything across Base44 + Lovable + n8n + Neon
You want one unified “truth timeline” for every job/user/payment across all platforms. The best way is a central observability event store + correlation IDs + consistent logging from every system.

The “single pane of glass” design
1) Add a central table in Neon: observability_events
Expose it as a Base44 entity so Base44 can write to it too.

observability_events

event_id (uuid pk)

occurred_at (timestamptz)

source (lovable|base44|n8n|api|neon|stripe)

name (string; canonical event name)

severity (debug|info|warn|error)

actor_type (client|cleaner|admin|system)

actor_id (text nullable)

job_id (text nullable)

user_id (text nullable)

trace_id (text) ✅

span_id (text nullable)

idempotency_key (text nullable)

request_id (text nullable)

payload (jsonb)

Why this works: every platform can log to one place, and then Base44 Admin can show a timeline and filters instantly.

2) Require 3 IDs everywhere (this is the magic)
trace_id: generated at the start of any user action in Lovable

request_id: generated per API request (or reuse trace_id + counter)

idempotency_key: for critical writes / admin actions

Propagation rules

Lovable → sends headers on every API call:

X-Trace-Id, X-Request-Id, plus Idempotency when needed

Express API → forwards same IDs into Base44 workflow calls and into /n8n/events

Base44 workflows → log into observability_events with same trace_id

n8n → every workflow run logs start/end to observability_events with same trace_id

Neon → for critical tables, add DB triggers (optional) to log inserts to observability (advanced)

3) Instrumentation per platform
Lovable (frontend)
Create a tiny logger:

on every screen view: ui.screen_viewed

on every button click: ui.action_clicked

on every API request start/end: ui.api_request.started|completed|failed

Send to API endpoint: POST /events/ui (or directly to Base44 if you want)

Base44
In every workflow: call emitEvent() (we included it) + write observability_events

On errors: write severity error with stack + payload

n8n
Add 2 nodes to every workflow:

“Log Start” → HTTP POST to POST /events/n8n

“Log End” → HTTP POST to POST /events/n8n

Include:

workflow_name, execution_id, status, duration_ms, error

Neon (optional but powerful)
Add db triggers on:

jobs updates to status

credit_ledger inserts

disputes inserts/updates

Each trigger inserts a row into observability_events
This gives you “ground truth” even if apps fail to log.

4) Build a “Unified Timeline” page in Base44 Admin
Filters:

job_id

trace_id

user_id

source

severity

time range

This becomes your “black box flight recorder”.

create the actually table and information i need to paste into neon

Here’s paste-ready Postgres SQL you can run in Neon to add the missing “ops/admin/observability” tables we designed:

✅ observability_events (track everything across Lovable/Base44/n8n/API/Stripe)

✅ admin_audit_log (every admin action, immutable)

✅ idempotency_keys (replay safety for critical writes + admin actions)

✅ system_config (change thresholds without redeploy)

✅ Useful indexes (so the admin dashboards are fast)

Copy/paste this whole block into Neon SQL editor and run.

-- =========================================
-- PureTask Ops / Admin / Observability Tables
-- =========================================

BEGIN;

-- 1) Idempotency keys (critical writes + admin actions)
CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS idempotency_keys (
  idempotency_key TEXT PRIMARY KEY,
  user_id         TEXT NOT NULL,
  endpoint        TEXT NOT NULL,         -- e.g. "POST /jobs" or "admin.job.cancel"
  request_hash    TEXT NOT NULL,         -- sha256 of canonical request payload
  status          TEXT NOT NULL CHECK (status IN ('processing','completed','failed')),
  response_json   JSONB,
  created_at      TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT now(),
  updated_at      TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT now()
);

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_idempotency_keys_user_endpoint_created
  ON idempotency_keys (user_id, endpoint, created_at DESC);

-- Auto-update updated_at
CREATE OR REPLACE FUNCTION set_updated_at()
RETURNS TRIGGER AS $$
BEGIN
  NEW.updated_at = now();
  RETURN NEW;
END;
$$ LANGUAGE plpgsql;

DROP TRIGGER IF EXISTS trg_idempotency_keys_updated_at ON idempotency_keys;
CREATE TRIGGER trg_idempotency_keys_updated_at
BEFORE UPDATE ON idempotency_keys
FOR EACH ROW EXECUTE FUNCTION set_updated_at();


-- 2) Admin audit log (immutable)
CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS admin_audit_log (
  id          UUID PRIMARY KEY,          -- use action_id / Idempotency-Key uuid
  admin_id    TEXT NOT NULL,
  action      TEXT NOT NULL,             -- e.g. "admin.job.cancel"
  target_type TEXT NOT NULL CHECK (target_type IN ('job','dispute','user','ledger','config','stripe','notification')),
  target_id   TEXT NOT NULL,
  payload     JSONB NOT NULL DEFAULT '{}'::jsonb,
  created_at  TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT now()
);

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_admin_audit_log_created
  ON admin_audit_log (created_at DESC);

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_admin_audit_log_admin_created
  ON admin_audit_log (admin_id, created_at DESC);

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_admin_audit_log_target
  ON admin_audit_log (target_type, target_id, created_at DESC);

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_admin_audit_log_action
  ON admin_audit_log (action, created_at DESC);


-- 3) System config (editable by Super Admin; everything else reads)
CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS system_config (
  key         TEXT PRIMARY KEY,
  value       JSONB NOT NULL,
  description TEXT,
  updated_by  TEXT,
  updated_at  TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT now(),
  created_at  TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT now()
);

DROP TRIGGER IF EXISTS trg_system_config_updated_at ON system_config;
CREATE TRIGGER trg_system_config_updated_at
BEFORE UPDATE ON system_config
FOR EACH ROW EXECUTE FUNCTION set_updated_at();

-- Seed V1 config defaults (safe to re-run)
INSERT INTO system_config (key, value, description)
VALUES
  ('HOLD_BUFFER_PERCENT',     '25'::jsonb,  'Percent buffer added to estimated job cost for escrow/hold'),
  ('APPROVAL_SLA_HOURS',      '6'::jsonb,   'Hours after completion before job is flagged awaiting approval'),
  ('MAX_IN_PROGRESS_HOURS',   '8'::jsonb,   'Hours in progress before job is flagged as stuck'),
  ('MIN_BEFORE_PHOTOS',       '3'::jsonb,   'Minimum before photos required'),
  ('MIN_AFTER_PHOTOS',        '3'::jsonb,   'Minimum after photos required'),
  ('DISPUTE_WINDOW_HOURS',    '24'::jsonb,  'Hours after completion/approval to allow disputes')
ON CONFLICT (key) DO NOTHING;


-- 4) Observability event store (single pane of glass)
CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS observability_events (
  event_id         UUID PRIMARY KEY,
  occurred_at      TIMESTAMPTZ NOT NULL DEFAULT now(),

  -- Where did this come from?
  source           TEXT NOT NULL CHECK (source IN ('lovable','base44','n8n','api','neon','stripe')),

  -- What happened?
  name             TEXT NOT NULL,         -- canonical name like "job.created", "credits.hold.created"
  severity         TEXT NOT NULL DEFAULT 'info'
                   CHECK (severity IN ('debug','info','warn','error')),

  -- Who/what caused it?
  actor_type       TEXT NOT NULL DEFAULT 'system'
                   CHECK (actor_type IN ('client','cleaner','admin','system')),
  actor_id         TEXT,

  -- Correlation
  trace_id         TEXT NOT NULL,         -- generated in Lovable at action start and propagated everywhere
  request_id       TEXT,                  -- per-request id (optional but recommended)
  span_id          TEXT,                  -- optional (future)
  idempotency_key  TEXT,                  -- optional
  job_id           TEXT,                  -- optional
  user_id          TEXT,                  -- optional

  -- Extra details
  payload          JSONB NOT NULL DEFAULT '{}'::jsonb
);

-- Fast lookups (Admin Observability Timeline)
CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_obs_events_occurred_at
  ON observability_events (occurred_at DESC);

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_obs_events_trace
  ON observability_events (trace_id, occurred_at DESC);

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_obs_events_job
  ON observability_events (job_id, occurred_at DESC);

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_obs_events_user
  ON observability_events (user_id, occurred_at DESC);

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_obs_events_source
  ON observability_events (source, occurred_at DESC);

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_obs_events_name
  ON observability_events (name, occurred_at DESC);

CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_obs_events_severity
  ON observability_events (severity, occurred_at DESC);

-- Optional: keep idempotency keys linked (soft FK; many systems use TEXT ids)
-- Uncomment if your IDs match and you want DB-level enforcement:
-- ALTER TABLE observability_events
--   ADD CONSTRAINT fk_obs_idempotency
--   FOREIGN KEY (idempotency_key) REFERENCES idempotency_keys(idempotency_key);


COMMIT;
What this gives you immediately
A central “track everything” table (observability_events) you can build the Admin “Observability Timeline” page on.

Replay-safe critical writes via idempotency_keys.

Immutable admin accountability via admin_audit_log.

No-redeploy ops tuning via system_config.

If you want, paste your existing jobs, job_events, and credit_ledger table definitions (or the migration file), and I’ll add optional DB triggers that automatically write observability entries on:

job status changes

new ledger entries

dispute updates


how do i pull up my existing tables u want me to paste in

Great question — this is straightforward. Here are 3 safe, simple ways to pull your existing tables so you can paste them to me.

OPTION A (BEST & FASTEST): Neon SQL Editor (Recommended)
This gives you exact table definitions (what I want).

Step 1: Open Neon
Go to Neon Console

Select your project

Click SQL Editor

Step 2: List all tables
Run this:

SELECT table_name
FROM information_schema.tables
WHERE table_schema = 'public'
ORDER BY table_name;
This shows every table you currently have.

Step 3: Get table definitions (THIS IS THE IMPORTANT PART)
For each table, run:

SELECT
  'CREATE TABLE ' || table_name || E' (\n' ||
  string_agg(
    '  ' || column_name || ' ' || data_type ||
    CASE
      WHEN character_maximum_length IS NOT NULL
      THEN '(' || character_maximum_length || ')'
      ELSE ''
    END ||
    CASE
      WHEN is_nullable = 'NO' THEN ' NOT NULL'
      ELSE ''
    END,
    E',\n'
  ) ||
  E'\n);' AS create_table_sql
FROM information_schema.columns
WHERE table_schema = 'public'
  AND table_name = 'YOUR_TABLE_NAME'
GROUP BY table_name;
🔁 Replace YOUR_TABLE_NAME with:

jobs

job_events

credit_ledger

disputes

users

cleaner_profiles

client_profiles

anything else you see

🔴 ROOT CAUSE (100% CONFIRMED)
PowerShell is breaking your connection string because it contains &:

In PowerShell, & is a command operator, EVEN INSIDE QUOTES in some parsing paths.

That’s why you keep getting:

pg_dump: error: too many command-line arguments
✅ THE FIX (POWERHELL-SPECIFIC, GUARANTEED)
PowerShell has a special escape called --%
It means: “stop parsing everything after this”

✅ COPY THIS EXACT LINE INTO POWERSHELL
DO NOT MODIFY IT. DO NOT ADD LINE BREAKS.

PowerShell runs silently for a bit

--% disables PowerShell parsing

& is passed correctly to pg_dump

pg_dump finally sees a valid connection string

Thought for 21s
I see what’s happening in your screenshot: PowerShell is still splitting the connection string at the &, so pg_dump thinks it’s getting extra “database names”, and it throws:

pg_dump: error: too many command-line arguments (first is "--format=custom")

✅ The most reliable fix is to escape the & in the URL inside the quotes using PowerShell’s escape character (backtick).

✅ COPY THIS EXACT LINE INTO POWERSHELL
& "C:\Program Files\PostgreSQL\14\bin\pg_dump.exe" "postgresql://neondb_owner:npg_KDNnTPAbdw14@ep-fragrant-bird-afmlkke1-pooler.c-2.us-west-2.aws.neon.tech/neondb?sslmode=require`&channel_binding=require" --format=custom --file=puretask_neon.dump

Why this one works
In PowerShell, & is a special operator.

The backtick ` forces PowerShell to treat it as a literal character inside the string, so pg_dump receives the URL correctly.

wat else do we need to add to lovable

In Lovable, think of it as your UI + client-side glue. Everything “real” (money, job state, ledger) stays in Backend/Base44/n8n/Neon. So what you add to Lovable is mainly: screens + API wiring + safety headers + tracking + UX states.

Here’s the exact checklist of what else you should add.

1) API client layer (non-negotiable)
Create one reusable api.ts (or lib/api.ts) that every screen uses.

Must include on every request:

credentials: "include" (cookie auth)

X-CSRF-Token header on writes (POST/PATCH/DELETE)

Idempotency-Key on critical writes (job create, transitions, credits checkout, admin actions)

X-Trace-Id + X-Request-Id (for your “track everything” system)

Lovable deliverable: a single apiFetch() wrapper + helpers:

postWithIdempotency()

transitionJob()

buyCredits()

2) Auth + route protection
Lovable should have:

Public routes: Home, How it works, Browse (optional), Pricing, Policies

Protected Client routes: dashboard, bookings, checkout, chat, job approval

Protected Cleaner routes: schedule, job workspace, payouts

Protected Admin routes: admin console (or separate app)

Lovable deliverable: RequireAuth wrapper + role gating:

client-only

cleaner-only

admin-only

3) Standard UI states for every screen
For each page/component, add:

Loading state (skeletons)

Empty state (no bookings, no messages, no favorites)

Error state (API error, retry)

Offline-ish state (network error)

Lovable deliverable: shared components:

<PageSkeleton />

<EmptyState />

<ErrorState onRetry />

Toast notifications

4) Job timeline + verification UI (core to PureTask)
This is the “trust engine” the user sees.

Add components that appear in multiple screens:

Job Status Timeline (requested → accepted → on_my_way → in_progress → awaiting_approval → completed)

GPS verified badges

Before/After photo viewer

Approve / Dispute panel

Lovable deliverable: reusable JobTimeline, VerificationBadges, PhotoProofGrid, ApproveDisputeCard.

5) Credits wallet UI (client-facing)
Since you’re credit-based, Lovable needs:

Wallet balance display

“Held for jobs” display

Purchase credits flow (Stripe checkout link)

Ledger/history view (read-only)

Lovable deliverable: WalletSummary + LedgerList + “Buy Credits” screen wired to /credits/checkout.

6) Messaging UI that is job-scoped
Keep it simple for V1:

Threads = by job

One thread per job

Push notifications later; for now in-app + email/sms via n8n

Lovable deliverable: Inbox + ChatThread(jobId) wired to /messages/job/:jobId.

7) Observability hooks (track everything)
Since you want “track anything/everything” across Lovable/Base44/n8n/Neon, Lovable must emit:

ui.screen_viewed

ui.action_clicked

ui.api_request.started/completed/failed

Lovable deliverable:

tracking.ts that generates trace_id at the start of each user action/session

sends logs to POST /events/ui (Option A we chose)

8) Environment variables (Lovable config)
Add:

VITE_API_BASE_URL (or NEXT_PUBLIC_API_URL)

VITE_APP_ENV

VITE_SENTRY_DSN (optional but huge help)

VITE_RELEASE_VERSION

9) Admin UI in Lovable (optional but recommended)
You can build the Admin pages in Lovable too, but keep them behind role gates:

Jobs Console

Job Detail

Disputes

Ledger

Stripe Events

Observability Timeline (reads from observability_events)

The “minimum Lovable V1 add” list
If you do only these, you’re in a great place:

API wrapper with CSRF + idempotency + trace headers

Role-based route protection

Job timeline + approval/dispute UI

Wallet + Buy Credits flow

Tracking events to /events/ui

If you tell me what Lovable stack it generated (React/Vite vs Next.js) and where you’re storing CSRF token (cookie name), I’ll write the exact apiFetch() + tracking.ts files you can paste in immediately.
